Modifications to Stolen Property: Hanafi Rulings on Hadd
List of rulings on modifications to stolen goods before exiting the place of theft

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hand-cutting (hadd) for each type of modification a thief makes to stolen goods before removing them from the place of theft, and explain the underlying principle of value and identity.

Core Idea
Hand-cutting applies unless the modification reduces value below nisab or fundamentally alters the item's identity.

When a thief modifies stolen property before carrying it out of the place of theft, the application of the hand-cutting penalty (hadd) depends on whether the change is reversible and whether the item's value or identity is affected. This passage from al-Hidayah presents several concrete examples that illustrate the Hanafi position on common scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the starting conditions
Before analyzing the modification, establish that all ordinary conditions for hadd are met: the stolen item was taken from a secure place (hizr), its value was at least ten dirhams, and the thief had no ownership claim.
2
Classify the modification type
Determine whether the modification affects the item's physical essence (e.g., tearing, slaughtering, melting) or its appearance (e.g., dyeing). This determines if the item can be returned intact or if compensation is due.
Tearing a cloth does not change its identity; slaughtering a goat also does not change the fact it is property. Melting gold/silver changes form but not substance.
3
Assess effect on value
Check whether after the modification, the value of the item is still at or above the nisab of ten dirhams. If the modification reduces the value below nisab, no hadd applies.
In the examples given, the value remains sufficient (they were originally worth ten dirhams).
4
Determine ownership and liability
If the change is irreversible and increases value (like dyeing red), the thief becomes owner of the modified item by paying its value; thus no return of the cloth, but hadd applies. If the change is reversible (like dyeing black), the thief must return the original item, and the question of hadd depends on whether the item was fully removed with intent to steal.
The text states that for red dyeing, hand-cutting applies and cloth not returned; for black dyeing, cloth is returned (three imams).
5
State the final hukm for each case
Apply the rule: the hadd is wajib unless the item is returned before removal or the modification negates the nisab. In the given cases, hand-cutting applies for tearing, slaughtering, melting, and dyeing red; for dyeing black, the cloth is returned, implying no permanent deprivation, but the hadd ruling is not explicitly given – assume it still applies if the theft is complete.
The text leaves the ruling for black dyeing ambiguous regarding hadd; we follow the principle that hadd is not dropped by return after the fact.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب ما يحدث الشارق في السرقة
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ششم
چور نے کپڑا چوری کیا اور گھر ہی میں اسکے دو ٹکڑے کر کے باہر لے آیا اس کی قیمت دس درہم ہو تو ہاتھ کا ٹا جائے گا یا نہیں کسی نے بکری چرا کر اسے ذبح کر دیا اس کے بعد اسے باہر لایا تو اس کا حکم چور نے سونا یا چاندی چوری کیا اس کے در اھم ای دنا نیر بنالئے قطع ید ہوگا اور در اہم ودنا نیر کار بھی لازم ہوگا کپڑا چوری کیا اور اسے سرخ رنگ کر لیا قطع ید ہو گا اور کپڑا واپس نہیں لیا جائے گا اور نہ ہی کپڑے کا ضمان ہوگا کپڑے کو سیاہ رنگ کر دیا تو ائمہ ثلاثہ کے نزدیک کپڑا واپس لیا جائے گا
Chapter on what the thief does in theft. Ashraf al-Hidaya Urdu commentary volume 6. A thief stole cloth and tore it into two pieces inside the house and brought it out; its value is ten dirhams, will the hand be cut or not? Someone stole a goat and slaughtered it, then brought it out; what is its ruling? A thief stole gold or silver and made them into dirhams and dinars; hand-cutting will occur and the dirhams and dinars will also be obligatory. He stole cloth and dyed it red; hand-cutting will occur and the cloth will not be returned, nor will there be liability for the cloth. If he dyed it black, then according to the three imams the cloth will be returned.
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage lists several cases from the chapter on what changes a thief makes to stolen property before removing it from the place of theft. The key principle is that the hand-cutting penalty (hadd) for theft applies only if the value of the stolen item at the time of removal from the place of theft reaches the nisab (ten dirhams). Modifications made before removal are examined: if the modification increases value or changes the item's identity, the original item is considered consumed and liability may shift. The text gives examples: tearing cloth inside the house does not prevent hadd if value remains; slaughtering a goat before removal similarly; melting gold/silver into coins does not prevent hadd but also requires compensation; dyeing cloth red is considered a change that makes the cloth not returnable (the thief owns it by payment), whereas dyeing black is a reversible change according to the three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad), so the cloth is returned.

Key Terms
قطع يد (qat' al-yad): The prescribed punishment (hadd) for theft: amputation of the right hand.
ضمان (damān): Liability, compensation for value of destroyed or consumed property.
ائمہ ثلاثہ (a'immah thalāthah): The three imams: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A thief steals a goat worth 10 dirhams and slaughters it inside the property before carrying the meat out. According to the passage, what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) No hand-cutting because the goat is now meat
B) Hand-cutting applies because slaughtering does not change the value or identity
C) Hand-cutting applies only if the meat is worth at least 10 dirhams
D) No hand-cutting because the thief rendered the goat unusable

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school imposes hand-cutting for theft when the stolen property is removed from its secure place with intent and the value at that moment meets the nisab, regardless of modifications that do not fundamentally alter the item's identity or drop its value below the threshold.

Rulings on Highway Robbery (Qat' al-Tariq)
Summary of penalties for highway robbers based on their actions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings for highway robbery (qat' al-tariq) and distinguish between the penalties based on the robbers' actions.

Core Idea
Highway robbery triggers distinct hadd penalties — death, crucifixion, or amputation — depending on whether murder or theft occurs.

Highway robbery (qat' al-tariq) is a severe crime in Hanafi law, treated separately from ordinary theft. The penalties are graduated based on the robbers' actions: killing, taking property, or both. This lesson outlines the conditions for applying these hadd penalties and the exceptions that may drop them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the crime of qat' al-tariq
Determine that the crime is armed robbery occurring outside settled areas, committed by a group against a Muslim or dhimmi, with intent to take property or commit murder.
The location and group element distinguish it from ordinary theft.
2
Classify the robbers' actions
Identify whether the robbers killed, took property, wounded, or any combination. This determines the specific hadd penalty.
Killing and taking property leads to crucifixion; killing only leads to execution; taking property and wounding leads to amputation.
3
Apply the corresponding penalty
Match the action to the prescribed hadd: crucifixion alive then execution (kill+take), execution (kill only), amputation of hand and foot from opposite sides (wound+take), qisas (wound only).
If they kill but take no property, they are executed without crucifixion.
4
Note exceptions and special conditions
Exceptions like repentance after capture, presence of a minor or insane person, or robbery within a city drop the hadd for highway robbery. In those cases, alternative rulings apply (qisas, diyah, or no penalty).
Repentance before capture does not drop hadd for highway robbery; after capture, it may affect only murder liability.
5
Determine effect on hadd and alternative rulings
If an exception applies, the hadd of highway robbery falls. For murder, the guardians may seek qisas or diyah. For property, compensation may be due.
The hadd is a right of Allah; its dropping does not nullify private claims.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب قطع الطريق
ڈاکہ ڈالنے والی جماعت نے مسلمان یا ذمی کا حال لوٹا لیا اس جماعت کو امام وقت کیا سزا دے گا
ڈا کہ کب متحقق ہو گا یعنی ڈاکہ کی شرائط
ڈاکوؤں نے قتل بھی کیا اور مال بھی چھینا امام کیا سزا دے گا
ڈاکووں کو زندہ سولی پر لٹکایا جائے گا اور نا کے پیٹ نیزے سے چاک کرنے گا یہاں تک کہ انہیں موت کے گھاٹ اتار دے
سولی پر کتنے دن لڑکا یا جائے
ڈا کو کو قتل کر دیا گیا تو سرقہ صغریٰ کا تاوان اس پر نہیں لا دا جائے گا
اگر قتل کا فعل کسی ایک نے انجام دیا تو سب پر حد جاری کی جائے گی لاٹھی ، پتھر اور تلوار سے قتل برابر ہے
ڈاکو نے قتل بھی نہیں کیا اور مال بھی نہیں لو ٹا فقط زخمی کیا تو اس سے قصاص لیا جائے گا
ڈاکو نے مال لوٹا اور زخمی کیا تو ہاتھ اور پاؤں خلاف جانب سے کاٹا جائے اور جو زخم لگائے وہ ساقط ہو جائیں گے ڈا کو تو بہ کرنے کے بعد پکڑا گیا اور اس نے عمد اقتل کیا تھا تو اولیاء مقوتول چاہے قصاص لیں چاہے معاف کر دیں ڈاکوؤں کی جماعت میں کوئی نا بالغ، مجنون مقطوع لعی ہکا قریبی رشتہ دار ہو تو باقی ڈاکوؤں سے حد ساقط ہو جائے گی حد ساقط ہو گئی تو قصاص لینے کا حکم اولیاء مقتول کو ہو گا اگر بعض قافلہ والوں بعض دوسرے قافلہ والوں پر ڈاکہ ڈالا تو ڈاکہ کی حد جاری نہیں ہوگی ڈاکوؤں نے شہر میں یا شہر کے قریب دن یا رات کو ڈاکہ ڈالا تو ڈاکہ کی حد جاری نہیں ہوگی کسی نے دوسرے کا گلا دبا کر مار ڈالا تو دیت قاتل کی عاقلہ پر ہوگی
اگر شہر میں کسی کو گلا دبا کر موت کی گھاٹ اتار چکا ہے تو قتل کیا جائے گا
Chapter on cutting the road (highway robbery). What punishment will the ruling Imam give to a group that robbed a Muslim or dhimmi? When does highway robbery become established, i.e., its conditions. If the robbers both killed and seized property, what punishment will the Imam give? The robbers will be hung alive on a cross and their stomachs will be pierced with spears until they are put to death. How many days will they be hung? If the robber was killed, then the compensation for minor theft will not be imposed on him. If one person committed the killing, the hadd will be applied to all; killing with a stick, stone, or sword is equal. If the robber neither killed nor took property but only wounded, then qisas will be taken from him. If the robber took property and wounded, then his hand and foot will be cut from opposite sides, and the wounds he inflicted will be dropped. If he was caught after repenting and committed intentional murder, then the guardians of the slain may either take qisas or forgive. If among the group of robbers there is a minor, insane person, one with a severed hand, or a close relative, then the hadd falls from the rest; if the hadd falls, then the guardians of the slain have the right to qisas. If some members of a caravan rob another caravan, the hadd for highway robbery is not applied. If robbers commit robbery in a city or near a city by day or night, the hadd for highway robbery is not applied. If someone strangles another to death, the blood money is on the killer's 'aqila. If someone in a city strangles another to death, he will be killed.
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage is a summary of rulings from the chapter on highway robbery (qat' al-tariq). It defines the crime as robbery occurring outside settled areas, with conditions that the perpetrators are a group that forcibly takes property or commits murder. The penalties are graduated: if they kill and take property, they are crucified alive and then executed; if they only take property, hands and feet are cut from opposite sides; if they only wound, qisas (retaliation) applies; if they kill but do not take property, they are executed. Exceptions are noted: repentance after capture affects liability; presence of a minor, insane person, or close relative among the group drops the hadd for all; robbery within a city or between caravans does not constitute qat' al-tariq, and hadd is not applied; instead, other penalties apply. Strangling is treated as a form of murder requiring qisas or diyah.

Key Terms
قطع الطريق (qat' al-tariq): Highway robbery: armed robbery outside settled areas with the intent to take property or commit murder.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following scenarios would NOT trigger the hadd of highway robbery?
A) A group robs a traveler on a desert road, kills him, and takes his money.
B) A group robs a merchant inside the city market, kills him, and takes his money.
C) A group robs a dhimmi on a remote road, takes his property but does not kill.
D) A group robs a Muslim on a remote road, wounds him but takes no property.

Key Takeaway
Highway robbery (qat' al-tariq) carries graduated hadd penalties—crucifixion, execution, or amputation—based on the robbers' actions, with exceptions for location, repentance, and presence of certain individuals that drop the hadd.

Hadd: Fixed Punishment as Allah's Right
Defining 'hadd' linguistically and legally, and explaining its purpose

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi legal definition of hadd, distinguish it from qisas and tazir, and explain the primary purpose of hadd according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Hadd is a fixed punishment as Allah's right, solely for deterrence — not purification.

In this lesson, we unpack the precise Hanafi definition of 'hadd' (fixed punishment). The text clarifies that hadd is a predetermined penalty that belongs to Allah's rights, distinguishing it from qisas (retaliation) which is a human right that can be waived. We also learn that the primary goal of hadd is to deter harmful behavior, not to purify the sinner. This distinction is crucial for understanding the Hanafi approach to criminal justice.

Guided Path
1
Parse the linguistic meaning
Identify the root meaning of 'hadd' (منع, prevention) and its connection to the term 'haddad' (doorkeeper). This linguistic foundation sets the stage for the legal definition.
The term 'hadd' carries the core idea of prevention, which is central to its legal function.
2
Extract the legal definition
Locate the Shari'ah definition: 'a fixed punishment as a right of Allah.' Note that the definition includes two key elements: fixedness (muqaddara) and being a right of Allah (haqqan lillah).
This definition automatically excludes punishments that are not fixed or that are rights of humans.
3
Distinguish from qisas and tazir
The text explicitly states that qisas is not called hadd because it is a right of the servant (haqq al-'abd), and tazir is not called hadd because it lacks predetermined measure. Understand why each is excluded.
Qisas can be waived by the victim's heirs; tazir is discretionary. Hadd is neither.
4
Identify the primary purpose
The passage says the primary purpose (maqsad asli) is to deter people from what harms them (inzijar). Purification (tahara) is not primary, as evidenced by hadd being legislated for disbelievers.
This is a distinctive Hanafi position; other schools may give purification a role.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ الْحَدُّ لُغَةً هُوَ الْمَنْعُ وَمِنْهُ الْحَدَّادُ لِلْبَوَّابِ وَفِى الشَّرِيعَةِ هُوَ الْعُقُوبَةُ الْمُقَدَّرَةُ حَقًّا لِلَّهِ تَعَالَى حَتَّى لَا يُسَمَّى الْقِصَاصُ حَدَّ الأَنَّهُ حَقُّ الْعَبْدِ وَلَا التَّعْزِيرُ لِعَدْمِ التَّقْدِيرِ وَالْمَقْصَدُ الأصْلِيُّ مِنْ شَرْعِهِ الْإِنْزِ جَارُ عَمَّا يَتَضَرَّرُبِهِ الْعِبَادُ وَالطَّهَارَةُ لَيْسَتْ اَصْلِيَّةٌ فِيْهِ بِدَلِيْلِ شَرْعِهِ فِي حَقِّ الْكَافِرِ
He (the author) said: Hadd linguistically means prevention; from it is 'haddad' for doorkeeper. In Shari'ah, it is a fixed punishment as a right of Allah Almighty, such that qisas is not called hadd because it is a right of the servant, nor tazir because it lacks determination. The primary purpose of its legislation is to deter people from what harms them, and purification is not primary in it, as evidenced by its legislation for the disbeliever.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage defines the term 'hadd' (fixed punishment) from the Hanafi perspective. Linguistically, 'hadd' means prevention; thus a doorkeeper is called 'haddad' because he prevents entry. Legally, a hadd is a predetermined punishment that is a right of Allah, meaning it cannot be pardoned or reduced by human authority. This distinguishes it from qisas (retaliation) which is a right of the victim (or their heirs) and can be waived, and from tazir (discretionary punishment) which is not fixed in measure. The primary purpose of hadd is deterrence and prevention of harm to society, not purification of the sinner. This is proven by the fact that even a disbeliever receives hadd, whereas purification through repentance is only for believers. The text emphasizes that hadd does not automatically cleanse the sinner; rather, repentance (tawba) is the means of purification before Allah. This is supported by scholarly consensus that hadd does not fall due to repentance.

Key Terms
حد (ḥadd): A fixed punishment prescribed as a right of Allah for certain crimes (e.g., zina, theft, drinking).
قصاص (qiṣāṣ): Retaliation; a right of the victim's heirs for murder or bodily harm.
تعزیر (taʿzīr): Discretionary punishment left to the judge's discretion for crimes without fixed hadd.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary purpose of hadd punishments according to the Hanafi school?
A) To purify the sinner from sin.
B) To deter people from harmful actions.
C) To extract revenge for the victim.
D) To provide financial compensation.

Key Takeaway
Hadd is a fixed punishment as Allah's right, primarily for deterrence, and it must not be confused with qisas (human right) or tazir (discretionary).

Proof of Zina: Testimony and Confession
Stating the two methods of proving zina and the rationale for relying on apparent proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two methods of proving zina in Hanafi fiqh and explain why apparent proof (zahir) suffices for the hadd penalty.

Core Idea
Zina is proven only by four witnesses or a voluntary confession — certain knowledge is impossible, so the law rests on apparent proof.

In Islamic criminal law, the crime of zina carries a severe fixed punishment (hadd), yet it is also the most private of acts. This passage from al-Quduri’s Mukhtasar lays down the fundamental principle: zina is established before the judge only through clear testimony (bayyinah) or a voluntary confession (iqrar). The reasoning is deeply practical — since direct certain knowledge of the act is almost impossible, the law accepts apparent (zahir) proofs that are likely to be truthful.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two proofs
The text states that zina is established by bayyinah (testimony of witnesses) and iqrar (confession). Note that these are the only two methods accepted in the Hanafi school; circumstantial evidence such as pregnancy is not sufficient.
Bayyinah here specifically means four male Muslim witnesses who saw the actual act.
2
Recognize the role of the Imam
The proof must be presented before the Imam (ruler or judge). The hadd cannot be implemented by individuals or vigilante groups; it requires a properly constituted authority.
In the absence of a legitimate Imam, the hadd is not carried out.
3
Understand the rationale for apparent proof
The author argues that both testimony and confession are 'zahir' (apparent) proofs. For confession, truthfulness is assumed because no sane person would voluntarily admit to such a harmful and disgraceful act unless it were true. Testimony, when meeting strict conditions (four witnesses), also provides strong apparent evidence.
This reasoning is an example of istihsan (juristic preference) based on the practical difficulty of proving such acts.
4
Grasp the epistemological principle
The text concludes: 'Arriving at certain knowledge is unattainable, so one is satisfied with the apparent.' This is a key principle in Hanafi usul: in matters where absolute certainty is impossible, the law operates on predominant probability supported by apparent proofs.
This principle also applies to the acceptance of ahad hadith and other areas where certainty is not required.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ الزِنَاءُ يُثْبَتُ بِالْبَيِّنَةِ وَالْإِقْرَارِ وَالْمُرَادُ ثُبُوتَهُ عِنْدَ الْإِمَامِ لِاَنَّ الْبَيْنَةَ دَلِيلٌ ظَاهِرٌ وَكَذَا الْإِقْرَارُ لِاَنَّ الصَّدْقَ فِيهِ مُرَجِّحٌ لَا سِيَّمَا فِيمَا يَتَعَلَّقُ بِقُبُوتِهِ مَضَرَّةً وَمَعَرَّةٌ وَالْوَصُولُ إِلَى الْعِلْمِ الْقَطْعِيِّ مُتَعَدَّرٌ فَيُكْتَفَى بِالظَّاهِرِ
He (Quduri) said: Zina is established by evidence (bayyinah) and by confession (iqrar). And what is meant is its establishment before the Imam, because evidence is an apparent proof, and similarly confession, because truthfulness is predominant in it, especially in what involves harm and disgrace. And arriving at certain knowledge is unattainable, so one is satisfied with the apparent.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage from Quduri, a key Hanafi matn, establishes the two ways to prove the crime of zina: (1) bayyinah (testimony of four witnesses) and (2) iqrar (confession by the accused). The proof is to be presented before the Imam (ruler or judge). The reasoning is that both evidence and confession are apparent (zahir) proofs; truthfulness is assumed in confession due to the harm and disgrace it brings, so it is often reliable. Since certain knowledge (qat'i 'ilm) of the act is nearly impossible to obtain (as it is private), Islamic law relies on these apparent proofs to establish the hadd. This underscores the strict requirements: for testimony, four male witnesses are needed (as per Quranic stipulation); for confession, it must be clear and voluntary, and the accused can retract. The ruling only applies when the case is brought before the proper authority; ifno Imam, the hadd cannot be implemented by individuals.

Key Terms
زنا (zinā): Unlawful sexual intercourse between a man and a woman not married to each other.
بينة (bayyinah): Legal evidence, specifically testimony of witnesses (shuhud).
اقرار (iqrār): Confession by the accused of committing zina.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school rely on apparent proofs (zahir) for proving zina rather than requiring absolute certainty?
A) Because absolute certainty is impossible in such private matters.
B) Because the Quran commands it specifically.
C) Because the Prophet only accepted apparent proofs.
D) Because it makes prosecution easier.

Key Takeaway
Zina is proven only by four male witnesses or a voluntary confession; Islamic law relies on apparent proof because absolute certainty is unattainable.

Definition and Purpose of Hadd (Prescribed Punishment)
Defines hadd linguistically and legally, and discusses its primary purpose

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of hadd, distinguish it from qisas and tazir, and explain its primary purpose.

Core Idea
Hadd is a fixed punishment as Allah's right; its aim is deterrence, not purification.

You likely know that Islamic punishments like amputation for theft and stoning for adultery are fixed by revelation. But what exactly is a hadd, and how is it different from other punishments? This passage from our text establishes the precise Hanafi definition, excluding qisas and tazir, and clarifies that the primary goal of hadd is to deter crime, not to purify the sinner. Understanding this distinction is key to the entire jurisprudence of criminal law.

Guided Path
1
Understand the linguistic root
The Arabic word 'hadd' literally means prevention. A gatekeeper is called 'haddad' because he prevents entry. This linguistic sense sets the tone for the legal meaning.
2
Identify the legal definition
In sacred law, hadd is defined as a fixed punishment (muqaddara) that is an exclusive right of Allah (haqq Allah). It is not subject to modification by human parties.
3
Exclude other punishments
Two punishments are explicitly excluded: qisas (retaliation) is not hadd because it is a right of the servant (haqq al-ʿabd) and can be waived; tazir (discretionary punishment) is not hadd because its measure is not fixed by revelation.
4
Determine the primary purpose
The primary purpose of legislation of hadd is deterrence (inzijar) from harmful acts, not purification (tahara). Purification from sin is achieved through sincere repentance (tawba), not the punishment itself. Evidence: hadd is applied to disbelievers who are not purified.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ الْحَدُّ لُغَةً هُوَ الْمَنْعُ وَمِنْهُ الْحَدَّادُ لِلْبَوَّابِ وَفى الشَّرِيعَةِ هُوَ الْعُقُوبَةُ الْمُقَدَّرَةُ حَقًّا لِلَّهِ تَعَالَى حَتَّى لَا يُسَمَّى الْقِصَاصُ حَدًّا لِأَنَّهُ حَقُّ الْعَبْدِ وَلَا التَّعْزِيرُ لِعَدَمِ التَّقْدِيرِ وَالْمَقْصَدُ الْأَصْلِيُّ مِنْ شَرْعِهِ الْإِنْزِجَارُ عَمَّا يَتَضَرَّرُ بِهِ الْعِبَادُ وَالطَّهَارَةُ لَيْسَتْ أَصْلِيَّةً فِيهِ بِدَلِيلِ شَرْعِهِ فِي حَقِّ الْكَافِرِ

ترجمہ مصنف نے فرمایا ہے کہ لغت میں حد منع کرنے کے معنی میں ہے۔ اسی بناء پر دربان کو حداد کہا جاتا ہے ( کیونکہ وہ لوگوں کو اس کے اندر داخل ہونے سے منع کرتا ہے۔ ) اور شریعت میں حد ایسی سزا کو کہتے ہیں جو محض حق الہی کے لئے مقدر کر دی گئی ہے ۔ یہاں تک کہ قصاص کو بھی حد نہیں کہا جاتا ہے کیونکہ یہ قصاص بندوں کا حق ہوتا ہے (اسی لئے ولی کو حق قصاص معاف کر کے دینے لینے کا اختیار حاصل ہے) اور تعزیر کوبھی حد نہیں کہا جاتا ہے کیونکہ وہ مقدر نہیں ہے۔ یعنی اس کی کوئی مقدار معین نہیں ہوتی ہے کہ اس میں کمی و بیشی نہ ہو سکے۔ حد مشروع کرنے کا مقصد اصلی یہ ہے کہ جس بات سے بندون کو تکلیف ہوتی ہو اس کے کرنے والے کو تنبیہ اور سزادی جائے یہ گناہ سے پاک ہونا حد کا مقصد اصل نہیں ہے۔ جس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حد و کافروں کے بارے میں بھی ثابت ہے حالانکہ کا فر تو بھی منانا سے پاک نہیں ہوگا۔

تشریح فائدہ جس شخص نے جرم کیا ہے جب اس کو حد ماری گئی تو ہمارے نزدیک وہ حد اس شخص کو اس کے گناہ سے پاک کرنے والی نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ بلکہ پاک ہونا تو تو بہ سے ہوتا ہے۔ علماء کا اجماع ہے کہ تو بہ کرنے سے دنیاوی حد ساقط نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ اگر یہ کہا جائے کہ پاک ہونا تو حدیث سے ثابت ہوتا ہے۔ تو جواب یہ ہے کہ جن لوگوں پر حد جاری کی گئی خود انہوں نے تو بہ کر لی تھی ۔ چنانچہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کا فرمان "لقد تاب توبہ (اس نے بڑی تو بہ کی ) اس باب میں ضریح ہے۔ الحاصل یہی مذہب قوی ہے۔ واللہ تعالی اعلم۔

فائده .... (پھر گواہی اور اقرار دونوں میں سے ہر ایک کا تفصیلی حال مصنف نے اس کے بعد بیان فرمایا ہے)۔
Hadd linguistically is prevention, from which is derived 'haddad' for the gatekeeper. In sacred law it is a fixed punishment as a right of Allah, so that qisas is not called hadd because it is a right of the servant, nor tazir because it is not fixed. The primary purpose of its legislation is deterrence from what harms the servants, and purification is not primary, evidenced by its legislation regarding the disbeliever. (Remainder of the passage is Urdu translation and commentary.)
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling statement on the concept of hadd. The author first gives the linguistic meaning: hadd means prevention, hence a gatekeeper (who prevents people) is called haddad. Then he gives the legal definition: a fixed punishment that is the right of Allah. This excludes qisas (retaliation) because it is the right of the individual (the victim's heir has the option to forgive, take diya, or execute), and it excludes tazir (discretionary punishment) because it is not fixed in measure. The primary aim of hadd is deterrence (inzijar) from harmful acts, not purification (tahara). Purification from sin is achieved through sincere repentance (tawba), not through the punishment itself. Evidence that purification is not the main aim is that hadd is applied to disbelievers too, who are not purified by it (since they do not repent with faith). The commentary then resolves a potential doubt: some hadiths indicate that hadd purifies, but the answer is that those hadiths refer to people who repented before the punishment. The consensus of scholars is that tawba does not remove the worldly hadd.

Key Terms
حد (hadd): A fixed punishment prescribed by Allah as a right of Allah, intended for deterrence.
قصاص (qisas): Retaliation in kind for murder or injury, considered a right of the servant.
تعزير (tazir): Discretionary punishment for offenses that do not have a fixed hadd or qisas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary purpose (maqsad asli) of prescribing hadd according to the text?
A) Purification of the sinner
B) Deterrence from harmful acts
C) Compensation for the victim
D) Testing the faith

Key Takeaway
Hadd is a fixed, immutable punishment as a right of Allah; its primary aim is to deter harm, not to purify, and it must be distinguished from qisas and tazir.

Proof of Zina: Testimony and Confession
States the two proofs for zina and the justification for relying on apparent evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two means of proving zina according to the Hanafi school and explain why the law suffices with apparent evidence.

Core Idea
Zina is proven by testimony or confession; the law accepts apparent evidence because certainty is unattainable.

This passage from Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar states the foundational rule for proving the crime of zina. It identifies two valid proofs: testimony (bayyinah) and confession (iqrar), both presented before the imam. The author then provides a rationale rooted in legal epistemology — since absolute certainty is impossible, the Shariah relies on manifest indicators.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two proofs
Read the first sentence and note the two Arabic terms: bayyinah (testimony) and iqrar (confession). Understand that these are the sole means of proving zina in the Hanafi school.
Bayyinah in this context specifically refers to four male witnesses.
2
Note the condition of proof before the imam
The text clarifies that the proof must be 'before the imam' — meaning the ruler or his deputy. This ensures formal judicial proceedings.
Confession outside court is valid in Hanafi law but becomes operative only when made in the presence of the imam.
3
Analyse the justification for apparent evidence
The author explains that testimony and confession are both 'apparent proofs' (dalil dhahir). For confession, truth is considered preponderant (marjih), especially in matters involving harm and shame, as one would not falsely admit to such acts.
The Urdu translation emphasizes that the proof must be 'such proof that exists before the imam of the time.'
4
Understand the epistemological principle
The text concludes that since reaching certain knowledge (ilm qat'i) is extremely difficult in such cases, the law suffices with the apparent (dhahir). This is a key Hanafi usul principle in hudud matters.
This principle allows for punishment based on strong probability rather than absolute certainty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ الزِنَاءُ يُثْبَتُ بِالْبَيِّنَةِ وَالْإِقْرَارِ وَالْمُرَادُ ثُبُوتُهُ عِنْدَ الْإِمَامِ لِأَنَّ الْبَيِّنَةَ دَلِيلٌ ظَاهِرٌ وَكَذَا الْإِقْرَارُ لِأَنَّ الصِّدْقَ فِيهِ مُرَجَّحٌ لَا سِيَّمَا فِيمَا يَتَعَلَّقُ بِثُبُوتِهِ مَضَرَّةً وَمَعَرَّةٌ وَالْوُصُولُ إِلَى الْعِلْمِ الْقَطْعِيِّ مُتَعَذَّرٌ فَيُكْتَفَى بِالظَّاهِرِ

ترجمہ قدوری نے کہا ہے کہ زنا کا ثبوت گواہوں کے ساتھ ہوتا ہے اور اقرار کے ساتھ ہوتا ہے اور ثبوت سے مراد ایسا ثبوت ہے جو امام وقت کے سامنے ہوں۔ کیونکہ گواہی ایک ظاہری دلیل ہے۔ اقرار کا بھی یہی حکم ہے۔ کیونکہ اقرار میں بھی سچائی غالب ہوتی ہے۔ بالخصوص جس چیز کے ثابت ہونے میں نقصان اور شرمندگی ہو۔ مسئلہ کے حقیقی علم تک پہنچنا محال ہوتا ہے۔ اسی لئے صرف ظاہر پر بھی اکتفاء کر لیا جاتا ہے۔
Zina is proven by testimony and confession. What is meant is its proof before the imam, because testimony is an apparent proof, and similarly confession because truth is preponderant in it, especially in matters whose proof entails harm and shame, and reaching certain knowledge is difficult, so one suffices with the apparent.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This is a ruling statement on the methods of proving zina. The author (Al-Quduri) states that zina is established through two means: bayyinah (testimony of witnesses) and iqrar (confession). The proof must be presented before the imam (ruler or his deputy). The text gives a rational justification: both testimony and confession are manifest indicators (dalil dhahir) of the act. Confession is given weight because truthfulness is presumed (sadq marjih), especially when the matter entails harm and disgrace (that is, one would not falsely admit to something so shameful). Since absolute certainty (ilm qat'i) is unattainable, the law suffices with the apparent (dhahir). The Urdu translation clarifies that 'bayyinah' here refers to witnesses (gawahi), and that the proof must be before the imam of the time.

Key Terms
بينة (bayyinah): Testimony of four male witnesses for the crime of zina.
إقرار (iqrar): A voluntary confession of guilt by the accused, considered valid proof for establishing zina.
ظاهر (dhahir): The apparent or manifest evidence, as opposed to inner certainty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) To make the process easier for the judge
B) Because reaching certain knowledge is difficult
C) Because testimony is always truthful
D) Because speculation is sufficient in hudud

Key Takeaway
Zina is proven by testimony (bayyinah) and confession (iqrar) before the imam, and the law suffices with apparent evidence because certainty is unattainable.

Requirement of Four Witnesses for Zina
Definition of bayyinah for zina with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the number of witnesses required for zina, cite the Quranic and Hadith proofs, and explain the wisdom of satr.

Core Idea
Four witnesses are required for zina — the Quran and Sunnah make this a strict condition to protect honor and prevent false accusations.

The Hanafi school holds that the testimony (bayyinah) for zina must come from four male witnesses. This lesson examines the ruling and its proofs from the Quran, Sunnah, and legal wisdom (satr). Understanding this requirement is crucial for distinguishing hudud cases from other areas of testimony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Locate the exact statement of the ruling: 'al-bayyinah an tashhada arba'atun min al-shuhood' — the evidence is that four witnesses testify.
This is the definition of bayyinah in the context of zina.
2
Examine the Quranic proofs
Two verses are cited: Quran 4:15 (call four witnesses) and Quran 24:4 (if they do not bring four witnesses). Identify the imperative and the conditional phrasing.
The number 'four' is explicitly mentioned in both verses.
3
Analyze the Hadith proof
The Prophet (pbuh) told an accusing husband to bring four witnesses. This adds a clear precedent from the Sunnah.
This hadith reinforces the Quranic requirement.
4
Understand the wisdom (hikmah)
The requirement of four witnesses achieves satr (concealment) — it is difficult to fabricate testimony with four people, so many guilty individuals escape punishment, which is preferred over punishing the innocent.
Satr is an encouraged practice; spreading lewdness (isha'ah) is its opposite.
5
Note the practical consequence
If less than four witnesses testify, the testimony is dismissed and the false accuser may face hadd al-qadhf (punishment for false accusation).
This underscores the heavy burden of proof in zina cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ فَالْبَيِّنَةُ أَنْ تَشْهَدَ أَرْبَعَةٌ مِنَ الشُّهُودِ عَلَى رَجُلٍ وَامْرَأَةٍ بِالزِّنَاءِ لِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى فَاسْتَشْهِدُوا عَلَيْهِنَّ أَرْبَعَةً مِنْكُمْ وَقَالَ اللهُ تَعَالَى ثُمَّ لَمْ يَأْتُوا بِأَرْبَعَةِ شُهَدَاءَ وَقَالَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لِلَّذِي قَذَفَ امْرَأَتَهُ ائْتِ بِأَرْبَعَةٍ يَشْهَدُونَ عَلَى صِدْقِ مَقَالَتِكَ وَلِأَنَّ فِي اشْتِرَاطِ الْأَرْبَعَةِ يَتَحَقَّقُ مَعْنَى السَّتْرِ وَهُوَ مَنْدُوبٌ إِلَيْهِ وَالْإِشَاعَةُ ضِدُّهُ

ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا ہے کہ گواہی کی صورت یہ ہوگی کہ گواہوں میں سے چار شخص ایک مرد اور ایک عورت پر زنا کی گواہی دیں۔ اس فرمان باری تعالیٰ کی وجہ سے فَاسْتَشْهِدُوا عَلَيْهِنَّ أَرْبَعَةً مِنْكُمْ یعنی ایسی عورتوں پر اپنوں میں چار شخص گواہ تلاش کرو۔ اور اللہ تعالیٰ نے یہ بھی فرمایا ہے ثُمَّ لَم يَأْتُوا بِأَرْبَعَةِ شُهَدَاءَ پھر وہ لوگ چار گواہ نہ لائیں اور رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے اس مرد کو جس نے اپنی بیوی پر زنا کی تہمت لگائی تھی یوں فرمایا تھا کہ تم ایسے چار مر ولاؤ جو تمہاری بات کے سچے ہونے پر گواہی دیں۔ اور یہ بھی دلیل ہے کہ چار مردوں کی شرط لگانے میں پردہ پوشی کے معنی پائے جاتے ہیں۔ اور پردہ پوشی کرنا ایک ایسا کام ہے جس کی ترغیب دی گئی ہے۔ اور مشت بے حیائی کی بات کو مشہور کرنا اس پردہ پوشی کے عمل کے خلاف ہے۔

فائدہ چنانچہ روایت حضرت ابو ہریرہ و ابن عمر رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہما میں مذکور ہے کہ جس نے کسی مسلمان کی پردہ پوشی کی اللہ تعالیٰ دنیا و آخرت میں اس کی پردہ پوشی کرے گا۔ ترمذی، ابوداؤد اور نسائی نے اس کی روایت کی ہے۔
He said: The testimony (that establishes zina) is that four witnesses testify against a man and a woman, because of Allah's saying: 'Then call four witnesses from among you' (Quran 4:15), and Allah said: 'Then they did not produce four witnesses' (Quran 24:4), and the Prophet (peace be upon him) said to the one who accused his wife: 'Bring four witnesses who will testify to the truth of your statement.' And because in stipulating four, the meaning of concealment (satr) is achieved—and concealment is encouraged—while spreading (the accusation) is its opposite.
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling with explicit textual proofs for the requirement of four witnesses in zina cases. The author (Al-Quduri) specifies that the testimony must come from four male witnesses who testify against a specific man and woman. The proofs are: (1) Quran 4:15 ('...call four witnesses from among you') regarding female fornicators; (2) Quran 24:4 ('...then they did not produce four witnesses') regarding the punishment for false accusation; (3) The Prophet (pbuh) told a man who accused his wife to bring four witnesses. The philosophical reason is that requiring four witnesses achieves the objective of satr (concealment) — it is difficult for four people to conspire on false testimony, so many guilty people will escape punishment, which is better than wrongfully punishing the innocent. Concealing the faults of others is encouraged in Islam, as highlighted by the hadith cited in the Urdu commentary: 'Whoever conceals the fault of a Muslim, Allah will conceal his fault in this world and the next.' Spreading lewdness is contrary to this value.

Key Terms
بينة (bayyinah): Specifically, the testimony of four male witnesses for zina.
ستر (satr): Concealment of faults and sins, an encouraged practice to protect people's honor.
إشاعة (isha'ah): Spreading rumors or publicizing lewdness, which is contrary to the spirit of satr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Quran 24:4
B) Quran 4:15
C) Quran 24:2
D) Quran 4:34

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires four male witnesses to prove zina, a ruling firmly based on the Quran, Sunnah, and the wisdom of satr.

Judge's Obligation to Investigate Zina Testimony
Ruling on the judge's obligation to question witnesses in zina cases.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the obligatory procedure for a judge when witnesses testify to zina and explain how the principles of ihtiyat and shubha operate to avert the hadd punishment.

Core Idea
Judges must investigate every detail of zina testimony to find any ambiguity that could avert the hadd.

When witnesses come forward with testimony about zina, the judge does not simply accept it and apply the punishment. The Hanafi school holds that the judge must interrogate the witnesses on the precise details: what was done, where, when, and with whom. This procedural obligation is rooted in the Prophet's own practice and the overriding principle of caution in hudud. The goal is to exhaust every possibility that could legally prevent the hadd from being imposed, including unknown shubha.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the judge's investigation after witnesses testify to zina. The text states that the imam (judge) asks about the details. The ruling is that this investigation is wajib (obligatory).
The text explicitly says 'al-ihtiyata fi dhalika wajib' (caution is obligatory).
2
Trace the dalil
The source of this obligation is the Prophet's (pbuh) questioning of Ma'iz ibn Malik about the manner and the woman. This precedent is cited as proof.
The hadith is narrated by Abu Dawud and is an ahad hadith, which Hanafis accept as evidence.
3
Understand the rationale
The reason for this thorough investigation is ihtiyat (caution) in hudud. The judge must ensure that the act meets the strict legal definition of zina (penetration) and that no circumstances exist that would prevent the hadd.
Examples of circumstances: the act might have been in dar al-harb, long ago, or may be a shubha like the father and his son's slave-girl.
4
Apply the concept of shubha
Shubha (legal ambiguity) can avert the hadd even if the witnesses and accused are unaware of it. The judge must probe all possibilities, using ihtiyal (seeking a lawful way) to find a valid reason to avoid punishment.
The principle is 'udra'u al-hududa bi al-shubuhat' (avert hudud by ambiguities).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا شَهِدُوا يَسْأَلُهُمُ الْإِمَامُ عَنِ الزِّنَاءِ مَا هُوَ وَكَيْفَ هُوَ وَأَيْنَ زَنَى وَمَتَى زَنَى وَبِمَنْ زَنَى لِأَنَّ النَّبِيَّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ اسْتَفْسَرَ مَاعِزًا عَنِ الْكَيْفِيَّةِ وَعَنِ الْمَزْنِيِّ بِهَا وَلِأَنَّ الْإِحْتِيَاطَ فِي ذَلِكَ وَاجِبٌ لِأَنَّهُ عَسَاهُ غَيْرَ الْفِعْلِ فِي الْفَرْجِ عَنَاهُ أَوْ زَنَى فِي دَارِ الْحَرْبِ أَوْ فِي الْمُتَقَادِمِ مِنَ الزَّمَانِ أَوْ كَانَتْ لَهُ شُبْهَةٌ لَا يَعْرِفُهَا هُوَ وَلَا الشُّهُودُ كَوَلِيِّ جَارِيَةِ الِابْنِ فَيُسْتَقْصَى فِي ذَلِكَ احْتِيَالًا لِلدَّرْءِ

ترجمہ اور جب ان گواہوں نے گواہی دیدی تب امام ان سے زنا کے بارے میں پوچھے گا کہ زنا کیا چیز ہے۔ اور کس کیفیت سے ہوتا ہے اور کہاں ہوتا ہے اور اس نے زنا کہاں پر کیا ہے۔ اور کب کیا ہے اور کس کے ساتھ کیا ہے۔ کیونکہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے حضرت ماعز بن مالک رضی اللہ عنہ سے زنا کی کیفیت اور جس عورت کے ساتھ زنا کیا تھا ان تمام باتوں کے بارے میں دریافت فرمایا تھا۔ جیسا کہ ابوداود نے روایت کی ہے اس طرح کے سوالات کرنے میں احتیاط اس لئے واجب ہے کہ شاید اس شخص نے فرج میں کچھ کرنے کی بجائے کوئی دوسری چیز مراد لی ہو یعنی مثلا نظر بازی تاک جھانک ) بوس و کنار کوہی زنا سمجھ لیا ہو یا اس نے دار الحرب میں زنا کیا ہو یا پرانے زمانہ میں ایسا کیا ہو یا جس عورت کے ساتھ ایسا کیا وہاں کوئی ایسا شبہ موجود ہو جس کی وجہ سے حد جاری نہیں ہوسکتی ہو۔ حالانکہ وہ خود نہیں جانتا ہو اور نہ گواہ جانتے ہوں۔ مثلاً کسی باپ نے اپنے بیٹے کی باندی سے زنا کیا ہو (یعنی باپ کا اپنے بیٹے کی باندی سے وطی کرنا اس کے لیے شبہ ہے جس کی وجہ سے حد ساقط ہو جاتی ہے، اور یہ شبہ خود اسے بھی معلوم نہ ہو اور نہ گواہوں کو معلوم ہو)۔ خلاصہ یہ ہوا کہ ان تمام باتوں کے بارے میں امام اچھی طرح تحقیق کرے، شاید کہ اس طرح حد ختم کرنے کا کوئی موقع مل جائے۔ تشریح فَيُسْتَقْصَى فِي ذَلِكَ احْتِيَالًا لِلدَّرْءِ یعنی اچھی طرح معلومات حاصل کرے تا کہ حد جاری نہ کرنے کی کوئی امکانی وجہ نکل آئے۔ فائدہ اس کی توضیح یہ ہے کہ جس مرد پر گواہوں نے زنا کی گواہی دی ہے ہوسکتا ہے کہ ان کو زنا کے پورے معنی معلوم نہ ہوں چنانچہ ایک مرد نے کسی اجنبیہ کا بوسہ لے لیا پھر بہت زیادہ گھبراتا ہوا رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کی خدمت میں آکر عرض کیا کہ یا رسول اللہ مجھ پر حد جاری کیجئے۔
And when they testify, the imam asks them about the zina: what is it, how was it, where did he commit zina, when did he commit zina, and with whom did he commit zina? Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) questioned Ma'iz about the manner and about the woman with whom he committed zina, and because caution is obligatory in that, for perhaps he meant something other than actual penetration, or he committed zina in the land of war, or in the distant past, or there was a legal ambiguity (shubha) that neither he nor the witnesses know—like the case of a father and his son's slave-girl. So one must be thorough in that, seeking a way to avert (the hadd).
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the procedure after witnesses have testified. The imam (judge) is required to interrogate the witnesses about the details of the alleged act: what zina is, how it was done, where, when, and with whom. This is based on the precedent of the Prophet (pbuh) questioning Ma'iz ibn Malik. The reason for such detailed inquiry is the principle of ihtiyat (caution) in hudud. The judge must explore all possibilities that could avert the hadd, such as: the witnesses might have misunderstood the definition of zina (they might think kissing or gazing constitutes zina), the act might have occurred in dar al-harb (where hadd may not apply), it might have been a long time ago (timeliness issue), or there may be a shubha (legal ambiguity) that the witnesses or even the accused are unaware of, e.g., a father having intercourse with his son's female slave (which is considered a shubha in the Hanafi school because the father has a right of ownership over his son's property, including slaves). The Urdu commentary adds the example of a man who kissed a woman and then asked the Prophet to apply hadd, showing the need to clarify the true nature of the act. The phrase 'ihtiyalan li al-dar'' means to seek a way to avert the punishment, i.e., to find any legal excuse to avoid imposing the hadd.

Key Terms
شبهة (shubha): A legal ambiguity that prevents the imposition of hadd, even if the act resembles zina.
درء (dar'): Averting or deflecting the hadd punishment; the principle that hudud should be avoided when possible.
احتيال (ihtiyal): Seeking a way or stratagem, here meaning to find a legal loophole to avert the hadd.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why must the imam ask witnesses about the details of the alleged zina?
A) To humiliate the accused
B) To ensure the punishment is carried out
C) To find any ambiguity that could avert the hadd
D) To satisfy public curiosity

Key Takeaway
A judge must exhaustively investigate zina testimony to find any legal ambiguity that would avert the hadd punishment.

Definition of Evidence (Bayyinah) for Zina
Defines the evidence requirement of four witnesses for zina

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi requirement for proving zina and identify the Quranic and Hadith proofs for the four-witness rule.

Core Idea
Zina is proven only by four male eyewitnesses — no less, no substitute.

This lesson examines the evidentiary standard for the hadd of zina in Hanafi fiqh. The requirement of four witnesses is unique to this offense, derived explicitly from the Quran. Understanding this rule reveals the Shariah's emphasis on concealment and protection of reputation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what is being defined: bayyinah (evidence) for zina. The ruling is that it must consist of four witnesses.
The act here is the proof itself, not the crime.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites two Quranic verses (an-Nisa:15 and an-Nur:4) and the hadith of li'an.
All proofs are naqli (textual).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'ista-shhidu' indicates a command; the number 'arba'atan' is explicit and definitive.
Hanafi usul holds that al-amr yufidu al-wujub.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may accept two witnesses; Hanafi insists on four based on the specific text.
The thamarah al-khilaf is whether the hadd can be established with fewer witnesses.
5
Evaluate the wisdom
The requirement facilitates satr (concealment), which is encouraged, and prevents isha'ah (spreading obscenity).
The hadith of concealment supports this.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ فَالْبَيِّنَةُ أَنْ تَشْهَدَ ارْبَعَةٌ مِنَ الشُّهُودِ عَلَى رَجُلٍ وَاِمْرَأَةِ بِالزِّنَاءِ لِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى فَاسْتَشْهِدُ وَا عَلَيْهِنَّ أَرْبَعَةً مِّنْكُمْ وَقَالَ اللهُ تَعَالَى ثُمَّ لَمْ يَأْتُوا بِاَرْبَعَةِ شُهَدَاءَ وَقَالَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لِلَّذِى قَذَفَ امْرَأَتَهُ الْتِ بِأَرْبَعَةٍ يَشْهَدُونَ عَلَى صِدْقٍ مَقَالَتِكَ وَلَانَّ فِي اِشْتِرَاطِ الْأَرْبَعَةِ يَتَحَقَّقُ مَعْنَى السَّتْر وَهُوَ مَنْدُوبٌ إِلَيْهِ وَالْإِشَاعَةُ ضِدُّهُ ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا ہے کہ گواہی کی صورت یہ ہوگی کہ گواہوں میں سے چار شخص ایک مرد اور ایک عورت پر زنا کی گواہی دیں۔ اس فرمان باری تعالیٰ کی وجہ سے فَاسْتَشْهِدُ وَا عَلَيْهِنَّ اَرْبَعَةً مِنْكُمْ یعنی ایسی عورتوں پر اپنوں میں چار شخص گواہ تلاش کرو۔ اور اللہ تعالیٰ نے یہ بھی فرمایا ہے ثُمَّ لَم يَأْتُوا بِارْبَعَةِ شُهَدَاءَ پھر وہ لوگ چار گواہ نہ لائیں اور رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے اس مرد کو جس نے اپنی بیوی پر زنا کی تہمت لگائی تھی یوں فرمایا تھا کہ تم ایسے چار مر ولاؤ جو تمہاری بات کے بچے ہونے پر گواہی دیں۔ اور یہ بھی دلیل ہے کہ چار مردوں کی شرط لگانے میں پردہ پوشی کے معنی پائے جاتے ہیں۔ اور پردہ پوشی کرنا ایک ایسا کام ہے جس کی ترغیب دی گئی ہے۔ اور مخش بے حیائی کی بات کو مشہور کرنا اس پر دہ پوشی کے عمل کے خلاف ہے۔ فائدہ چنانچہ روایت حضرت ابو ہریرہ و ابن عمر رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہما میں مذکور ہے کہ جس نے کسی مسلمان کی پردہ پوشی کی اللہ تعالیٰ دنیاو آخرت میں اس کی پردہ پوشی کرے گا۔ ترمذی، ابوداؤد اور نسائی نے اس کی روایت کی ہے۔
He said: The evidence is that four witnesses testify against a man and a woman for zina due to His statement: 'Then call four witnesses from among you' and Allah said: 'Then they did not bring four witnesses.' And the Prophet (peace be upon him) said to the one who accused his wife: 'Bring four witnesses who testify to the truth of your statement.' And because in stipulating four, the meaning of concealment is achieved, which is commendable; whereas publicizing is its opposite. Translation: Quduri said that the form of testimony is that four of the witnesses testify against a man and a woman for zina. Due to the command of Allah: 'Then call four witnesses from among you' meaning on such women, call four men from among yourselves. And Allah also said: 'Then they did not bring four witnesses.' And the Prophet (peace be upon him) said to the man who accused his wife: 'Bring four witnesses who testify to the truth of your statement.' And this is also evidence that in stipulating four men, the meaning of concealment is found. And concealment is an act that is encouraged. And publicizing obscene matters is the opposite of concealment. Benefit: In the narration of Abu Hurairah and Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with them) it is mentioned: 'Whoever conceals the fault of a Muslim, Allah will conceal his fault in this world and the Hereafter.' Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud, and Nasa'i narrated it.
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from Kitab al-Hudud. It defines the evidentiary requirement for zina: four male witnesses testifying against a specific man and woman. The author cites two Quranic verses (Surah an-Nisa:15 and Surah an-Nur:4) and the hadith of li'an (mutual imprecation) as proof. The wisdom behind the requirement of four witnesses is to conceal sins (satr), which is commendable, and to avoid spreading obscenity (isha'). The Urdu commentary elaborates on these points and adds a benefit about the virtue of concealment. The Hanafi position is that zina can only be proven by four eyewitnesses, not less, unlike some other schools.

Key Terms
البَيِّنَة (al-bayyinah): Legal evidence; here specifically the testimony of four witnesses for zina.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many witnesses are required to prove zina in Hanafi fiqh?
A) Two
B) Three
C) Four
D) One

Key Takeaway
Zina in Hanafi fiqh can only be proven by four male eyewitnesses, based on explicit Quranic commands and the principle of concealment (satr).

The Imam's Investigation (Tafteesh) Before Applying Hadd for Zina
Describes the obligatory investigation by the imam after testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five questions the imam must ask witnesses and explain why this investigation is wajib in Hanafi law to avert the hadd.

Core Idea
The hadd for zina is not automatic upon testimony; the imam must investigate to uncover any doubt that would avert punishment.

The Hanafi school prioritizes caution in hudud. This passage from al-Hidayah explains the mandatory investigation by the imam after witnesses testify. You will learn the specific questions and the rationale rooted in the Prophet's practice with Ma'iz ibn Malik.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its subject
Determine the legal status (wajib) of the imam's investigation and what it applies to (the act of questioning witnesses after testimony).
The ruling is wajib, not fard, because the evidence is zanni.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the prophetic precedent cited: the Prophet's questioning of Ma'iz about the manner and the woman.
The hadith is narrated by Abu Dawud.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the Prophet's action proves the obligation: his practice indicates the need for detailed questioning to establish zina.
Hanafi usul treats prophetic actions as evidence for obligation unless proven otherwise.
4
Note the rationale and cross-madhhab comparison
Understand the principle of ihtiyat (caution) and that other schools may not require such detail.
The text explicitly states 'ihtiyalan lil-dar'i' (to find a way to avert the hadd).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا شَهِدُوا يَسْأَلُهُمُ الْاِمَامُ عَنِ الزَّنَاءِ مَا هُوَ وَ كَيْفَ هُوَ وَايْنَ زَنى وَمَتَى زَنَى وَبِمَنْ زَنَى لِاَنَّ النَّبِيُّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ اسْتَفْسَرَ مَاعِراعَنِ الْكَيْفِيَّةِ وَعَنِ الْمَزْنِيَّةِ وَلَانَّ الْإِحْتِيَاطَ فِي ذَالِكَ وَاجِبٌ لِأَنَّهُ عَسَاهُ غَيْرَ الْفِعْلِ فِي الْفَرْجِ عنَاهُ اَوْزَنَى فِي دَارِ الْحَرْبِ اَوْ فِى الْمُتَقَادَمِ مِنَ الزَّمَانِ اَوْ كَانَتْ لَهُ شِبْهَةٌ لَا يَعْرِفُهَا هُوَ وَلَا الشُّهُودُ كَوَلِّي جَارِيَةِ الْإِبْنِ فَيُسْتَقْصَى فِي ذَالِكَ احْتِيَالًا لِلدَّرْءِ ترجمہ اور جب ان گواہوں نے گواہی دیدی تب امام ان سے زنا کے بارے میں پوچھے گا کہ زنا کیا چیز ہے۔ اور کس کیفیت سے ہوتا ہے اور کہاں ہوتا ہے اور اس نے زنا کہاں پر کیا ہے۔ اور کب کیا ہے اور کس کے ساتھ کیا ہے۔ کیونکہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے حضرت ماعز بن مالک رضی اللہ عنہ سے زنا کی کیفیت اور جس عورت کے ساتھ زنا کیا تھ ان تمام باتوں کے بارے میں دریافت فرمایا تھا۔ جیسا کہ ابوداود نے روایت کی ہے اس طرح کے سوالات کرنے میں احتیاط اس لئے واجب ہے کہ شاید اس شخص نے فرج میں کچھ کرنے کی بجائے کوئی دوسری چیز مراد لی ہو یعنی مثلا نظر بازی تاک جھانک ) بوس و کنار کوہی زنا سمجھ لیا ہو یا اس نے دار الحرب میں زنا کیا ہو یا پرانے زمانہ میں ایسا کیا ہو یا جس عورت کے ساتھ ایسا کیا وہاں کوئی ایسا شبہ موجود ہو جس کی وجہ سے حد جاری نہیں ہوسکتی ہو۔ حالانکہ وہ خود نہیں جانتا ہو اور نہ گواہ جانتے ہوں۔ مثلاً کسی باپ نے اپنے بیٹے کی باندی سے ...... ولی کی ہو۔ خلاصہ یہ ہوا کہ ان تمام باتوں کے بارے میں امام اچھی طرح تحقیق کرلے ، شاید کہ اس طرح حد ختم کرنے کا کوئی موقع مل جائے۔ تشریح فَيُسْتَقْصَى فِي ذَالِكَ احْتِيَالًا . الخ تو اچھی طرح معلومات حاصل کرے تا کہ حد جاری نہ کرنے کی کوئی امکانی وجہ نکل آئے۔ فائدہ اس کی توضیح یہ ہے کہ جس مرد پر گواہوں نے زنا کی گواہی دی ہے ہوسکتا ہے کہ ان کو زنا کے پورے معنی معلوم نہ ہوں چنا نچہ ایک مرد نے کسی اجنبیہ کا بوسہ لے لیا پھر بہت زیادہ گھبراتا ہوا رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کی خدمت میں آکر عرض کیا کہ یا رسول اللہ مجھ پر حد جاری کیجئے۔
And when they testify, the imam asks them about the zina: what it is, how it was, where he committed zina, when he committed zina, and with whom he committed zina. Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) asked Ma'iz about the manner and the woman with whom he committed zina. And because caution is obligatory there, since perhaps he intended something other than actual penetration, or he committed zina in dar al-harb, or in the distant past, or there was a doubt unknown to him and the witnesses, like a father with his son's slave-girl. So he should investigate thoroughly to find a way to avert the hadd. Translation: And when the witnesses have testified, then the imam will ask them about the zina: what is zina, in what manner, where he committed zina, when, and with whom. Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) asked Ma'iz ibn Malik about the manner and the woman with whom he committed zina, as narrated by Abu Dawud. Such questions are obligatory for caution because perhaps the person meant something other than penetration in the private part—e.g., he considered looking, staring, kissing, or embracing as zina—or he committed zina in dar al-harb, or it was a long time ago, or the woman had some doubt that would prevent the hadd, even though he and the witnesses may not know it, e.g., a father with his son's slave-girl. Summary: The imam should thoroughly investigate all these matters, so that some opportunity to avert the hadd may be found. Explanation: 'Fa yastaqsa fi dhalika ihtiyalan' means he should investigate thoroughly to find a possible reason not to implement the hadd. Benefit: The clarification is that the man against whom the witnesses testified may not know the full meaning of zina; for example, a man kissed a non-mahram woman and then came greatly distressed to the Prophet (peace be upon him) and said, 'O Messenger of Allah, impose the hadd on me.'
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the practice of the Prophet. After witnesses testify, the imam must question them to ensure the act legally constitutes zina. The questions cover the nature, manner, location, time, and partner of the act. The proof is the Prophet's questioning of Ma'iz. The reason for caution is to uncover possible doubts or misunderstandings. Examples include misinterpretation of zina (e.g., kissing considered zina), zina in dar al-harb (where hadd is not applicable), staleness of the case (delay in testimony indicates witness dishonesty), or a valid doubt (like a father with his son's slave-girl). The Urdu commentary elaborates with examples and a benefit about a man who mistook kissing for zina. The Hanafi principle is to avert hudud through doubts.

Key Terms
تفتیش (tafteesh): Investigation of the details of the alleged zina by the imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the imam ask the witnesses detailed questions about the zina?
A) To humiliate the accused
B) To establish the exact time for the record
C) To uncover doubts that may avert the hadd
D) To fulfill a procedural formality

Key Takeaway
The imam must conduct a detailed investigation after testimony to uncover any doubt that would avert the hadd.

Requirements for Testimony in Zina: Description and Verification of Witnesses
Details the description of the act and verification of witnesses' integrity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two key conditions for accepting zina testimony in Hanafi law and explain why the judge must investigate hidden justice.

Core Idea
Zina testimony requires precise description and verification of witnesses' character to avert hudud.

Hanafi law imposes stringent requirements on testimony for zina to protect the accused. Witnesses must provide a graphic description of penetration, and the judge must verify their moral integrity in both public and private. This lesson unpacks the ruling from al-Hidayah, grounded in the Prophetic command to avert hudud whenever possible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal context
Recognize that the passage deals with testimony in hudud cases, specifically zina, which requires four witnesses. The ruling establishes special conditions for acceptance.
2
Understand the required description
Focus on the simile 'like a pencil in a kohl container' (ka al-mil fi al-muk'hala). Witnesses must explicitly describe actual penetration; vague testimony is insufficient.
This simile is unique to Hanafi law for zina testimony.
3
Grasp the verification of justice
The judge must investigate witnesses' justice (adalah) in both open (apparent) and hidden (private) aspects. Mere outward piety is not enough in hudud cases.
This stricter standard aims to avert the hadd punishment.
4
Connect to the dalil
The hadith 'Idra'u al-hudud ma istata'tum' (Avert hudud as much as you can) is cited. The command to avert implies stringent procedural safeguards.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut), but it is operative here.
5
Note the contrast with other cases
In non-hudud rights (e.g., debts), apparent justice suffices unless challenged. Detention of the accused during investigation is also specific to hudud cases.
This contrast highlights the exceptionality of hudud.

اس مرد کے زنا کا طریقہ بیان کر دیں اور یہ کہدیں کہ ہم نے اس مرد کو اس حالت میں دیکھا ہے کہ اس مرد نے فلاں عورت کی شرم گاہ (فرج) میں ایسی وطی کی ہے کہ سرمہ دانی میں سلائی داخل ہوتی ہے۔ پھر قاضی ان ۔ ترمذی نے اس کی روایت کی ہے۔ یعنی ثابت ہونے سے دفع کرو۔ بخلاف دوسرے حقوق کے۔ کہ ان میں امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک ان گواہوں کی ظاہری عدالت پر ہی اکتفا کیا جائے گا۔ بشرطیکہ فریق ثانی ان گواہوں پر کوئی رکھے۔ یہاں تک کہ گواہوں کا اصل حال معلوم کرنے کیونکہ اس پر جرم کرنے ( عیب لگانے) کی تہمت موجود ہے۔ اور رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے بھی ایک شخص کو تہمت کی وجہ سے قید میں ڈال دیا تھا۔ (رواہ ابوداؤد ) برخلاف قرضوں کے کہ ان میں گواہوں کی عدالت ظاہر نہ ہونے تک مقروض کو قید میں نہیں رکھا جائے گا اور فرق کی وجہ انشاء اللہ تعالیٰ بعد میں بیان کر دی جائے گی۔ (لیکن مصنف نے فرق بیان نہیں فرمایا ہے)۔
When they clarify that and say: 'We saw him penetrating her private part like a pencil in a kohl container,' and the judge asks about their condition and they are found just in private and in public, he judges by their testimony. And he does not suffice with apparent justice in hudud, as a means to avert the hadd. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Avert the hudud as much as you can.' Contrary to other rights according to Abu Hanifa. And the investigation of private and public justice we will explain in Kitab al-Shahadat, if Allah wills. Imam Muhammad said in al-Asl: He detains him until he inquires about the witnesses because of the accusation of criminality. And the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) detained a man on suspicion. Contrary to debts, where he does not detain before the appearance of justice. The difference will come to you, if Allah wills. Translation: Then when all the witnesses describe the manner of the man's zina and say: 'We saw this man in the state that he penetrated the private part of such woman like a pencil entering a kohl container,' then the judge inquires about their condition and knows them to be just in private and public, then the judge decides on their testimony. That is, in the testimony of fornication and hudud, the judge does not suffice with their apparent justice (i.e., outward appearance and Islam) so that a means to avert the hadd can be found. Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Avert the hudud as much as you can.' Tirmidhi narrated it. That is, repel them from being established. Contrary to other rights, where according to Imam Abu Hanifa, apparent justice is sufficient, provided the opposing party does not object. And regarding the investigation of hidden and apparent justice of witnesses, we will explain it in Kitab al-Shahadat, if Allah wills. Imam Muhammad said in al-Asl: The judge detains the man against whom the testimony is given until he inquires about the witnesses because of the accusation of crime. And the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) detained a man on suspicion. (Narrated by Abu Dawud). Contrary to debts, where the debtor is not detained before the appearance of justice. And the reason for the difference will be explained later, if Allah wills. (But the author did not explain the difference.)
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof detailing the quality of testimony for zina. Witnesses must describe actual penetration using the simile of a pencil in a kohl container (al-mil fi al-muk'hala). The judge must verify both open (apparent) and hidden (private) justice of the witnesses, not merely their outward appearance. This strictness is based on the hadith 'Idra'u al-hudud' (Avert the hudud). Unlike other legal rights, where apparent justice suffices, in hudud the judge must investigate their integrity in private. Additionally, Imam Muhammad in al-Asl states that the accused may be detained during investigation to prevent collusion, contrasting with debt cases. The Urdu commentary elaborates on these points.

Key Terms
الْمُكْحَلَة (al-muk'hala): A kohl container; the simile illustrates full penetration in the required testimony.

Confession of Zina: Conditions and the Four-Time Requirement
Inter-madhhab dispute on conditions of zina confession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi conditions for a valid confession of zina and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument on the number of confessions.

Core Idea
A confession of zina is not accepted until repeated four times, each time rejected by the judge.

The Hanafi school imposes strict conditions on confessions in hudud cases. For zina, the confessor must be an adult and sane, and the confession must be made in four separate sittings, with the judge rejecting it each time. This contrasts with the Shafi'i position, which accepts a single confession by analogy to other legal matters. Why such stringency? Because hudud involve severe punishments, and the law seeks to avoid them by requiring utmost clarity and providing opportunities for retraction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three conditions for a valid confession
From the text, note the requirements: baligh (adult), aqil (sane), and the confession must occur four times in four different sittings. The judge must reject (radda) the confessor each time.
The text says 'kullama afarra raddahu al-qadi' – each time he confesses, the judge rejects him.
2
Understand the rationale for adulthood and sanity
The text explains: 'the statement of a minor and insane person is not considered or does not necessitate the hadd.' This is a general Hanafi principle: the legal capacity of the confessor is essential.
Minor and insane persons are not fully accountable; their admissions lack legal effect in hudud.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof for four repetitions
Though not quoted directly, the Hanafi proof is the hadith of Ma'iz: the Prophet (saw) turned away from him each time he confessed until the fourth time. This establishes the requirement by sunnah.
The principle of ihtiyat (caution) in hudud also supports requiring multiple confessions.
4
Contrast with the Shafi'i position and its proof
Imam al-Shafi'i argues by qiyas: since one confession suffices for other legal rights (e.g., debts), it should suffice for zina. The Hanafi response is that zina is unique due to its gravity and the hadd punishment.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) is clear: a single confession never triggers hadd in Hanafi, but it does in Shafi'i.
5
Determine the operative ruling in the Hanafi madhhab
The mufta bihi position is that four confessions in four separate sittings are required, with the judge rejecting each time. This is based on the established practice of the Prophet and the Quranic principle of avoiding hudud in doubtful cases.
The text mentions 'madhhabuna' – our madhhab – affirming the Hanafi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَالْإِقْرَارُانْ يُقِرَّ الْبَالِغُ الْعَاقِلُ عَلَى نَفْسِهِ بِالزِنَاءِ اَرْبَعَ مَرَّاتٍ فِي أَرْبَعِ مَجَالِسَ مِنْ مَجَالِسِ الْمُقِرِ كُلَّمَا أَفَرِّرَدَّهُ الْقَاضِي فَاشْتِرَاطُ الْبُلُوغ وَالْعَقْلِ لِاَنَّ قَوْلَ الصَّبِيِّ وَالْمَجْنُونِ غَيْرُ مُعْتَبَرٍ أَوْ هُوَ غَيْرُ مُوجِبِ لِلْحَدِوَ اشْتِرَاطُ الْاَرْبَعِ مَذْهَبُنَا وَعِنْدَ الشَّافِعِيُّ يُكتفى بِالْإِقْرَارِ مَرَّةً وَاحِدَةً اِعْتِبَارًا بِسَائِرِ الْحَقُوقِ وَهَذَا لِأَنَّهُ مُظْهِرْوَ
He said: The confession is that the adult, sane person confesses zina against himself four times in four sittings of the confessor, each time the judge rejects him. The condition of adulthood and sanity is because the statement of a minor and insane person is not considered or does not necessitate the hadd. The condition of four is our madhhab. With al-Shafi'i, a single confession suffices, by analogy with other rights. And this is because he is manifesting...
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with inter-madhhab dispute. It defines the conditions for a valid confession of zina. The confessor must be adult (baligh) and sane (aqil). The confession must be made four times in four separate sittings, and each time the judge should reject/refuse the confession. This is the Hanafi position. Imam al-Shafi'i accepts a single confession, analogizing to other legal cases. The rationale for Hanafi is that zina is a grave matter requiring strong proof; the repetition and judge's rejection provide opportunity for retraction. The Arabic text cuts off here, but the Urdu commentary would likely elaborate on the Hanafi proof.

Key Terms
الْإِقْرَار (al-iqrar): Confession; a legal acknowledgment, here specifically for zina.
الْحَدّ (al-hadd): Fixed corporal punishment prescribed by Islamic law for certain crimes.
مَجْلِس (majlis): Sitting; a discrete session of court or legal proceeding.

A confession of zina in Hanafi fiqh is only valid if the adult, sane person confesses four times in four separate judicial sittings, with the judge rejecting each time.

Testimony in Zina: Witness Screening and Dar' al-Hudud
Ruling with proof: witness screening in zina

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the judge's duty to investigate inner rectitude of witnesses in zina cases, explain the dalil from the hadith 'Idra’u al-hudud', and distinguish this from the standard applied to other rights.

Core Idea
In hudud, the judge must probe inner rectitude to avert punishment per the Prophet's command.

This lesson examines the heightened scrutiny required for witness testimony in zina cases according to the Hanafi school. The judge is not satisfied with apparent rectitude; he must investigate both outward and inward probity. This is rooted in the famous principle of dar' al-hudud (averting penalties) derived from the prophetic command. Understanding this distinction is crucial for appreciating how the Hanafi school prioritizes the protection of the accused in capital offenses.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
The act is the judge's acceptance of testimony in a zina case. The ruling is that he must investigate the secret rectitude of witnesses, not merely their apparent piety. This is a wajib (obligatory) duty on the judge.
The passage contrasts this with other rights (huquq) where apparent rectitude suffices according to Abu Hanifa.
2
Locate the Dalil
The proof is the hadith: 'Idra’u al-hudud ma istata’tum' (Avert the hudud as much as you can). This is a sunnah ahad from Tirmidhi.
The Hanafi school treats this hadith as zanni al-thubut but qati al-dalalah due to the clear command 'Idra’u'.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
The imperative 'Idra’u' (avert) indicates obligation (wujub). The phrase 'ma istata’tum' (as much as you can) encourages exhausting all lawful means to avoid punishment. Investigating inner rectitude is one such means.
This shows that the judge is obliged to create doubt by thorough verification, if possible.
4
Note the Ikhtilaf with Other Rights
In hudud, the judge must go beyond apparent rectitude; in other rights (debts, contracts), apparent rectitude suffices unless challenged. This is the position of Abu Hanifa.
Imam Muhammad’s al-Asl prescribes detaining the accused pending investigation, similar to the Prophet's own practice.
5
Evaluate the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical consequence: in hudud cases, the judge must actively seek grounds for doubt before accepting testimony, often leading to acquittals. In civil matters, testimony is accepted at face value unless contested.
This reflects the Hanafi maxim that hudud are averted by shubuhat (doubts).

عدالت (یعنی ظاہری شکل و صورت اور ان کے اسلام پر اکتفا نہیں کرے گا تا کہ حد جاری نہ کرنے کا حیلہ پیدا ہو سکے۔ اس لئے کہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ جہاں تک تم سے ہو سکے حدود کو ٹال دو ۔ ترمذی نے اس کی روایت کی ہے۔ یعنی ثابت ہونے سے دفع کرو۔ بخلاف دوسرے حقوق کے۔ کہ ان میں امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک ان گواہوں کی ظاہری عدالت پر ہی اکتفا کیا جائے گا۔ بشرطیکہ فریق ثانی ان گواہوں پر کوئی اعتراض نہ کرے) اور گواہوں کے خفیہ اور ظاہری عدالت کے بارے میں ہم انشاء اللہ کتاب الشہادات میں بیان کریں گے۔ امام محمد نے اصل میں فرمایا ہے کہ قاضی اس مرد کو جس کی گواہی پیش کی گئی ہے قید خانہ میں رکھے۔ یہاں تک کہ گواہوں کا اصل حال معلوم کرنے کیونکہ اس پر جرم کرنے ( عیب لگانے) کی تہمت موجود ہے۔ اور رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے بھی ایک شخص کو تہمت کی وجہ سے قید میں ڈال دیا تھا۔ (رواہ ابوداؤد ) برخلاف قرضوں کے کہ ان میں گواہوں کی عدالت ظاہر نہ ہونے تک مقروض کو قید میں نہیں رکھا جائے گا اور فرق کی وجہ انشاء اللہ تعالیٰ بعد میں بیان کر دی جائے گی۔ (لیکن مصنف نے فرق بیان نہیں فرمایا ہے)۔
Then when they (the witnesses) explain that and say: 'We saw him insert it into her private part like the insertion of a kohl stick into the kohl container,' and the judge asks about them and they are found to be rectitudinous in secret and in public, then he will judge by their testimony. And he will not be satisfied with apparent rectitude in hadd cases, as a means of averting (the penalty). The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Avert the hudud as much as you can.' Unlike other rights according to Abu Hanifa. We will explain the verification of secret and public rectitude in the Book of Testimony, if Allah wills. He (Imam Muhammad) said in al-Asl: 'He will imprison him until he asks about the witnesses, due to the accusation of crime. And the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) imprisoned a man on suspicion.' Unlike debts, where one is not imprisoned before the appearance of rectitude. The distinction will come to you, if Allah wills. Translation: Then when all those witnesses describe the manner of the man's zina and say...
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage deals with the stringent requirements for testimony in zina cases. The witnesses must describe the act in graphic detail (like a kohl stick into its container) to eliminate any ambiguity. The judge must investigate their inner and outer rectitude, not just apparent piety, because the Prophet commanded us to avert hudud punishments by any lawful means. Unlike other legal rights (e.g., debts), where Abu Hanifa holds that apparent rectitude suffices unless challenged, in hudud the judge must actively probe. Following Imam Muhammad's al-Asl, the accused may be detained pending this investigation because of the serious accusation, analogously to the Prophet's practice. This reflects the Hanafi principle that hudud are averted by doubts (shubuhat).

Key Terms
شهادة (shahada): Testimony; the formal act of bearing witness in court. In zina, requires four male witnesses and detailed description.
عدالة (adala): Rectitude; probity of a witness, both apparent and hidden. In hudud, inner rectitude must be verified.
درء الحدود (dar’ al-hudud): The principle of averting prescribed punishments by any legal doubt (shubha).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why does the judge not accept apparent rectitude alone in zina testimony?
A) Because the witnesses must be Muslims
B) To create a means of averting the hadd punishment as instructed by the Prophet
C) Because the accused is always guilty
D) Because debts require public rectitude

Key Takeaway
In hudud cases, the judge must investigate both apparent and inner rectitude of witnesses to fulfil the duty of averting punishment as commanded by the Prophet.

Hudud — Fixed Penalties
intermediate
8 min
Conditions for a Valid Confession of Zina
States the Hanafi requirement for valid confession in zina cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to STATE the four conditions for a valid confession of zina in Hanafi law and IDENTIFY why each condition is required.

Core Idea
A confession of zina must be made four times in four separate sittings by a sane adult.

This passage from al-Quduri’s Mukhtasar, as explained by al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah, lays down the strict procedural requirements for establishing zina through confession. Unlike other legal claims where a single confession suffices, the Hanafi school demands a fourfold repetition in separate sessions. Understanding these conditions is essential to grasp the school’s rigorous approach to hudud penalties and the underlying principle of averting punishment through doubts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the confessor’s qualifications
The text states the confessor must be baligh (adult) and aaqil (sane). The statement of a child or insane person is not considered (ghayr mu'tabar) and does not necessitate hadd.
Adulthood and sanity are prerequisites for legal capacity (ahliyyah).
2
Count the required number of confessions
The confession must be made four times. This is a requirement of the Hanafi school (madhhabuna). The number is derived from the hadith of Ma'iz and analogy to four witnesses in zina.
Four is the same number as required for witnesses in zina.
3
Examine the requirement of separate sittings
The four confessions must occur in four different sittings (majalis). The judge turns the confessor away after each confession to ensure separation.
Unity of sitting could create doubt about the independence of each confession.
4
Define the separation method according to Abu Hanifa
The confessor must leave the judge's sight after each confession, then return for the next. This is derived from the practice with Ma'iz.
The difference of the confessor's sitting is considered, not the judge's.
5
Understand the legal effect
The hadd (punishment) becomes wajib only after all four confessions are completed. Before that, the judge must avert the hadd by turning the confessor away.
This aligns with the principle of averting hudud through doubts (shubuhat).

الْبُلُوغ وَالْعَقْلِ لِاَنَّ قَوْلَ الصَّبِيِّ وَالْمَجْنُونِ غَيْرُ مُعْتَبَرٍ أَوْ هُوَ غَيْرُ مُوجِبِ لِلْحَدِوَ اشْتِرَاطُ الْاَرْبَعِ مَذْهَبُنَا وَعِنْدَ الشَّافِعِيُّ يُكتفى بِالْإِقْرَارِ
