وَلَادَّ الشَّهَادَةَ اخْتَصَّتْ فِيهِ بِزِيَادَةِ الْعَدَدِ فَكَذَا الْإِقْرَارُ اِعْظَامًا لِامْرِ الزَّنَاءِ وَتَحْقِيقًا لِمَعْنَى السَّتْرِ وَلَا بُدَّ مِنْ اخْتِلَافِ الْمَجَالِسِ لِمَارَوَيْنَا وَلِاَنَّ لِاِتِّحَادِ الْمَجْلِسِ أَثرًا فِى جَمِيعِ الْمُتَفَرِّقَاتِ فَعِنْدَهُ يَتَحَقَّقُ شُبُهَةُ الْإِتِحَادِ فِي الْإِقْرَارِ وَالْإِقْرَارُ قَائِمَ بِالْمُقِرِ فَيُعْتَبَرُ اخْتِلَافُ مَجْلِسِهِ دُونَ مَجْلِسِ الْقَاضِي فَالْاِخْتِلَافُ بِأَنْ يَرُدَّهُ الْقَاضِي كُلَّمَا أَقَرَّ فَيَذْهَبُ حَيْثُ لَا يَرَاهُ ثُمَّ يَجِيءُ فَيُقِرُّ هُوَ الْمَرْوِيُّ عَنْ أَبِي حَنِيفَةٌ لِأَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ طَرَدَمَاعِزَافِي كُلَّ مَرَّةٍ حَتَّى تَوَارَى بِحِيْطَانِ الْمَدِينَةِ ترجمه قدوری نے کہا ہے کہ از خود اقرار کرنے کی صورت یہ ہوگی کہ عاقل بالغ اپنی ذات پر چار مرتبہ چار مجلسوں میں زنا کرنے کا اقرار کرے اور ہر بار جب بھی اقرار کرے تو قاضی اسے رد کر دے۔ اس مسئلہ میں مجرم کے بارے میں عاقل و بالغ ہونے کی شرط اس لئے لگائی گئی ہے کہ بچہ اور دیوانہ کا اقرار معتبر نہیں ہوگا یا اس سے حد واجب نہیں ہوگی اور چار مرتبوں کی شرط لگانا ہمارا مذہب ہے اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک صرف ایک بار اقرار کافی ہے۔ جیسا کہ دوسرے حقوق میں ایک بار اقرار کرنا کافی ہوتا ہے اور یہ اس وجہ سے کہ اقرار ایک ظاہر کرنے والا قول ہے۔ اور بار بار اقرار کرنے سے زیادہ ظہور کا کچھ بھی فائدہ نہیں دیتا ہے۔ بخلاف گواہوں میں عدد زیادہ ہونے کے یعنی گواہوں کی تعداد زیادہ ہونے سے دل کا اطمینان بڑھتا ہے اور ہماری دلیل وہ حدیث ہے جس میں حضرت ماعز بن مالک رضی اللہ عنہ کا قصہ مروی ہے۔ کہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے ان پر حد قائم کرنے میں تاخیر فرمائی۔ یہاں تک کہ ان کا چار بار اقرار چار مجلسوں میں پورا ہوا۔ اس کی روایت بخاری، مسلم، ابوداؤ داور نسائی وغیرہ نے کی ہے۔ پھر اگر چار سے کم میں وہ اقرار ظاہر ہو جاتا جس سے حد لازم آ جاتی تو آپ حد مارنے میں تاخیر نہ فرماتے کیونکہ حد واجب ثابت ہو گئی اور اس دلیل سے بھی کہ زنا میں ایک خاموش قسم کی گواہی چار مردوں کی معتبر ہے۔ تو اقرار میں بھی یہی بات ہوگی۔ تاکہ زنا کے معاملہ کا زیادہ خوفناک ہونا ظاہر ہو جائے اور اس لئے بھی کہ اس طرح پردہ پوشی کے معنی پائے جائیں۔ نیز ۔ اقرار میں مجلسوں کا مختلف ہونا بھی ضروری ہے۔ اس کی دلیل وہ حدیث ہے جس کی روایت ہم نے پہلے کر دی ہے اور اس دلیل سے بھی کہ ایک مجلس کو متفرق چیزوں کو جمع کرنے میں دخل ہوتا ہے۔ اور مجلس متحد ہونے کے وقت اقرار متحد ہونے کا شبہ پیدا ہو گا۔ اور اقرار اپنے اقرار کرنے والے کے ساتھ قائم ہے اس لئے اقرار کرنے والے کی مجلس کا اختلاف معتبر ہو گا۔ لیکن قاضی کی مجلسوں کے مختلف ہونے کا اعتبار نہیں ہے۔ اور مجلسوں کے مختلف ہونے کی صورت یہ ہوگی کہ وہ مجرم جب قاضی کے سامنے اقرار کرے تو قاضی ہر بار یعنی جب بھی اقرار کرے قاضی اسے رد کر دے تا کہ وہ چلا جائے اور اتنا دور کہ قاضی اسے نہ دیکھے پھر دوبارہ آکر اقرار کرے۔ امام ابو حنیفہ سے یہی مروی ہے کیونکہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے حضرت ماعز رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ کو ہر بار رد کیا یہاں تک وہ مدینہ کی دیواروں میں پوشیدہ ہو گئے۔
He (al-Quduri) said: Confession is that the adult, sane person confesses against himself of zina four times in four sittings of his own sessions; whenever he confesses, the judge turns him away. The stipulation of adulthood and sanity is because the statement of a child and insane is not considered or does not necessitate hadd. The stipulation of four is our madhhab. According to al-Shafi'i, one confession suffices, by analogy to other rights. And this is because confession is a manifesting statement, and repetition of confession does not give added clarity, unlike increase in number in testimony. Our proof is the hadith of Ma'iz ibn Malik: the Prophet (peace be upon him) delayed carrying out the hadd until the confession from him was completed four times in four sittings. If it had been established with fewer, he would not have delayed, because the obligation would be immediate. And because testimony in zina is specified with four witnesses, so also confession, to magnify the matter of zina and realize the meaning of concealment. The sittings must differ, based on what we narrated, and because unity of sitting has an effect on all separated matters; then at the time of unity the doubt of unity in confession arises. Confession is established by the confessor, so the difference of his sitting is considered, not the judge's sitting. The difference is that the judge turns him away each time he confesses, so he goes where he cannot see him, then comes and confesses. This is narrated from Abu Hanifa, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) turned away Ma'iz each time until he hid behind the walls of Madina.
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage explains the Hanafi procedure for a valid confession (iqrar) of zina. The confessor must be adult and sane; children and the insane are excluded because their statements carry no legal weight. The confession must be repeated four times in four separate sittings. The judge actively turns the confessor away after each confession to ensure the sitting is separate and to confirm the confessor's sincerity. The Hanafi school relies on the famous hadith of Ma'iz ibn Malik, where the Prophet delayed the hadd penalty until Ma'iz had confessed four times, each time in a different session. Had one confession been sufficient, the Prophet would not have delayed. Moreover, since zina witnesses must be four men, the confession likewise requires four repetitions to emphasize the gravity of the offense and to promote concealment (sitr). The Shafi'i school disagrees, holding that one confession suffices, analogizing to other legal rights. The Hanafi response is that the hadith of Ma'iz is explicit, and the analogy to testimony is stronger. The sittings must be separate in the sense that the confessor leaves the judge's presence after each confession, as practiced with Ma'iz.

Key Terms
إقرار (iqrar): Confession; a statement by a person against his own interest. Here specifically confession of zina.
مجلس (majlis): Session or sitting; a physical gathering where the confession takes place. Separate sitting means the confessor leaves the judge's presence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if a sane adult confesses to zina only three times in three separate sittings before a Hanafi judge?
A) The judge imposes the hadd immediately
B) The judge must still impose the hadd because three is a majority
C) The judge cannot impose the hadd; the confession is incomplete
D) The judge asks for a fourth confession in the same sitting

Key Takeaway
A valid confession of zina in Hanafi law requires four separate confessions by a sane adult, each in a distinct sitting, with the judge actively turning the confessor away after each.

Hudud — Fixed Penalties
intermediate
8 min
The Proof and Dispute: Why Four Confessions?
Presents the proof and dispute regarding the number of confessions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to EXPLAIN the Hanafi proof (hadith of Ma'iz) and ANALYZE the Shafi'i objection and Hanafi response regarding the number of confessions for zina.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school demands four confessions based on the explicit hadith of Ma'iz, overriding qiyas to other rights.

This passage continues from the conditions and introduces the key proof for the fourfold requirement: the hadith of Ma'iz ibn Malik. It also presents the Shafi'i objection that one confession should suffice by analogy to other legal rights, and the Hanafi rebuttal that the hadith is explicit and the gravity of zina requires special treatment. Understanding this debate exposes the methodological differences between the schools in handling evidence and analogical reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi proof (dalil)
The Hanafi school relies on the hadith of Ma'iz. The Prophet delayed the hadd until four confessions were made in four sittings. This indicates that the hadd was not obligatory until four confessions were completed.
The hadith is narrated by Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud, and Nasa'i.
2
Understand the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that one confession suffices, analogizing to other legal claims where a single confession establishes liability. Repetition does not add evidentiary value, unlike witnesses.
Shafi'i uses qiyas on other rights (huquq).
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school responds that the explicit hadith overrides qiyas. Moreover, the analogy to testimony is stronger: since zina requires four witnesses, confession should also require four repetitions. This emphasizes the gravity of the offense and the principle of concealment (sitr).
The Hanafi position is based on dalil naqli (hadith) and qiyas jali (analogy to testimony).
4
Determine the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Hanafi law, a single confession does not trigger the hadd; the judge must turn the confessor away. Under Shafi'i law, one confession suffices, and the hadd is imposed immediately unless retracted.
This difference has significant implications for the implementation of hudud.
5
Evaluate the tarjih (preferred view)
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi in the school. Al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah upholds it against Shafi'i, citing the hadith and the principle of averting hudud through doubts.
The strength of the Hanafi position lies in its reliance on a clear prophetic practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَالْإِقْرَارُانْ يُقِرَّ الْبَالِغُ الْعَاقِلُ عَلَى نَفْسِهِ بِالزِنَاءِ اَرْبَعَ مَرَّاتٍ فِي أَرْبَعِ مَجَالِسَ مِنْ مَجَالِسِ الْمُقِرِ كُلَّمَا أَفَرِّرَدَّهُ الْقَاضِي فَاشْتِرَاطُ الْبُلُوغ وَالْعَقْلِ لِاَنَّ قَوْلَ الصَّبِيِّ وَالْمَجْنُونِ غَيْرُ مُعْتَبَرٍ أَوْ هُوَ غَيْرُ مُوجِبِ لِلْحَدِوَ اشْتِرَاطُ الْاَرْبَعِ مَذْهَبُنَا وَعِنْدَ الشَّافِعِيُّ يُكتفى بِالْإِقْرَارِ مَرَّةً وَاحِدَةً اِعْتِبَارًا بِسَائِرِ الْحَقُوقِ وَهَذَا لِأَنَّهُ مُظْهِرْوَ تَكْرَارُ الْإِقْرَارِ لَا يُفِيدُ زِيَادَةُ الظُّهُورِ بِخِلَافِ زِيَادَةِ الْعَدَدِفِي الشَّهَادَةِ وَلَنَا حَدِيثُ مَاغِزٌ فَإِنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ أَخَّرَ الا قَامَةَ إِلَى أَنْ تَمَّ الْإِقْرَارُ مِنْهُ اَرْبَعَ مَرَّاتٍ فِي أَرْبَعِ مَجَالِسَ فَلَوْظَهَرَ دُونَهَالَمَا أَخَّرَهَا لِقُبُوتِ الْوُجُوبِ وَلَادَّ الشَّهَادَةَ اخْتَصَّتْ فِيهِ بِزِيَادَةِ الْعَدَدِ فَكَذَا الْإِقْرَارُ اِعْظَامًا لِامْرِ الزَّنَاءِ وَتَحْقِيقًا لِمَعْنَى السَّتْرِ وَلَا بُدَّ مِنْ اخْتِلَافِ الْمَجَالِسِ لِمَارَوَيْنَا وَلِاَنَّ لِاِتِّحَادِ الْمَجْلِسِ أَثرًا فِى جَمِيعِ الْمُتَفَرِّقَاتِ فَعِنْدَهُ يَتَحَقَّقُ شُبُهَةُ الْإِتِحَادِ فِي الْإِقْرَارِ وَالْإِقْرَارُ قَائِمَ بِالْمُقِرِ فَيُعْتَبَرُ اخْتِلَافُ مَجْلِسِهِ دُونَ مَجْلِسِ الْقَاضِي فَالْاِخْتِلَافُ بِأَنْ يَرُدَّهُ الْقَاضِي كُلَّمَا أَقَرَّ فَيَذْهَبُ حَيْثُ لَا يَرَاهُ ثُمَّ يَجِيءُ فَيُقِرُّ هُوَ الْمَرْوِيُّ عَنْ أَبِي حَنِيفَةٌ لِأَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ طَرَدَمَاعِزَافِي كُلَّ مَرَّةٍ حَتَّى تَوَارَى بِحِيْطَانِ الْمَدِينَةِ ترجمه قدوری نے کہا ہے کہ از خود اقرار کرنے کی صورت یہ ہوگی کہ عاقل بالغ اپنی ذات پر چار مرتبہ چار مجلسوں میں زنا کرنے کا اقرار کرے اور ہر بار جب بھی اقرار کرے تو قاضی اسے رد کر دے۔ اس مسئلہ میں مجرم کے بارے میں عاقل و بالغ ہونے کی شرط اس لئے لگائی گئی ہے کہ بچہ اور دیوانہ کا اقرار معتبر نہیں ہوگا یا اس سے حد واجب نہیں ہوگی اور چار مرتبوں کی شرط لگانا ہمارا مذہب ہے اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک صرف ایک بار اقرار کافی ہے۔ جیسا کہ دوسرے حقوق میں ایک بار اقرار کرنا کافی ہوتا ہے اور یہ اس وجہ سے کہ اقرار ایک ظاہر کرنے والا قول ہے۔ اور بار بار اقرار کرنے سے زیادہ ظہور کا کچھ بھی فائدہ نہیں دیتا ہے۔ بخلاف گواہوں میں عدد زیادہ ہونے کے یعنی گواہوں کی تعداد زیادہ ہونے سے دل کا اطمینان بڑھتا ہے اور ہماری دلیل وہ حدیث ہے جس میں حضرت ماعز بن مالک رضی اللہ عنہ کا قصہ مروی ہے۔ کہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے ان پر حد قائم کرنے میں تاخیر فرمائی۔ یہاں تک کہ ان کا چار بار اقرار چار مجلسوں میں پورا ہوا۔ اس کی روایت بخاری، مسلم، ابوداؤ داور نسائی وغیرہ نے کی ہے۔ پھر اگر چار سے کم میں وہ اقرار ظاہر ہو جاتا جس سے حد لازم آ جاتی تو آپ حد مارنے میں تاخیر نہ فرماتے کیونکہ حد واجب ثابت ہو گئی اور اس دلیل سے بھی کہ زنا میں ایک خاموش قسم کی گواہی چار مردوں کی معتبر ہے۔ تو اقرار میں بھی یہی بات ہوگی۔ تاکہ زنا کے معاملہ کا زیادہ خوفناک ہونا ظاہر ہو جائے اور اس لئے بھی کہ اس طرح پردہ پوشی کے معنی پائے جائیں۔ نیز ۔ اقرار میں مجلسوں کا مختلف ہونا بھی ضروری ہے۔ اس کی دلیل وہ حدیث ہے جس کی روایت ہم نے پہلے کر دی ہے اور اس دلیل سے بھی کہ ایک مجلس کو متفرق چیزوں کو جمع کرنے میں دخل ہوتا ہے۔ اور مجلس متحد ہونے کے وقت اقرار متحد ہونے کا شبہ پیدا ہو گا۔ اور اقرار اپنے اقرار کرنے والے کے ساتھ قائم ہے اس لئے اقرار کرنے والے کی مجلس کا اختلاف معتبر ہو گا۔ لیکن قاضی کی مجلسوں کے مختلف ہونے کا اعتبار نہیں ہے۔ اور مجلسوں کے مختلف ہونے کی صورت یہ ہوگی کہ وہ مجرم جب قاضی کے سامنے اقرار کرے تو قاضی ہر بار یعنی جب بھی اقرار کرے قاضی اسے رد کر دے تا کہ وہ چلا جائے اور اتنا دور کہ قاضی اسے نہ دیکھے پھر دوبارہ آکر اقرار کرے۔ امام ابو حنیفہ سے یہی مروی ہے کیونکہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے حضرت ماعز رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ کو ہر بار رد کیا یہاں تک وہ مدینہ کی دیواروں میں پوشیدہ ہو گئے۔
He (al-Quduri) said: Confession is that the adult, sane person confesses against himself of zina four times in four sittings of his own sessions; whenever he confesses, the judge turns him away. The stipulation of adulthood and sanity is because the statement of a child and insane is not considered or does not necessitate hadd. The stipulation of four is our madhhab. According to al-Shafi'i, one confession suffices, by analogy to other rights. And this is because confession is a manifesting statement, and repetition of confession does not give added clarity, unlike increase in number in testimony. Our proof is the hadith of Ma'iz ibn Malik: the Prophet (peace be upon him) delayed carrying out the hadd until the confession from him was completed four times in four sittings. If it had been established with fewer, he would not have delayed, because the obligation would be immediate. And because testimony in zina is specified with four witnesses, so also confession, to magnify the matter of zina and realize the meaning of concealment. The sittings must differ, based on what we narrated, and because unity of sitting has an effect on all separated matters; then at the time of unity the doubt of unity in confession arises. Confession is established by the confessor, so the difference of his sitting is considered, not the judge's sitting. The difference is that the judge turns him away each time he confesses, so he goes where he cannot see him, then comes and confesses. This is narrated from Abu Hanifa, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) turned away Ma'iz each time until he hid behind the walls of Madina.
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage explains the Hanafi procedure for a valid confession (iqrar) of zina. The confessor must be adult and sane; children and the insane are excluded because their statements carry no legal weight. The confession must be repeated four times in four separate sittings. The judge actively turns the confessor away after each confession to ensure the sitting is separate and to confirm the confessor's sincerity. The Hanafi school relies on the famous hadith of Ma'iz ibn Malik, where the Prophet delayed the hadd penalty until Ma'iz had confessed four times, each time in a different session. Had one confession been sufficient, the Prophet would not have delayed. Moreover, since zina witnesses must be four men, the confession likewise requires four repetitions to emphasize the gravity of the offense and to promote concealment (sitr). The Shafi'i school disagrees, holding that one confession suffices, analogizing to other legal rights. The Hanafi response is that the hadith of Ma'iz is explicit, and the analogy to testimony is stronger. The sittings must be separate in the sense that the confessor leaves the judge's presence after each confession, as practiced with Ma'iz.

Key Terms
إقرار (iqrar): Confession; a statement by a person against his own interest. Here specifically confession of zina.
مجلس (majlis): Session or sitting; a physical gathering where the confession takes place. Separate sitting means the confessor leaves the judge's presence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary Hanafi response to the Shafi'i argument that one confession should suffice by analogy to other rights?
A) The Shafi'i argument is rejected because other rights are not as serious as zina
B) The explicit hadith of Ma'iz overrides the qiyas, and analogy to testimony is stronger
C) The Hanafi school does not accept qiyas at all
D) The Shafi'i position is considered weak due to lack of evidence

Key Takeaway
The fourfold confession requirement in Hanafi law is justified by the explicit hadith of Ma'iz and the analogy to four witnesses, overriding the Shafi'i qiyas to other rights.

Four Confessions for Zina: The Hanafi Requirement
Establishing the Hanafi ruling on multiple confessions with proof from the hadith of Ma'iz

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school requires four confessions in four separate sittings to establish the hadd for zina and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Four confessions in separate sittings are required for zina—the Prophet's treatment of Ma'iz teaches the gravity of this crime.

In Hanafi fiqh, establishing the hadd punishment for zina through confession is not straightforward. A single confession does not suffice; the confessor must voluntarily state his guilt four times in four different sittings, each time being rejected by the judge. This stringent requirement reflects the school's commitment to caution and concealment. In this lesson, we examine the textual proof and reasoning behind this position, as well as the opposing view of Imam al-Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact condition: four confessions in four separate sittings. Note that the hadd is wajib only when this condition is fulfilled.
The passage begins by stating that repetition of confession does not add certainty, unlike testimony.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi'i holds that one confession suffices, as in other legal acknowledgments.
The opposing dalil is that repetition does not increase certainty, so one confession should be enough.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand the Shafi'i reasoning: since a single confession is accepted for other rights (e.g., debt), why require multiple for zina?
The Hanafi response counters by emphasizing the unique gravity of zina.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Examine the two proofs: (1) the hadith of Ma'iz, where the Prophet delayed punishment until four confessions, and (2) analogy (qiyas) to the requirement of four witnesses in testimony.
The commentator explains that separate sittings are necessary to avoid doubt of unity.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Conclude the practical difference: under Hanafi, less than four confessions do not trigger the hadd; under Shafi'i, one confession does.
This reflects the Hanafi emphasis on caution (al-hadd yudra'u bi al-shubuhat).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تَكْرَارُ الْإِقْرَارِ لَا يُفِيدُ زِيَادَةُ الظُّهُورِ بِخِلَافِ زِيَادَةِ الْعَدَدِفِي الشَّهَادَةِ وَلَنَا حَدِيثُ مَاعِزٍ فَإِنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ أَخَّرَ الْإِقَامَةَ إِلَى أَنْ تَمَّ الْإِقْرَارُ مِنْهُ أَرْبَعَ مَرَّاتٍ فِي أَرْبَعِ مَجَالِسَ فَلَوْ ظَهَرَ دُونَهَا لَمَا أَخَّرَهَا لِقُبُوتِ الْوُجُوبِ وَلَأَنَّ الشَّهَادَةَ اخْتَصَّتْ فِيهِ بِزِيَادَةِ الْعَدَدِ فَكَذَا الْإِقْرَارُ اِعْظَامًا لِأَمْرِ الزِّنَاءِ وَتَحْقِيقًا لِمَعْنَى السَّتْرِ وَلَا بُدَّ مِنْ اخْتِلَافِ الْمَجَالِسِ لِمَا رَوَيْنَا وَلِأَنَّ لِاتِّحَادِ الْمَجْلِسِ أَثَرًا فِي جَمِيعِ الْمُتَفَرِّقَاتِ فَعِنْدَهُ يَتَحَقَّقُ شُبُهَةُ الْإِتِحَادِ فِي الْإِقْرَارِ وَالْإِقْرَارُ قَائِمٌ بِالْمُقِرِّ فَيُعْتَبَرُ اخْتِلَافُ مَجْلِسِهِ دُونَ مَجْلِسِ الْقَاضِي فَالْاخْتِلَافُ بِأَنْ يَرُدَّهُ الْقَاضِي كُلَّمَا أَقَرَّ فَيَذْهَبُ حَيْثُ لَا يَرَاهُ ثُمَّ يَجِيءُ فَيُقِرُّ هُوَ الْمَرْوِيُّ عَنْ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ لِأَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ طَرَدَ مَاعِزًا فِي كُلِّ مَرَّةٍ حَتَّى تَوَارَى بِحِيطَانِ الْمَدِينَةِ
Repetition of confession does not add to its apparentness, unlike increase in the number of witnesses. Our evidence is the hadith of Ma'iz, for the Prophet (peace be upon him) delayed the enforcement until his confession was complete four times in four sittings. If it had been established with less than that, he would not have delayed it due to the establishment of obligation. And because testimony in this matter is specific to an increase in number, so too is confession, to magnify the matter of zina and to achieve the meaning of concealment. And different sittings are necessary due to what we have narrated, and because one sitting has an effect on all separate matters; in that case there would be a doubt of unity in the confession. The confession is attached to the confessor, so the difference in his sitting is considered, not the sitting of the judge. The difference is that the judge rejects him every time he confesses, so he goes where he cannot see him, then comes and confesses. This is what is narrated from Abu Hanifa, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) repelled Ma'iz every time until he hid behind the walls of Madinah.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute about the number of confessions needed to establish the hadd for zina. The matn (al-Quduri) states the condition of four confessions in four different sittings. The commentator (Ashraf al-Hadaya) explains the reasoning. The Hanafi position is that four confessions are required, analogously to four witnesses in testimony. Imam al-Shafi'i holds that one confession suffices, as in other rights. The Hanafi dalil is the hadith of Ma'iz, where the Prophet delayed the punishment until Ma'iz confessed four times in four separate sittings. The commentary also explains that different sittings are necessary to avoid doubt of unity; the confessor must be rejected by the judge each time and then return from a place where the judge does not see him. This is based on the practice of the Prophet with Ma'iz. The authority weight is from the Zahir al-Riwayah, as it is the relied-upon position of the madhhab.

Key Terms
إقرار (iqrar): A confession by an adult sane person that he committed zina, requiring repetition four times in four sittings to establish the hadd.
مجلس (majlis): A separate sitting in which the confessor appears before the judge and confesses; the judge must reject him each time, and he must leave and return from a place hidden from the judge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view, what is required for a confession of zina to establish the hadd?
A) One confession in one sitting
B) Four confessions in one sitting
C) Four confessions in four separate sittings
D) Two confessions in two separate sittings

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi requirement of four confessions in four separate sittings for zina reflects the school's commitment to caution, concealment, and avoiding hasty punishment.

The Judge's Investigation After Four Confessions of Zina
Procedural steps for accepting a zina confession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four required questions the judge must ask after four confessions of zina and explain why the time is not asked.

Core Idea
A confession alone does not trigger the hadd—details are needed to complete the evidence.

This passage from al-Quduri outlines the procedure a judge must follow after a person confesses to zina four times. It emphasizes that the mere repetition of confession is not enough; the judge must investigate the details to ensure the act legally constitutes zina. This safeguard prevents hasty punishment and upholds the principle of removing doubts in hudud.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the trigger
Identify that the judge's duty arises only after the confessor has completed four separate confessions of zina. The number four is significant for establishing certainty.
Four confessions are analogous to four witnesses in zina testimony.
2
Identify the four questions
List the four specifics the judge must ask: what is zina (definition), how it was done (manner), where it occurred (location), and with whom (partner).
These questions aim to ensure the act matches the legal definition of zina.
3
Connect to completeness of proof
Understand that the hadd becomes binding only after the confessor explains these details. This is because the evidence (hujjah) is then complete: the confession plus the detailed description remove any doubt.
The phrase 'li tamam al-hujjah' is key.
4
Note the omission of time
Observe that the judge does not ask about the time of the zina. This is because lapse of time (taqadum al-'ahd) does not invalidate a confession—unlike testimony, where delay might create suspicion.
Confession is an admission against oneself, so it is accepted even after a long time.
5
Consider the optional question about time
Note that it is permissible for the judge to ask about time, to rule out the possibility that the act occurred during the confessor's childhood, which would preclude the hadd.
This is an extra precaution mentioned in the text as 'qila'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ فَإِذَا أَتَمَّ إِقْرَارُهُ أَرْبَعَ مَرَّاتٍ سَأَلَهُ عَنِ الزِّنَاءِ مَا هُوَ وَكَيْفَ هُوَ وَأَيْنَ زَنَى وَبِمَنْ زَنَى فَإِذَا بَيَّنَ ذَلِكَ لَزِمَهُ الْحَدُّ لِتَمَامِ الْحُجَّةِ وَمَعْنَى السُّؤَالِ عَنْ هَذِهِ الْأَشْيَاءِ بَيَّنَّاهُ فِي الشَّهَادَةِ وَلَمْ يَذْكُرِ السُّؤَالَ فِيهِ عَنِ الزَّمَانِ وَذَكَرَهُ فِي الشَّهَادَةِ لِأَنَّ تَقَادُمَ الْعَهْدِ يَمْنَعُ الشَّهَادَةَ دُونَ الْإِقْرَارِ وَقِيلَ لَوْ سَأَلَهُ جَازَ لِجَوَازِ أَنَّهُ فِي صِبَاهُ
He said: When he completes his confession four times, he (the judge) asks him about the zina: what it is, how it is, where he committed zina, and with whom he committed zina. When he explains that, the hadd becomes binding upon him due to the completeness of the proof. The meaning of the question about these things we have explained in the section on testimony. And he did not mention asking about the time here, while he mentioned it in testimony, because lapse of time prevents testimony but not confession. And it is said that if he asks him, it is permissible, because it is possible that it was in his childhood.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_statement from al-Quduri, explaining the procedure after a confessor completes four confessions of zina. The judge must investigate the details of the act: what zina is, how it is performed, the location, and the identity of the partner. Only when the confessor provides a clear explanation does the hadd become binding, because the evidence (hujjah) is then complete. This investigation mirrors what is done with witnesses in zina cases. Notably, the judge does not ask about the time (zaman) of the act, because unlike testimony, a delayed confession is still accepted; lapse of time does not invalidate the confession. However, it is permissible to ask about time to rule out the possibility that the act occurred during the confessor's childhood (when the hadd would not apply). The authority weight is from the Zahir al-Riwayah as it is part of the standard matn.

Key Terms
حجة (hujjah): The legal evidence or proof sufficient to establish the hadd; here, the four confessions combined with the detailed explanation.
تقادم العهد (taqadum al-'ahd): Lapse of time between the act and the confession/testimony. It prevents testimony from being accepted but not confession.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the judge not ask about the time (zaman) of the zina when taking the confession?
A) Because time is irrelevant to zina
B) Because lapse of time does not prevent acceptance of confession
C) Because the confessor may not remember the time
D) Because it is already mentioned in the testimony

Key Takeaway
The judge must investigate the specifics of the zina after four confessions to complete the evidence; omitting time is allowed because confession is not weakened by delay.

Hudud — Fixed Penalties

Investigation of Zina after Four Confessions
Hadith proofs and ruling on questioning the confessor after four confessions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi procedure for investigating a confession of zina after four confessions and explain the evidential basis from the Prophet's practice.

Core Idea
After four confessions, the judge must investigate the details of the zina before imposing the hadd, as taught by the Prophet.

Confession of zina is a serious matter that can lead to the hadd penalty. The Hanafi school, following the example of the Prophet ﷺ, requires not only four separate confessions but also a detailed inquiry into the nature, manner, place, and partner of the act. This lesson examines the textual evidence from the hadith of Ma'iz and the Ghamidiyyah woman, and explains the ruling derived from them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act being ruled is the imposition of the hadd penalty for zina after a confession. The ruling is that the hadd becomes binding (wajib) only after four confessions and a clear description by the confessor.
The hadd is not imposed immediately upon the first confession.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary dalil is the practice of the Prophet ﷺ in the cases of Ma'iz and the Ghamidiyyah woman, as recorded in multiple authentic hadith collections.
The narrations are from Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud, Nasa'i, Tirmidhi, etc.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet did not order stoning immediately after the first confession. He waited for four confessions and then asked specific questions about the act, the person involved, and the place. This demonstrates that such investigation is a required part of the process.
The questions serve to confirm the confession and eliminate any doubt (shubhah).
4
Identify the details required
Al-Quduri states that the judge must ask about: what zina is, how it was done, where it occurred, and with whom. These four elements are derived from the hadith.
Time is not mentioned as a required question, but some scholars permit it.
5
Compare with testimony on the issue of time
In the case of testimony, time is a required question because a long delay may affect the witnesses' memory. In confession, the confessor knows his own actions, so time is not essential.
This shows the difference in the two modes of proof.

اور روایت حضرت جابر بن سمرہ میں ہے کہ دو مرتبہ اقرار کیا۔ لیکن آپ نے رد کیا۔ پھر دو مرتبہ اقرار کیا یہاں تک کہ چار مرتبہ اقرار ہو گیا۔ تب حکم دیا۔ ابو داؤد و نسائی اور مسلم نے اس کی روایت کی ہے اور حضرت بریدہ رضی اللہ تعالی عنہ کی روایت میں چار بار اقرار چار دن میں ہے۔ اس کی روایت مسلم نے کی ہے اور حضرت صدیق رضی اللہ تعالی عنہ سے منقول حدیث میں ہے کہ چوتھی بار اقرار کے بعد آپ نے ان کو قید خانہ میں رکھ کر ان کا حال دریافت کیا۔ اسحاق اور ابن ابی شیبہ نے اس کی روایت کی ہے۔
اور حضرت غامد یہ رضی اللہ عنہا کے قصہ میں آیا ہے کہ انہوں نے خود پر زنا کا اقرار چار بار کیا ہے اور ہر بار رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم ان کا رد کرتے تھے ۔ تب انہوں نے عرض کیا کہ کیا آپ یہ چاہتے ہیں کہ مجھے واپس کر دیں۔ جیسا کہ آپ نے ماعز رضی اللہ عنہ کو پھیر دیا تھا۔ (رواہ مسلم) اور چار بار اقرار کے بعد آپ نے فرمایا کہ تم ابھی جاؤ یہاں تک کہ یہ بچہ پیدا ہو جائے۔ پھر جب بچہ پیدا ہو گیا تب پھر حاضر ہو کر انہوں نے مطلع کیا تب پھر رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا کہ تم پھر واپس جاؤ یہاں تک کہ اس کا دودھ چھڑا دو پھر جب دودھ بھی چھڑا دیا تب وہ حاضر ہوئیں۔ اس حال میں کہ ان کے ہاتھ میں وہ بچہ بھی تھا اور روٹی کا ٹکڑا بھی تھا جسے وہ بچہ کھارہا تھا۔ اس وقت یہ کہا کہ اب یہ بچہ روٹی کھانے لگا ہے۔ اس لئے میں اس کے دودھ پلانے سے فارغ ہوں۔ تب پھر آپ نے فرمایا کہ اس بچہ کی دیکھ بھال کون کرے گا اس لئے تم اتنے دن اور بھی ٹھہر جاؤ کہ یہ اپنے ہاتھ اور پاؤں والا ہو جائے (اپنی ضرورتیں خود پوری کرنے لگے ) اتنے میں ایک صحابی نے عرض کیا کہ رسول اللہ! میں اس کی پرورش کروں گا۔ تب آپ نے اس عورت کو رجم کرنے کا حکم دیا۔ اسی رجم کے درمیان خالد بن الولید رضی اللہ عنہ نے کچھ بر الفظ کہہ کر ان کو ایک پتھر مارا جس کی وجہ سے ان کے سر سے خون بہنے لگا۔ تب رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے خالد رضی اللہ عنہ کے اس برا کہنے پر انتہائی غصہ کی حالت میں فرمایا کہ اللہ کی قسم اس نے تو ایسی توبہ کی ہے کہ اہل مدینہ میں سے ستر آدمیوں کے درمیان تقسیم کر دی جائے تو سب کے لئے کافی ہو جائے۔ (رواہ الترمذی وغیرہ) اتمام اقرار کے بعد تفتیش زنا
قَالَ فَإِذَ أَتَمَّ إِقْرَارُهُ أَرْبَعَ مَرَّاتٍ سَأَلَهُ عَنِ الزِنَاءِ مَاهُوَ وَكَيْفَ هُوَ وَايْنَ زَنَى وَبِمَنْ زَنَى فَإِذَا بَيْنَ ذَالِكَ لَزِمَهُ الْحَدُّ لِتَمَامِ الْحُجَّةِ وَمَعْنَى السُّؤالِ عَنْ هَذِهِ الْأَشْيَاءِ بَيَّنَّاهُ فِي الشَّهَادَةِ وَلَمْ يَذْكُرِ السُّوَّالَ فِيهِ عَنِ الزَّمَانِ وَذَكَرَهُ فِي الشَّهَادَةِ لِاَنَّ تَقَادُمَ الْعَهْدِ يَمْنَعُ الشَّهَادَةَ دُونَ الْإِقْرَارِ وَقِيلَ لَوْسَالَهُ جَازَ لِجَوَاز أَنَّهُ فِي صَبَاهُ
ترجمہ قدوری نے کہا ہے کہ مجرم جب اپنا اقرار چار بار پورا کر لے تو قاضی اس سے زنا کے بارے میں یہ دریافت کرے کہ زنا کیا کام ہے اور کس طرح ہوتا ہے اور اس نے کہاں پر زنا کیا ہے اور کسی عورت کے ساتھ کیا ہے۔ پھر وہ جب ٹھیک ٹھیک بتا دے تب اس پر حد لازم ہو جائے گی ۔ کیونکہ حجت پوری ہوگئی۔ ان چیزوں کو دریافت کرنے کے معنی ہم نے گواہی کی صورت میں بیان کر دیئے ہیں۔ اس جگہ زمانہ کے بارے میں دریافت کرنے کا ذکر نہیں کیا ہے۔ حالانکہ گواہی کی صورت میں ذکر کیا ہے۔ اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ زنا کئے ہوئے اگر بہت دن گذر جائیں تو اس کی گواہی میں رکاوٹ پیدا ہو کر قابل قبول ہو جاتی ہے مگر اقرار کی صورت میں مانع نہیں ہوتی ہے اور بعض مشائخ نے کہا ہے کہ اگر قاضی زمانہ کے متعلق بھی دریافت کرے تو جائز ہوگا۔ کیونکہ شاید اس نے ایسے وقت میں زنا کیا ہو جبکہ وہ بالغ نہیں ہوا تھا۔
Chapter of Hudud. Ashraf al-Bidaya Sharh Urdu Hidaya Volume 6. [Hadith of Ma'iz:] He [Ma'iz] confessed four times. [The Prophet] said: 'Tell me, with which woman did you commit zina?' He said: 'I committed zina with such-and-such woman.' He said: 'Perhaps you only kissed her or embraced her?' He said: 'No, I explicitly confessed zina.' Then the Prophet said: 'Are you insane?' In another narration, he sent people to his family to inquire about his sanity. They said no. Then he asked: 'Is he muhsan (married)?' They said yes. Then he ordered his stoning. In Abu Huraira's narration: after he confessed four times against himself. (Bukhari and Muslim) Similarly in Jabir ibn Abdillah's hadith. In Jabir ibn Samurah's hadith: he confessed twice, but the Prophet rejected it. Then he confessed twice more until it became four times, then he ordered. (Abu Dawud, Nasa'i, Muslim) In Buraydah's narration: four confessions over four days. (Muslim) In Siddiq's narration: after the fourth confession, he imprisoned him and inquired about his condition. (Ishaq and Ibn Abi Shayba) And the story of the Ghamidiyyah woman: she confessed four times, and each time the Prophet turned her away. She said: 'Do you want to send me back as you sent Ma'iz?' (Muslim) After four confessions, he said: 'Go until the child is born.' After birth, she came again. He said: 'Go until you wean him.' When she weaned him, she came with the child eating a piece of bread. She said: 'The child now eats bread; I am finished with nursing.' He said: 'Who will take care of the child?' A Companion volunteered. Then he ordered her stoning. During the stoning, Khalid ibn al-Walid said something and threw a stone, causing blood to flow from her head. The Prophet became angry and said: 'By Allah, she has made such a repentance that if it were divided among seventy people of Madinah, it would suffice them.' (Tirmidhi etc.) Investigation after completion of confession. He (al-Quduri) said: When his confession is completed four times, the judge asks him about zina: what it is, how it is, where he committed it, and with whom. When he clearly explains that, the hadd becomes binding upon him because the proof is complete. The meaning of asking these things we explained in the section on testimony. He did not mention asking about time here, while he mentioned it in testimony because the passage of time prevents testimony but not confession. And it is said: if he asks him about time, it is permissible because it is possible that he did it during his minority. Translation: Al-Quduri said: When the criminal completes his confession four times, the judge should ask him about zina: what act is zina, how is it done, where did he commit it, and with which woman. Then when he tells precisely, the hadd becomes binding because the proof is complete. The meaning of asking these things we have explained in the case of testimony. Here he did not mention asking about time, while there he mentioned it. The reason is that if many days have passed since the zina, it becomes an obstacle in testimony, but in confession it is not an obstacle. And some mashayikh said: if the judge also asks about time, it is permissible, because perhaps he committed zina at a time when he was not yet an adult.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, presenting the Hanafi procedure for imposing the hadd penalty for zina after a confession. It begins with extensive hadith narrations about Ma'iz and the Ghamidiyyah woman, which serve as the primary evidence (dalil) for the ruling. These narrations show that the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not immediately implement the hadd after the first confession; rather, he required four separate confessions and then investigated details—asking about the nature of the act, the person involved, and the place. The author then presents the matn of al-Quduri, stating that after four confessions the judge must ask about the definition, manner, location, and partner of the zina. If the confessor clearly describes it, the hadd becomes binding (lazima). This investigation is necessary to eliminate any possibility of misunderstanding or false confession. The text also distinguishes between testimony and confession regarding the question of time: in testimony, time is critical because a long delay may indicate forgetfulness or collusion, so the time must be asked; but in confession, since the confessor knows his own actions, time is not essential, though some scholars permit asking about time to rule out the possibility that the act occurred during the confessor's minority. This illustrates the Hanafi principle that in hudud, doubts (shubuhat) are to be avoided—thus investigation aims to confirm the confession's authenticity before executing the penalty.

Key Terms
اقرار (iqrar): Confession made by an individual against himself, which can be used as proof for establishing a hadd punishment.
حد (hadd): A fixed punishment prescribed by Allah for specific crimes, such as zina (stoning or lashing).
زنا (zina): Unlawful sexual intercourse between a man and a woman who are not married to each other and where there is no shubhah (doubt of ownership or marriage).
شهادة (shahadah): Testimony given by witnesses in court, which for zina requires four male witnesses or equivalent.
شبهة (shubhah): A doubt or ambiguity that can prevent the application of the hadd penalty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Twice
C) Three times

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires four confessions and a detailed investigation to eliminate any doubt before imposing the hadd for zina.

Hudud — Fixed Penalties
intermediate
8 min
Ruling on Retraction of Confession before Hadd Execution
Inter-madhhab dispute on retraction of confession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school accepts retraction of confession of zina before hadd execution, and compare this with the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Retraction creates doubt (shubhah), and hudud are repelled by doubts.

This lesson examines the effect of a confessor retracting his confession of zina before the hadd is carried out. The Hanafi school holds that such retraction invalidates the penalty, while the Shafi'i school maintains that the obligation persists. Understanding the distinction between rights of Allah and rights of servants is key.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling of the Hanafi school: retraction is accepted, and the hadd is dropped.
Note that the text says 'his retraction is accepted and he is released.'
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Al-Shafi'i and Ibn Abi Layla argue that the hadd must still be enforced despite the retraction.
Their rationale: obligation is fixed by confession and cannot be undone by retraction.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
They analogize to cases where hadd is established by testimony (irrevocable) and to qisas and hadd al-qadhf (which involve personal rights).
The analogy asserts that once obligatory, punishment endures regardless of retraction.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi rebuttal distinguishes: in cases with a personal right (qisas, qadhf), the claimant can contradict the retraction, so it is not accepted. In pure rights of Allah (zina), no claimant exists, so retraction creates doubt (shubhah) and hadd is repelled.
This is based on the maxim 'al-hudud tudra'u bi al-shubuhat'.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: under Hanafi law, the confessor goes free; under Shafi'i, the hadd is executed.
This difference arises from how each school classifies the right involved.

اقرار سے رجوع کا حکم
فَإِنْ رَجَعَ الْمُقِرُّعَنْ إِقْرَارِهِ قَبْلَ إِقَامَةِ الْحَدِ اَوْفِي وَسَطِهِ قَبْلَ رُجُوعِهِ وَخُلِيَ سَبِيْلُهُ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ وَهُوَ قَوْلُ ابْنِ أَبِي لَيْلَى يُقِيمُ عَلَيْهِ الْحَدَّلَانَّهُ وَجَبَ الْحَدُّ بِاقْرَارِهِ فَلَا يَبْطُلُ بِرُجُوعِهِ وَإِنْكَارِهِ كَمَا إِذَا وَجَبَ بِالشَّهَادَةِ وَ صَارَ كَالْقِصَاصِ وَحَدِ الْقَدْفِ وَ لَنَا اَنَّ الرُّجُوعَ خَيْرٌ مُحْتَمَلَ لِلصِّدْقِ كَالْإِقْرَارِ وَ ليسَ أَحَدٌ يُكَذِّبُهُ فِيْهِ فَيَتَحَقَّقُ الشَّبْهَةُ فِى الْإِقْرَارِ بِخِلَافِ مَا فِيهِ حَقُّ الْعَبْدِ وَهُوَ الْقِصَاصُ وَحَدُ الْقَذْفِ لِوُجُودِ مَنْ يُكَذِّبُهُ وَلَا كَذَالِكَ مَا هُوَ خَالِصُ حَقَّ الشَّرع
ترجمہ اب اگر اقراری مجرم اپنے اقرار سے رجوع کرے۔ اس پر حد قائم کرنے سے پہلے یا اس کے درمیان تو اس کے رجوع کر لینے کو قبول کر لیا جائے اور اسے چھوڑ دیا جائے اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا ہے۔ ابن ابی لیلی نے بھی یہی فرمایا ہے کہ قاضی اس پر بھی پوری حد جاری کر دے۔ کیونکہ اس کے اقرار سے اس پر حد واجب ہوگئی ہے۔ اس لئے اب اس کے پھر جانے اور اس کے انکار کر دینے کی وجہ سے حدختم نہیں کی جائے گی۔ جیسے کہ اگر دوسرے گواہوں سے زنا ثابت ہو کر حد واجب ہوتی تو اس زانی کے انکار سے وہ ختم نہیں ہوتی اور یہ زنا کی حد قصاص اور حد قذف کے مثل ہوگئی یعنی ان دونوں سے بھی اقرار کے بعد پھر جانے اور انکار کرنے سے حدختم نہیں ہوتی ہے اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ اقرار سے پھر جانا ایک ایسی خبر ہے جس میں سچ ہونے کا بھی احتمال ہے۔ جیسے اقرار بھی ایک خبر ہے (جس میں صدق کا احتمال ہے) جیسے اقرار تھا۔ اس اقرار سے پھر جانے کی صورت میں اسے دوسرا کوئی بھی جھٹلانے والا نہیں ہے۔ یعنی اس کے خلاف کہنے والا یا التزام ثابت کرنے والا نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے اس کے اقرار میں شبہہ پیدا ہو گیا۔ ( اور ہمیں تو اس بات کا حکم دیا گیا ہے کہ ہم شبہ ہونے کی صورت میں حد کو دور کر دیں یعنی جاری نہ کریں) بخلاف قصاص کے جس میں بندہ کا حق متعلق ہوتا ہے اور بخلاف حد قذف کے کہ اس میں بھی بندہ کا حق متعلق ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے پھر جانے یا مکر جانے سے باطل نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس کا جھٹلانے والا مدعی موجود ہوتا ہے۔ اور یہ حال ایسے حدود کا نہیں ہے جو خالص حق شرع ہیں جیسے حدز نا وغیرہ۔
Ruling on retraction of confession. If the confessor retracts his confession before implementation of the hadd or in the middle of it, his retraction is accepted and he is released. Al-Shafi'i said – and this is also the opinion of Ibn Abi Layla – that the hadd should be enforced upon him because the hadd became obligatory by his confession, so it is not invalidated by his retraction and denial, just as when it becomes obligatory by testimony, and it becomes like qisas and hadd of qadhf. Our evidence is that retraction is a statement that may be truthful just like the confession, and there is no one to contradict him in it, so a doubt arises in the confession, unlike cases where a right of a servant is involved, namely qisas and hadd of qadhf, because there is someone to contradict him, and unlike what is purely the right of Allah, like the hadd of zina. [Urdu translation follows.]
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the effect of retracting a confession of zina before the hadd is fully executed. The Hanafi position, based on the principle of shubhah (doubt), holds that retraction creates a doubt because the confessor's new statement could be true, and no one is there to refute him. Therefore, the hadd is dropped. The Shafi'i school and Ibn Abi Layla argue that once the hadd becomes obligatory through confession, it is not nullified by retraction, analogizing it to hadd established by testimony, qisas, and hadd of qadhf. The Hanafi response distinguishes: in cases involving the rights of Allah (huquq Allah), doubt prevents punishment, but in cases involving the rights of servants (huquq al-'ibad), such as qisas and qadhf, retraction does not cancel the penalty because the claimant (the victim or his heirs) can contradict the retraction. Since zina hadd is a pure right of Allah, the presence of doubt (shubhah) necessitates its suspension. This reflects the Hanafi maxim 'al-hudud tudra'u bi al-shubuhat' (fixed penalties are repelled by doubts).

Key Terms
رجوع (ruju'): Retraction or withdrawal of a previous confession.
حد قذف (hadd al-qadhf): Fixed punishment for false accusation of zina (usually 80 lashes).
قصاص (qisas): Retaliatory punishment for homicide or bodily harm.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what happens if a confessor retracts his confession of zina before the hadd is implemented?
A) The hadd is still applied
B) The hadd is dropped and he is released
C) He is imprisoned until further investigation
D) He is given a lighter punishment

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, retraction of confession of zina before hadd execution creates a doubt (shubhah) that repels the punishment, because it is a pure right of Allah.

Imam Suggesting Retraction to the Confessor
Recommendation for the imam to encourage retraction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the imam prompting retraction and identify its basis in the Prophet's practice.

Core Idea
The imam should encourage retraction to avoid hudud; it is mustahabb, not wajib.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a key principle in Hanafi hudud law: the imam's role is not to seek punishment but to exhaust possibilities for the confessor to retract. The ruling is derived from the Prophet's own words to Ma'iz ibn Malik, demonstrating that even the Prophet suggested excuses rather than immediately enforcing the hadd.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its level
Locate the phrase 'yustahabb' and note that the imam's action is recommended (mustahabb/sunnah ghayr muakkadah), not obligatory. This sets the legal weight.
The ruling is for the imam or judge, not the confessor.
2
Find the dalil (proof)
The text cites the Prophet's statement to Ma'iz: 'Perhaps you only touched her or kissed her.' Recognize this as a Sunnah ahad proof. Note how the Prophet himself prompted an excuse.
The hadith is authentic (Bukhari/Muslim) but zanni in transmission for fiqh derivation.
3
Examine the alternative wording from Imam Muhammad
Imam Muhammad in al-Asl suggests an alternative: 'Perhaps you married her or had intercourse under a shubhah.' Understand that both wordings serve the same purpose: offering a legal loophole for retraction.
The author notes this is close in meaning, indicating no substantive disagreement.
4
Grasp the underlying principle
The Prophet's action and the imam's recommendation reflect the Hanafi principle of 'avoiding hudud when in doubt' (idra al-hudud bi al-shubuhat). The imam should actively seek to avert the hadd by suggesting plausible excuses.
This principle is broader than just zina; it applies to all hudud.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
امام کیلئے رجوع کی تلقین کا حکم
وَيُسْتَحَبُّ لِلْإِمَامِ أَنْ يُلَقَّنَ الْمُقِرَّ الرُّجُوعَ فَيَقُولُ لَهُ لَعَلَّكَ لَمَسْتَ اَوْ قَبَّلْتَ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لِمَاعِزُّ لَعَلَّكَ لَمَسْتَهَا أَوْقَبَّلْتَهَا وَقَالَ فِي الْأَصْلِ وَيَنْبَغِي أَنْ يَقُولَ لَهُ الْإِمَامُ لَعَلَّكَ تَزَوَّجْتَهَا أَوْ وَطَيْتَهَا بِشُبُهَةٍ وَهَذَا قَرِيبٌ مِنَ الْأَوَّلِ فِي الْمَعْنَى
ترجمہ اور قاضی و امام کے لئے مستحب یہ ہے کہ اقراری مجرم کے سامنے ایسی باتیں کرے جن سے وہ اپنے اقرار سے پھر جائے۔ مثلا یوں کہے کہ تم نے تو اسے صرف ہاتھ لگایا ہوگا یا اس کا صرف بوسہ لیا ہوگا اور امام محمد نے مبسوط میں کہا ہے کہ امام کو یوں کہنا چاہئے کہ شاید تم نے اس سے نکاح کر لیا یا شبہ میں اس سے وطی کی ہے اور یہ بات بھی معنی کے اعتبار سے پہلی بات کے قریب ہے۔
تشريح وَهَذَا قَرِيبٌ مِنَ الْأَوَّلِ فِي الْمَعْنى الخ۔ مبسوط میں امام محمد کا قول معنی کے اعتبار سے پہلی بات کے قریب تر ہے۔
Ruling on the imam suggesting retraction. It is mustahabb for the imam to prompt the confessor to retract, saying to him: 'Perhaps you only touched her or kissed her' because of the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him) to Ma'iz: 'Perhaps you only touched her or kissed her.' And he said in al-Asl: The imam should say to him: 'Perhaps you married her or had intercourse with her under a shubhah.' And this is close to the first in meaning. Translation: It is mustahabb for the judge and imam to say things that might make the confessor retract his confession, e.g., 'You only touched her or kissed her.' And Imam Muhammad said in al-Mabsut: The imam should say: 'Perhaps you married her or had intercourse with her under a shubhah.' This is close to the first in meaning. Explanation: 'And this is close to the first in meaning' etc. Imam Muhammad's statement in al-Mabsut is closer in meaning to the first.
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on a recommended (mustahabb) action for the imam or judge. It instructs the imam to try to encourage the confessor to retract his confession by suggesting possible legal excuses, such as that what he did was only touching or kissing, or that he had a marriage or a shubhah (doubtful intercourse). This is based on the Prophet's own practice with Ma'iz ibn Malik, where he said, 'Perhaps you only touched her or kissed her.' The text also notes that Imam Muhammad in his book al-Asl (or al-Mabsut) suggests an alternative phrasing, referring to marriage or shubhah, which is similar in meaning. This practice reflects the Hanafi principle of avoiding hudud when possible, as the hadd is a severe punishment and any way to avoid it through a legitimate doubt is pursued. The imam should not zealously enforce the penalty but rather exhaust all possibilities to find an excuse for the confessor.

Key Terms
مستحب (mustahabb): A recommended action that is encouraged but not obligatory; omission does not incur sin.
تلقين (talqin): The act of prompting or suggesting something to another person; here, the imam suggesting an excuse to the confessor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the hukm (ruling) for the imam to prompt a confessor to retract by suggesting possible excuses?
A) Wajib (obligatory)
B) Mustahabb (recommended)
C) Mubah (permissible)
D) Makruh (disliked)

Key Takeaway
It is mustahabb for the imam to prompt retraction by suggesting a lesser act or a legal doubt, following the Prophet's sunnah and the Hanafi principle of avoiding hudud.

Retraction of Confession Before Hadd: Hanafi Position and Inter-Madhhab Dispute
Hanafi ruling on retraction before hadd with dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on retraction of confession before hadd, explain the Hanafi distinction between pure Shari'a rights and individual rights, and evaluate the opposing Shafi'i argument.

Core Idea
Retraction of confession creates doubt, and hadd is averted by doubts in pure Shari'a rights.

In Hanafi penal law, the role of doubt (shubha) is central to averting prescribed punishments (hudud). This lesson examines a key dispute: if someone confesses to zina but then retracts before the hadd is carried out, does the punishment still apply? The Hanafi school holds that retraction is accepted and the person is released, while the Shafi'i school insists the hadd must be executed. Understanding the reasoning behind each position is essential for grasping the Hanafi usul al-fiqh principle that hudud are suspended by doubts.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Begin by identifying the ruling in the text: if the confessor retracts before or during hadd execution, he is released. Note that this applies specifically to pure Shari'a rights (like zina) where no individual claimant exists.
2
Identify the opposing school and their proof
The text cites al-Shafi'i and Ibn Abi Layla. Their proof: hadd becomes obligatory by confession, so retraction does not nullify it, analogous to hadd established by testimony and to qisas and qadhf.
Note the analogies (qiyas) they use.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response distinguishes between cases. Retraction is a statement possibly true; since no one contradicts it, doubt (shubha) arises. Hadd is averted by doubt. This differs from qisas and qadhf where there is a plaintiff who can contradict the retraction.
Key concept: shubha averts hadd.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: a Hanafi judge releases the confessor; a Shafi'i judge carries out the hadd. This shows how the legal ruling directly affects the outcome.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ رَجَعَ الْمُقِرُّ عَنْ إِقْرَارِهِ قَبْلَ إِقَامَةِ الْحَدِّ أَوْ فِي وَسَطِهِ قَبْلَ رُجُوعِهِ وَخُلِّيَ سَبِيلُهُ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ وَهُوَ قَوْلُ ابْنِ أَبِي لَيْلَى يُقِيمُ عَلَيْهِ الْحَدَّ لَأَنَّهُ وَجَبَ الْحَدُّ بِإِقْرَارِهِ فَلَا يَبْطُلُ بِرُجُوعِهِ وَإِنْكَارِهِ كَمَا إِذَا وَجَبَ بِالشَّهَادَةِ وَصَارَ كَالْقِصَاصِ وَحَدِّ الْقَذْفِ وَلَنَا أَنَّ الرُّجُوعَ خَيْرٌ مُحْتَمَلٌ لِلصِّدْقِ كَالْإِقْرَارِ وَلَيْسَ أَحَدٌ يُكَذِّبُهُ فِيهِ فَيَتَحَقَّقُ الشَّبْهَةُ فِي الْإِقْرَارِ بِخِلَافِ مَا فِيهِ حَقُّ الْعَبْدِ وَهُوَ الْقِصَاصُ وَحَدُّ الْقَذْفِ لِوُجُودِ مَنْ يُكَذِّبُهُ وَلَا كَذَلِكَ مَا هُوَ خَالِصُ حَقِّ الشَّرْعِ
If the confessor retracts his confession before the establishment of hadd or during it, he is released. Al-Shafi'i said, and it is also the saying of Ibn Abi Layla: the hadd is carried out on him because hadd became obligatory by his confession, so it is not invalidated by his retraction and denial, just as when it becomes obligatory by testimony, and it becomes like qisas and the hadd of qadhf. Our evidence is that retraction is a news that is possibly true, like confession, and no one accuses him of lying in it, so doubt arises in the confession, unlike cases involving the right of a slave, which are qisas and the hadd of qadhf, because there is someone who accuses him of lying, and unlike that which is purely the right of Shari'a.
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute on the effect of retracting a confession to a hadd crime (specifically zina) before or during the execution of the punishment. The Hanafi position is that the retraction is accepted and the hadd is dropped. The passage first states the Hanafi ruling: if the confessor retracts before the hadd is established or during its execution, he is released. Then it presents the view of al-Shafi'i and Ibn Abi Layla, who hold that the hadd must still be carried out. Their reasoning is that the hadd became obligatory by the confession, and retraction does not nullify it, analogous to a hadd established by testimony (where retraction of witnesses after sentencing does not nullify) and analogous to qisas and the hadd of qadhf, where retraction after confession does not prevent execution. The Hanafi response follows: retraction is a statement that could be true (like the initial confession), and since no one contradicts him (no other claimant), doubt (shubha) arises in the confession. Hadd is to be averted by doubts. This is unlike qisas and the hadd of qadhf, where there is a plaintiff who can contradict the retraction, so the right of the slave (individual) prevents the retraction from being effective. For pure Shari'a rights (like hadd for zina), retraction is accepted because there is no opposing claimant.

Key Terms
المقر (al-muqirr): The person who confesses to a crime (specifically zina here).
الشبهة (al-shubhah): A doubt or ambiguity that prevents the application of hadd. In Hanafi usul, hadd is averted by shubhat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is retraction of confession accepted for zina but not for qisas?
A) Because zina is a lesser crime
B) Because in qisas there is a living claimant who can contradict the retraction
C) Because retraction is not allowed in any hadd
D) Because zina requires four witnesses

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accepts retraction of confession before or during hadd for pure Shari'a rights because it creates doubt, and hudud are averted by doubts.

The Imam's Role in Encouraging Retraction of Confession
Ruling with proof, expansion from al-Asl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that it is mustahabb for the imam to suggest excuses to a confessor of zina to encourage retraction, and explain the proof from the hadith of Ma'iz.

Core Idea
The imam should suggest excuses to avert the hadd, following the Prophet's example.

In Hanafi hudud, the imam is not merely a passive recipient of confessions. He is encouraged to actively probe for doubts to avert punishment. This passage teaches the specific method: the imam should suggest possible alternatives to full zina, such as touching or kissing, giving the confessor a dignified way to retract. This reflects the Hanafi principle that hudud are averted by doubts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The text explicitly states it is mustahabb (recommended) for the imam to prompt the confessor to retract.
This is not wajib; it is a commendable act.
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
The proof is the Prophet's statement to Ma'iz: 'Perhaps you only touched her or kissed her' (Sahih Muslim).
The wording 'perhaps' (la'alla) indicates a suggestion, not a command.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's words are a suggestion, demonstrating that the imam should likewise suggest possibilities that make the act less than full zina.
This shows the ruling is mustahabb, not obligatory.
4
Note the expansion from al-Asl
Imam Muhammad in al-Asl suggests that the imam say: 'Perhaps you married her or had intercourse under a shubha (doubt).' This provides a stronger excuse.
Both wordings serve the same purpose: to give the confessor an exit.
5
Extract the underlying principle
The principle is that hudud are averted by doubts (shubhat). The imam should actively seek doubts to prevent punishment.
This is a key Hanafi maxim: 'al-hudud tudra'u bi al-shubhat'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيُسْتَحَبُّ لِلْإِمَامِ أَنْ يُلَقِّنَ الْمُقِرَّ الرُّجُوعَ فَيَقُولَ لَهُ لَعَلَّكَ لَمَسْتَ أَوْ قَبَّلْتَ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لِمَاعِزٍ لَعَلَّكَ لَمَسْتَهَا أَوْ قَبَّلْتَهَا وَقَالَ فِي الْأَصْلِ وَيَنْبَغِي أَنْ يَقُولَ لَهُ الْإِمَامُ لَعَلَّكَ تَزَوَّجْتَهَا أَوْ وَطِئْتَهَا بِشُبْهَةٍ وَهَذَا قَرِيبٌ مِنَ الْأَوَّلِ فِي الْمَعْنَى
It is mustahabb for the imam to prompt the confessor to retract, saying to him: 'Perhaps you only touched her or kissed her,' because of his statement, peace be upon him, to Ma'iz: 'Perhaps you only touched her or kissed her.' And it is stated in al-Asl: the imam should say to him: 'Perhaps you married her or had intercourse with her under a shubha.' And this is close in meaning to the first.
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage states a recommended (mustahabb) action for the imam or judge when someone confesses to zina. The imam should try to find excuses for the confessor by suggesting possibilities that would make the act less than full zina, such as touching, kissing, marriage, or intercourse under a shubha (doubt). This is based on the practice of the Prophet ﷺ with Ma'iz, where he said, 'Perhaps you only touched her or kissed her,' giving Ma'iz an opportunity to retract. Imam Muhammad in al-Asl (a book of al-Mabsut) suggests even more specific wording: 'Perhaps you married her or had intercourse under a shubha.' Both suggestions serve the same purpose: to give the confessor a way out and avoid the hadd. This reflects the Hanafi principle that hadd should be avoided by doubts.

Key Terms
يلقن (yulaqqin): To prompt or suggest (the imam suggests a retraction).
مستحب (mustahabb): Recommended; an action that is rewardable but not obligatory.
لعل (la'alla): Perhaps; a word indicating possibility, used by the Prophet to suggest, not command.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling for the imam regarding suggesting retraction to a confessor of zina?
A) It is wajib
B) It is haram
C) It is mustahabb (recommended)
D) It is not allowed

Key Takeaway
The imam is encouraged to suggest excuses to a confessor of zina to retract, following the Prophet's sunnah, to avert the hadd punishment.

Stoning of the Muhsan: Ruling and Procedure with Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute
Ruling on stoning the muhsan with procedural dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of stoning for a muhsan zani, describe the prescribed procedure, and explain the Hanafi position on the witnesses initiating the stoning with its evidence.

Core Idea
Stoning is obligatory for the muhsan; witnesses must start the stoning as a condition.

This passage establishes the hadd of stoning for a muhsan (married, free, adult Muslim) who commits zina. It details the procedure: the condemned is taken to open ground and stoned, with the witnesses initiating the stoning, then the imam, then the people. A dispute with al-Shafi'i arises over whether witnesses must start; the Hanafi school considers it a condition based on a report from 'Ali and the wisdom of preventing retraction of testimony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon and the specific hukm (obligatory stoning for muhsan).
The ruling is fard (obligatory) for the state to execute.
2
Locate the dalil
Identify the proofs cited: the Prophet's stoning of Ma'iz (action), the hadith 'al-zina ba'da al-ihsan' (statement), and ijma of the Companions.
These provide the basis for stoning as hadd.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how each dalil proves the ruling: the action is a precedent, the hadith explicitly mentions zina after ihsan as a capital offense, and ijma confirms it.
The hadith is from the well-known 'blood of a Muslim' hadith.
4
Note the ikhtilaf on procedure
Identify the dispute: al-Shafi'i holds that witnesses are not required to start stoning; the Hanafi school requires it as a condition.
The opponent uses qiyas with lashing.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Analyze the Hanafi response: analogy fails because lashing requires skill, and untrained persons might kill undeservedly; witnesses starting is a precaution.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا وَجَبَ الْحَدُّ وَكَانَ الزَّانِي مُحْصَنًا رُجِمَ بِالْحِجَارَةِ حَتَّى يَمُوتَ لِأَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ رَجَمَ مَاعِزًا وَقَدْ أُحْصِنَ وَقَالَ فِي الْحَدِيثِ الْمَعْرُوفِ وَالزِّنَا بَعْدَ الْإِحْصَانِ وَعَلَى هَذَا إِجْمَاعُ الصَّحَابَةِ قَالَ وَيُخْرِجُهُ إِلَى أَرْضِ فَضَاءٍ وَيَبْدَأُ الشُّهُودُ بِرَجْمِهِ ثُمَّ الْإِمَامُ ثُمَّ النَّاسُ كَذَا رُوِيَ عَنْ عَلِيٍّ وَلِأَنَّ الشَّاهِدَ قَدْ يَتَحَاسَرُ عَلَى الْأَدَاءِ ثُمَّ يَسْتَعْظِمُ الْمُبَاشَرَةَ فَيَرْجِعُ فَكَانَ فِي بِدَايَتِهِ احْتِيَاطٌ لِلسَّوْءِ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ لَا يُشْتَرَطُ بِدَايَتُهُ اعْتِبَارًا بِالْجَلْدِ قُلْنَا كُلُّ أَحَدٍ لَا يُحْسِنُ الْجَلْدَ فَرُبَّمَا يَقَعُ مُهْلِكًا وَالْإِهْلَاكُ غَيْرُ مُسْتَحِقٍّ وَلَا كَذَلِكَ
When hadd becomes obligatory and the fornicator is muhsan, he is stoned with stones until death, because the Prophet, peace be upon him, stoned Ma'iz and he was muhsan, and he said in the well-known hadith: 'and zina after ihsan', and upon this is the consensus of the Companions. He said: He is taken out to an open land, and the witnesses begin stoning him, then the imam, then the people. Thus it is reported from 'Ali, and because the witness may be hesitant to testify then later feels the gravity of directly stoning and retracts, so having them start is a precaution against evil. Al-Shafi'i said: their starting is not a condition, by analogy with lashing. We say: Not everyone is skilled at lashing, so it might accidentally kill, and killing is not deserved, and not so.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage covers two related topics: the ruling that a muhsan (married, free, adult, Muslim) zani is to be stoned to death, and the procedure for carrying out stoning. The ruling is supported by the Prophet's action with Ma'iz, a well-known hadith stating 'zina after ihsan' (from the hadith about the blood of a Muslim being lawful in three cases), and the consensus of the Companions. The procedure: the condemned is taken to an open ground. The stoning begins with the witnesses who testified (or the confessor? The text says al-shuhuud), then the imam, then the general public. This is reported from 'Ali. The wisdom: the witness might hesitate to testify but then feel the gravity of directly participating in the execution, so requiring them to start ensures they do not retract their testimony (tahassur and then 'taking it big' leading to retraction). This is a precaution against the evil of false testimony. Al-Shafi'i disagrees, saying that having witnesses start is not a condition, analogizing to lashing where witnesses do not start. The Hanafi response: not everyone is skilled at lashing, so if an untrained person lashes, they might accidentally kill, and such killing is not deserved. The argument seems incomplete, but the core idea is that witnesses starting stoning is a precaution specific to rajm.

Key Terms
محصن (muhsan): A free, adult, Muslim who has previously had valid sexual intercourse within marriage (married and consummated). Also includes being free from previous hadd for false accusation? Standard definition: free, adult, Muslim, married, and consummated.
رجم (rajm): Execution by stoning with stones until death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Stoning the muhsan is obligatory with witnesses initiating the stoning as a condition (Hanafi), and the dispute with Shafi'i is resolved by distinguishing stoning from lashing.

Stoning the Muhsan Adulterer: Proof from Sunnah and Ijma
Establishes the ruling of stoning for muhsan zina with dalil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three proofs (Sunnah, hadith, ijma) for the ruling of stoning a muhsan adulterer and explain why each is binding in Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
Stoning the muhsan is proven by the Prophet's action, his words, and unanimous Companions' consensus.

The punishment for a married (muhsan) adulterer is stoning to death, a ruling firmly established in the Hanafi madhhab. This lesson unpacks the textual and consensus-based proofs that make this punishment binding. You will see how the Sunnah of the Prophet ﷺ and the collective agreement of the Sahaba form an unbroken chain of authority.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The passage states that when the hadd is due and the offender is muhsan, he is stoned with stones until death.
2
Locate the first dalil: Fi'l of the Prophet
The Prophet ﷺ stoned Ma'iz, who was muhsan. This action (fi'l) is a binding proof in Hanafi usul.
The action of a prophet indicates obligation when done in a legislative context.
3
Locate the second dalil: Qawl of the Prophet
The famous hadith includes 'zina after ihsan' as a capital offense. This is a direct statement (qawl) from the Prophet.
The hadith is referenced as 'the well-known hadith' (al-hadith al-ma'ruf).
4
Locate the third dalil: Ijma of the Companions
The Companions unanimously agreed on stoning the muhsan. This ijma is a binding source of law.
Ijma al-Sahabah is considered a proof in Hanafi fiqh.
5
Recognize the Hanafi acceptance
All three proofs are accepted in the Hanafi school. The ruling is mufta bihi and there is no intra-madhhab disagreement on this point.
The authority weight is zahir al-riwayah and cross-madhhab status is muttafaq alayh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا وَجَبَ الْحَدُّ وَكَانَ الزَّانِي مُحْصَارَ جَمَهُ[؟] بِالْحِجَارَةِ حَتَّى يَمُوتُ لِاَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ رَجَمَ مَاعِزًا وَقَدْ أخصِنَ[؟] وَقَالَ فِى الْحَدِيثِ الْمَعْرُوفِ وَزِنَا بَعْدَ الإِحْصَانِ وَعَلَى هَذَا إِجْمَاعُ الصَّحَابَةِ
And when the hadd becomes obligatory and the adulterer is muhsan, he is stoned with stones until he dies, because the Prophet ﷺ stoned Ma'iz while he was muhsan, and he said in the well-known hadith: 'And zina after ihsan', and upon this is the consensus of the Companions.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof for the hadd of rajm on a muhsan adulterer. The author states the ruling: when the hadd is wajib and the offender is muhsan, the punishment is stoning to death. The proof is threefold: first, the action of the Prophet ﷺ who stoned Ma'iz ibn Malik (radiAllahu anhu) when he confessed to adultery and was muhsan. Second, the famous hadith that counts 'zina after ihsan' as one of the three capital offenses. Third, the consensus (ijma) of the Companions on this ruling. The Urdu commentary explains the conditions of zina that necessitate hadd: penetration of the glans of a sane adult male into the vagina of a woman not his property, who is capable of desire, in Dar al-Islam, etc. It also notes exceptions like the blind person's stoning if he confesses, but not if he is mute.

Key Terms
محصن (muḥṣan): A person who is free, adult, Muslim, and has had valid sexual intercourse in a valid marriage (both parties must be free and Muslim).
رجم (rajm): Stoning to death as a legal punishment for muhsan zina.

Procedure of Stoning: Witnesses Begin, then Imam, then People
Inter-madhhab dispute on the order of stoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi order of stoning and defend it against the Shafi'i analogy using the rationale of precaution against false testimony.

Core Idea
Witnesses begin stoning — a precaution to allow retraction and avert wrongful execution.

The execution of rajm (stoning) is a severe hadd punishment. The Hanafi school prescribes a specific order: the witnesses who testified begin the stoning, then the imam, then the people. This procedure is not merely ceremonial; it serves a critical legal purpose: providing an opportunity for witnesses to retract, thereby preventing a possible miscarriage of justice. Imam al-Shafi'i disagreed, drawing an analogy from flogging. This lesson walks through the Hanafi position and its rebuttal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi Procedure
State the three parties in order: witnesses first, then the imam (or his deputy), then the general public.
The passage explicitly says: 'the witnesses begin stoning him, then the imam, then the people.'
2
Understand the Rationale
Why do Hanafis require witnesses to start? The text gives two reasons: a narration from Ali (karamallahu wajhah) and the wisdom that witnesses may become hesitant and retract, thus preventing a potential error.
The term 'ihtiyal' (stratagem) indicates a deliberate legal precaution.
3
Contrast with the Shafi'i Position
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the witnesses' beginning is not a condition (shart), drawing an analogy (qiyas) from flogging (jald), where witnesses do not begin.
The opposing school's dalil is qiyas, which is valid in usul al-fiqh.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi Rebuttal
The Hanafi response distinguishes flogging from stoning: anyone can flog, but improper flogging can accidentally kill, whereas stoning is intended to kill ('it is absolute'). Therefore, the precaution of witnesses starting is specific to stoning.
The rebuttal uses a distinction (farq) to block the qiyas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَ يُخْرِجُهُ إِلَى أَرْضِ فَضَاءٍ وَيَبْتَدِى الشُّهُودُ بِرَجْمِهِ ثُمَّ الْاِمَامُ ثُمَّ النَّاسُ كَذَارُوِيَ عَنْ عَلِيٌّ وَلَانَّ الشَّاهِدَ قَدْيَتَحَا سَرُ[؟] عَلَى الْآدَاءِ ثُمَّ يَسْتَعْظِمُ الْمُبَاشَرَةَ فَيَرْجِعُ فَكَانَ فِي بِدَايَتِهِ اِحْتِيَالْ لِلسَّوْءِ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِي لَا يُشْتَرَطُ بِدَايَتُهُ اِعْتِبَارًا بِالْجَلْدِ قُلْنَا كُلُّ اَحَدٍ لَا يُحْسِنُ الْجَلْدَ فَرُبَمَا يَقَعُ مُهْلِكًا وَالْإِهْلَاكُ غَيْرُ مُسْتَحِقٍ وَلَا كَذَالِكَ الرَّجمُ لِأَنَّهُ اتلاق[؟]
He said: He takes him out to an open space, and the witnesses begin stoning him, then the imam, then the people, as is narrated from Ali, and because the witness may become hesitant to testify, then consider the act grave and retract, so beginning with them is a stratagem against evil. Al-Shafi'i said: His beginning is not a condition, by analogy with flogging. We said: Not everyone knows how to flog, so it may become fatal, and killing is not deserved, and it is not like that for stoning because it is absolute.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi procedure for stoning and a dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i. The text from al-Quduri states that when stoning is wajib, the imam takes the condemned to an open plain. The witnesses who testified against him begin the stoning, then the imam, then the rest of the people. This is based on a narration from 'Ali (karamallahu wajhah). The wisdom behind this order is that witnesses may have testified falsely or become remorseful; by making them start, it provides an opportunity for them to retract before the punishment is fully carried out, thus averting a potential error. Imam al-Shafi'i argues that this order is not a necessary condition, drawing analogy from flogging (jald) where the witnesses do not have to begin. The Hanafi response is that flogging is not analogous: anyone can flog, but flogging done improperly can accidentally kill, whereas stoning is intended to kill (it is absolute). Therefore, the precaution of having witnesses start is specific to stoning.

Key Terms
شاهد (shāhid): A witness who testified against the accused before the judge; in this context, the witnesses to the act of zina who establish the hadd.
إمام (imām): The head of state or his deputy (the qadi) who executes the hadd punishment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do Hanafis require the witnesses to begin stoning before the imam and the people?
A) To give the witnesses honor
B) To allow the witnesses an opportunity to retract their testimony
C) Because the imam is too important to start
D) Because stoning is a collective punishment

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi order of stoning is a deliberate precaution rooted in a narration from Ali and the risk of false testimony, distinguishing it from the Shafi'i analogy with flogging.
