Punishment of Slaves and Lashing of Women in Zina
Rulings on slave punishment and woman's lashing procedure

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the punishment for male and female slaves convicted of zina, explain the evidence from Quran 4:25, and describe the procedure for lashing a woman.

Core Idea
Slaves receive 50 lashes for zina; women are lashed seated with only thick garments removed.

In this passage from Kitab al-Hudud, we learn how Islamic law adjusts hadd punishments based on legal capacity and modesty. The ruling for slaves is derived from the Quran, while the procedure for women is based on the sunnah and the principle of concealment. This lesson unpacks both rulings and their proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is zina committed by a slave (male or female). The ruling is 50 lashes, half of the 100 lashes for a free person.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary evidence is Quran 4:25, which explicitly states that the punishment for slave women is half of that for free women.
The verse applies to both male and female slaves by analogy (qiyas).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The verse uses the word 'half' (نصف) to indicate a quantitative reduction. This is a clear, definitive proof that cannot be overridden.
The Hanafi school considers this a qat'i dalalah.
4
Note the exception for stoning
If a married slave were to be stoned, the punishment cannot be halved. Therefore, married slaves are lashed instead of stoned.
This demonstrates the principle that hadd punishments must be executable exactly as prescribed.
5
Examine the procedure for lashing a woman
A woman is seated, and only thick padded garments (e.g., fur coat) are removed; other clothes remain to preserve modesty. This is based on the practice of Ali (RA) and the principle of concealment.
For men, clothes are removed except for covering the private parts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحدود.
۱۴۴
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ششم
وَالسَّتْرُ حاصِل بِدُونِهِمَا فَيُنْزَ عَان وَتُضْرَبُ جَالِسَةٌ لِمَارَوَيْنَا وَلَأَنَّهُ أَسْتَرُلَهَا ترجمہ اور اگر زنا کرنے والا کوئی غلام (یا باندی۔ ع) ہو تو اسے پچاس کوڑے مارے جائیں کیونکہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ہے۔ فعليهن نصف ما على المحصنات من العذاب یعنی باندیوں پر جو حد کی سزا لازم ہوگی، وہ آدھی ہوگی اس سزا کی جو آزاد عورتوں پر لازم ہوتی ہے۔ یہ آیت باندیوں کے بارے میں نازل ہوئی ہے اور اس وجہ سے بھی کہ غلامی نعمت خداوندی کو آدھا کر دیتی ہے۔ اسی لئے اس کی سزا کو بھی آدھا کر دے گی کیونکہ جس شخص کو انعامات بہت ملتے ہوں اس کے باوجود وہ نافرمانی کرتا ہو تو اس کی سزا بھی زیادہ ہی ہوا کرتی ہے۔ اسی لئے آزاد کی سزا میں بھی سختی ہوتی ہے۔ (اس کے برخلاف غلام کو صرف پچاس کوڑے مارے جاتے ہیں۔ معلوم ہونا چاہئے کہ حد کے بارے میں مرد و عورت دونوں برابر ہیں کیونکہ شرعی حکم عورت و مرد دونوں ہی کے لئے ہیں۔ لیکن مرد و عورت میں صرف اتنا فرق ہے کہ عورت کے کپڑے نہیں اتارے جائیں گے۔ سوائے پوستین اور ایسے کپڑے کے جن میں روئی وغیرہ بھرائی ہوئی ہو۔ کیونکہ عورت کے کپڑے اتار دینے سے بے پردگی اور بے حیائی ہوتی ہے اور موٹے کپڑے وغیرہ کے رہتے ہوئے مارنے سے چوٹ نہیں لگے گی۔ جب کہ ان کپڑوں کے بغیر بھی ان کا پردہ باقی رکھا جا سکتا ہے۔ اس لے اس قسم کے موٹے کپڑے اس کے اوپر سے اتار لئے جائیں اور عورت کو بٹھلا کر اس پر حد ماری جائے گی۔ حضرت علی رضی اللہ عنہ کی مذکورہ حدیث کے پیش نظر اور اس لئے بھی کہ ایسا کرنے سے اس کے لئے زیادہ پر دہ ہوگا۔ تشریح... لان الجناية عند تو افر النعم آزاد آدمیوں پر اللہ تعالیٰ کی نعمتیں بے شمار ہوتی ہیں اس لئے اس کی نافرمانی کی سزا بھی بہت زیادہ ہوتی ہے اور اسی لئے زنا کی صورت میں اس پر سو کوڑے مارنے کا حکم ہے جبکہ غلام بہت سی نعمتوں سے محروم ہوتا ہے اسی لئے زنا کی صورت میں اس پر صرف پچاس کوڑنے مارنے کا حکم دیا گیا ہے۔
فائدہ .... چنانچہ اگر آزاد مرد جسے چار عورتیں نکاح میں رکھنے کی اجازت ہے۔ پھر بھی وہ زنا کرے تو اسے سخت سزادی جائے گی اور غلام کو صرف دو عورتوں کو نکاح میں رکھنے کی اجازت ہے۔ وہ بھی اس شرط کے ساتھ کہ اس کا مولی اس کی اجازت بھی دے پھر بھی ان دونوں کو آپس میں ملنے جلنے کی پوری آزادی نہیں رہے گی بلکہ جب مالک کی خدمت کر کے باندی فارغ ہو چکی ہو اور اس وقت مالک نے آرام کرنے کی اجازت دیدی ہو۔ انہیں باتوں کی وجہ سے باندی اور غلام کی سزا میں بھی کمی ہے۔ یعنی آزاد کے مقابلہ میں یہ نصف سزا کے مستحق ہوں گے۔ البتہ سنگسار ہونے کی صورت میں چونکہ اس کا نصف نہیں ہو سکتا ہے اس لئے اس مسئلہ میں غلام شادی شدہ ہو یا غیر شادی شدہ سب برابر رکھے گئے ہیں۔ یعنی سب کو کوڑے مارے جائیں گے۔ ۔
Book of Hudud. 144. Ashraf al-Bidayah, Urdu commentary of Hidayah, Volume Six. 'And covering is achieved without them, so they are removed, and she is struck seated, because of what we narrated, and because it is more concealing for her.' Translation: And if the fornicator is a male slave (or female slave), then he/she is struck fifty lashes, because Allah the Exalted said: 'For them is half of what is prescribed for the free women of punishment' meaning that the prescribed punishment for female slaves will be half of that which is prescribed for free women. This verse was revealed concerning female slaves. And because slavery halves the divine blessing. Therefore its punishment will also be halved, because when a person receives many blessings and yet disobeys, his punishment is also greater. For this reason, the punishment of the free person is severe. (Conversely, the slave is struck only fifty lashes). It should be known that in matters of hadd, both men and women are equal, because the legal ruling applies to both women and men. However, the only difference between a man and a woman is that the woman's clothes will not be removed except for a fur coat and such clothes that are padded with cotton etc. Because removing the woman's clothes would cause exposure and indecency, and striking over thick clothes would not cause injury. While without these clothes her covering can still be maintained. Therefore, such thick clothes are removed from her, and the woman is made to sit and then the hadd is struck upon her, in view of the aforementioned hadith of Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) and because doing so is more concealing for her. Explanation... 'Because crime upon abundance of blessings' - Free people receive countless blessings from Allah the Exalted, so the punishment for their disobedience is very severe, and therefore in case of zina, the command is to strike one hundred lashes, while a slave is deprived of many blessings, so in case of zina, the command is to strike only fifty lashes. Benefit... So if a free man, who is permitted to keep four women in marriage, still commits zina, he will be given a severe punishment. And a slave is only permitted to keep two women in marriage, and that too with the condition that his master grants permission; moreover, those two will not have full freedom to intermix; rather, only when the female slave is free from serving her master and the master has given permission to rest. Due to these reasons, the punishment of the female and male slave is also reduced, i.e., compared to the free person, they deserve half punishment. However, in the case of stoning (rajm), since it cannot be halved, in this matter all slaves, whether married or unmarried, are treated equally; i.e., all will be struck lashes.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah covers two related rulings within Kitab al-Hudud. First, the procedure for lashing a woman: she is seated, and only thick padded garments (like a fur coat or quilted clothes) are removed, while other clothing remains to preserve modesty. The proof is the practice of Ali (RA) and the principle of concealment. Second, the punishment for slaves (male and female) in zina: they receive 50 lashes, half of the 100 prescribed for free persons. This is based on Quran 4:25 and the rational principle that slavery halves divine favors, thus halving the punishment. The author explains that married slaves are not stoned because stoning cannot be halved; instead, they are lashed. A benefit (fa'idah) elaborates on the reduced marital privileges of slaves, further justifying the reduced punishment.

Key Terms
حد (hadd): A fixed corporal punishment prescribed by Shari'ah for specific crimes like zina, theft, etc.
غلام (ghulam): A male slave owned by a master.
أمة (amah): A female slave owned by a master.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 100 lashes
B) 50 lashes
C) 40 lashes
D) 80 lashes

Key Takeaway
Slaves receive 50 lashes for zina, and women are lashed seated with only thick garments removed.

Ruling on Digging a Pit for a Woman Being Stoned
Ruling on digging a pit for a woman being stoned

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on digging a pit for a woman and a man during stoning, and explain the evidence and rationale.

Core Idea
A pit is recommended for a woman in stoning for modesty, but not required; for a man, it is not dug because the punishment aims at public exposure.

Stoning (rajm) is a hadd punishment for married adulterers. This lesson examines a subsidiary issue: should a pit be dug for the person being stoned? The Hanafi ruling distinguishes between a woman and a man based on prophetic practice and the objectives of the punishment. For a woman, digging a pit up to her chest is recommended (mustahabb) to preserve her modesty. For a man, a pit is not dug because the punishment is meant to be a public deterrent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine the hukm for digging a pit for a woman and for a man. For a woman: mustahabb (recommended); for a man: not done (and ordinarily not allowed, except when necessary).
The text uses 'jaza' (permissible) and later 'ahsan' (better), indicating recommendation.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the evidence: the Prophet dug a pit for al-Ghamidiyyah (Muslim) and Ali dug for Sharahah al-Hamdaniyyah (Ahmad). For a man, the Prophet did not dig for Ma'iz.
The hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri confirms no pit for Ma'iz.
3
Understand the rationale
The pit is for women to conceal their body during stoning. For men, the purpose is public exposure (tashhir) as a deterrent, so a pit would defeat that purpose.
The text says 'mabna al-iqamah 'ala al-tashhir fi al-rijal'.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Some narrations suggest a pit was dug for Ma'iz (Buraidah, Abu Dharr). Ibn al-Humam preferred the negation (Abu Sa'id) because a certain negation is stronger evidence.
The relied-upon position is no pit for men, as in the mashhur (widely transmitted) view.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
For a woman: pit dug up to the chest is recommended. For a man: no pit unless necessary for the punishment to be carried out (e.g., to prevent escape when witnesses prove zina).
Al-'Inayah adds the permissibility in necessity.

Source Text

عورت کو رجم کرنے کیلئے گڑھا کھودنے کا حکم
قَالَ وَإِنْ حُفِرَلَهَا فِي الرَّجُمِ جَازَلِاَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ حَفَرَ لِلْعَامِدِيَّةِ إِلى تَنْدُوَتِهَا وَحَفَرَ عَلَى لِشَرَاحَةِ الْهَمْدَانِيَّةِ وَإِنْ تُرِكَ لَا يَضُرُّهُ لِأَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لَمْ يَأْمُرُ بِذَالِكَ وَهِيَ مَسْتَوْرَةٌ بِثِيَابِهَا وَالْحَفْرُ اَحْسَنُ لِأَنَّهُ اسْتَرُ وَيُحْفَرُ إِلَى الصَّدْ زِ لِمَا رَوَيْنَا وَلَا يُحْفَرُ لِلرَّجُلِ لِأَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ مَا حَفَرَ لِمَا عِزَّ وَلَاتَ مَبْنَى الْإِقَامَةِ عَلَى التَّشْهِيْرِ فِي الرِّجَالِ وَالرَّبْطُ وَالْإِمْسَاكُ غَيْرُ مَشْرُوع
ترجمہ اور سنگسار کرنے کے لئے عورت کے واسطے گڑھا کھود لیا جائے تو جائز ہے۔ یعنی گڑھا کھود لینا بہتر ہے واجب نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے حضرت غامد یہ کے واسطے ان کے سینہ تک کا گڑھا کھدوایا تھا۔ (رواہ مسلم)

اور حضرت علی رضی اللہ عنہ نے شراحہ ہمدانیہ کے لئے گڑھا کھدوایا تھا۔ (رواہ احمد) اور اگر امام نے زانیہ عورت کے لئے گڑھا نہیں کھدوایا تو کوئی نقصان نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے اس کا حکم نہیں فرمایا ہے۔ اور عورت کا پردہ اس کے اپنے کپڑوں سے ہی باقی رہتا ہے۔ البتہ گڑھا کھود دینا بہتر ہے۔ کیونکہ ایسا کرنے سے عورت کے لئے پردہ پوشی زیادہ ہوتی ہے۔ سینہ تک گڑھا کھودنا اس حدیث سے ثابت ہے جسے ہم حضرت غامدیہ کے سلسلے میں پہلے بیان کر چکے ہیں۔ البتہ مرد کے لئے گڑھا نہیں کھودا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے حضرت ماعری کے واسطے گڑھا نہیں کھودا تھا اور اس دلیل سے کہ مردوں کے لئے خد قائم کرنے میں شہرت دینا مقصود ہے اور اسے باندھنا اور روکنا ثابت نہیں ہے۔
فائدہ لیکن اگر اس کے بغیر رحم کرناممکن نہ ہو حالانکہ گواہوں سے زنا ثابت ہو چکا ہو تو جائز ہے۔ جیسا کہ عنایہ میں ہے۔ تشریح.. ولا يحفر للرجل لانه عليه السلام ما حفز لما عزّ ولان مبنى الاقامة على التشهير الخ اور مرد کور جم کرنے کے لئے گڑھا نہیں کھودا جائے گا کیونکہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے حضرت ماعز بن مالک رضی اللہ تعالٰی عنہ کو سزا دینے کے لئے گڑھا نہیں کھدوایا تھا۔ فائده . چنانچہ حضرت ابو سعید خدری رضی اللہ عنہ نے کہا ہے کہ جب رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے ماعز بن مالک رضی اللہ عنہ کو رجم کرنے کا حکم دیا تو ہم نے ان کو بقیع میں رجم کیا۔ واللہ ہم نے اس وقت ان کو نہ تو باندھا اور نہ ہی ان کے گڑھا کھودا اور وہ تو کھڑے رہے۔ لیکن حضرت بریدہ وابوذر رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہما کی حدیث میں ہے کہ ان کے لئے گڑھا کھود لیکن ابن الہمام نے حضرت ابوسعید رضی اللہ عنہ کی (رواه مسلم) حدیث کو ترجیح دی ہے۔ اعتماد اور یقین کے ساتھ نفی کرنا دلیل ہے اور اگر گڑھا ہوتا تو بھاگنے کی گنجائش نہ ہوتی۔ (والربط) اور ایسے لوگوں کو باندھ دینا یا کسی طرح روک کر رکھنا ثابت اور مشروع نہیں ہے۔ البتہ اگر اس کے بغیر رحم ممکن نہ ہو تو اور زنا گواہوں کے ذریعہ ثابت ہو چکا ہو تو جائز ہے جیسا کہ عنایہ میں ہے۔
Ruling on digging a pit for a woman for stoning. He said: And if a pit is dug for her in stoning, it is permissible, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) dug a pit for al-Ghamidiyyah up to her chest, and Ali dug a pit for Sharahah al-Hamdaniyyah. And if it is left, it does not harm because the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not command that, and she is covered by her clothes. But digging is better because it is more concealing. And it is dug to the chest based on what we narrated. And it is not dug for a man because the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not dig for Ma'iz, and because the basis of establishing punishment for men is for public exposure, and binding and restraining is not legislated. Translation: And if a pit is dug for a woman for stoning, it is permissible. That is, digging a pit is better, not obligatory. Because the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) had a pit dug for al-Ghamidiyyah up to her chest. (Narrated by Muslim) And Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) had a pit dug for Sharahah al-Hamdaniyyah. (Narrated by Ahmad) And if the Imam does not dig a pit for the adulterous woman, there is no harm. Because the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) did not command it. And the woman's covering remains with her own clothes. However, digging a pit is better because it provides more concealment for the woman. Digging up to the chest is proven by the hadith we narrated earlier concerning al-Ghamidiyyah. However, a pit will not be dug for a man. Because the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) did not dig a pit for Ma'iz, and because the aim of establishing punishment for men is public exposure, and binding and restraining is not established. Benefit: But if without it stoning is not possible, while the zina has been proven by witnesses, then it is permissible, as is stated in al-'Inayah. Explanation: 'And a pit is not dug for a man because the Prophet did not dig for Ma'iz and because the basis of establishing punishment is for public exposure, etc.' And a pit will not be dug for a man for stoning, because the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) did not have a pit dug for punishing Ma'iz ibn Malik (may Allah be pleased with him). Benefit: So Abu Sa'id al-Khudri (may Allah be pleased with him) said: When the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) ordered the stoning of Ma'iz ibn Malik, we stoned him in Baqi'. By Allah, at that time we neither bound him nor dug a pit for him, and he stood. But in the hadith of Buraidah and Abu Dharr (may Allah be pleased with them), it is mentioned that a pit was dug for him. However, Ibn al-Humam preferred the hadith of Abu Sa'id (may Allah be pleased with him) because a negation with certainty and conviction is evidence, and if there were a pit, there would be no room for escape. (And binding) And binding such people or restraining them in any way is not established or legislated. But if without it stoning is not possible, and the zina has been proven by witnesses, then it is permissible, as is stated in al-'Inayah.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah addresses the ruling on digging a pit for a woman when she is to be stoned for zina. The author states that digging a pit is permissible and recommended (mustahabb), not obligatory. The evidence comes from the actions of the Prophet (peace be upon him) who had a pit dug for al-Ghamidiyyah up to her chest, and from Ali (RA) who dug for Sharahah al-Hamdaniyyah. The reason is modesty: the pit conceals her body during stoning. For men, a pit is not dug because the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not dig one for Ma'iz, and the purpose of stoning men is public exposure as a deterrent. The passage also clarifies that binding or restraining is not prescribed, unless necessary for the punishment to be carried out. The preferred view is that no pit is dug for men, based on the hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri.

Key Terms
رجم (rajm): Stoning to death as a hadd punishment for married adulterers.
حفرة (hufrah): A pit dug to partially bury the person being stoned, for modesty or to prevent escape.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Up to the waist
B) Up to the chest
C) Up to the knees
D) Up to the neck

Key Takeaway
Digging a pit for a woman in stoning is recommended for modesty; for a man it is not done because the punishment aims at public exposure.

Hudud — Fixed Penalties
intermediate
8 min
Master Enforcing Hadd on Slave: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Dispute on master's authority to enforce hadd on slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on a master enforcing hadd on his slave, identify the Shafi'i counter-argument, and explain the Hanafi response based on the distinction between hadd (right of Allah) and ta'zir (right of the slave).

Core Idea
Hadd is a right of Allah requiring state execution; ta'zir is a private right that a master may execute.

The question of whether a master can enforce capital or corporal fixed punishments (hudud) on his own slave directly touches on the boundary between private authority and state sovereignty in Islamic law. The Hanafi school draws a sharp line: hudud are reserved for the Imam or his deputy, while discretionary punishment (ta'zir) may be administered by the master. This lesson unpacks the proofs and the practical difference.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi Position
Identify exactly what the Hanafi school holds: the master cannot enforce hadd without the Imam's permission.
The ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah and all Hanafi authorities agree.
2
Identify the Opposing View
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi'i (and Malik and Ahmad) allow the master to enforce hadd independently, based on the master's absolute authority.
They equate hadd with ta'zir in this context.
3
Examine the Opponent's Proof
The opposing school argues that the master's authority over his slave is even more comprehensive than the Imam's, so he may execute punishment.
They see no need for state involvement.
4
Analyse the Hanafi Response
The Hanafi school distinguishes hadd (a right of Allah) from ta'zir (a right of the slave). Hadd aims to purge the world from corruption and cannot be waived, so only a representative of the Shari'ah (the Imam) executes it.
The report 'Four things are for the rulers' supports this, though it is not a confirmed hadith.
5
Determine the Practical Difference (Thamarah)
In Hanafi practice, the master must inform the Imam; in Shafi'i practice, the master acts alone. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is Hanafi.
This affects real cases where a master discovers his slave committing a hadd crime.

Source Text

آقا غلام پر حد جاری کر سکتا ہے یا نہیں؟
وَ لَا يُقِيمُ الْمَوْلَى الْحَدَّ عَلَى عَبْدِهِ إِلَّا بِإِذْنِ الْإِمَامِ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِى لَهُ اَنْ يُقِيمَهُ لِاَنَّ لَهُ وِلَايَةٌ مُطْلَقَةٌ عَلَيْهِ كَالْإِمَامِ بَلْ أَولَى لِأَنَّهُ يَمْلِكُ مِنَ التَّصَرُّفِ فِيهِ مَا لَا يَمْلِكُهُ الْإِمَامُ فَصَارَ كَالتَّعْزِيرِ وَلَنَا قَوْلُهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ أَرْبَعٌ إِلَى الْوُلَاةِ . مِنْهَا الْحُدُودَ وَلاَنَّ الْحَدَّحَقَّ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى لِاَنَّ الْمَقْصَدَ مِنْهَا إِخْلَاءُ الْعَالَم عَنِ الْفَسَادِ وَلِهَذَا لَا يَسْقُطُ بِإِسْقَاطِ الْعَبْدِ فَيَسْتَوْفِيهِ مَنْ هُوَ نَائِبٌ عَنِ الشَّرْعِ وَهُوَ الْإِمَامُ اَوْنَائِبُهُ بِخِلَافِ التَّعْزِيرِ لِأَنَّهُ حَقُّ الْعَبْدِ وَلِهَذَا يُعَزَّرُ الصَّبِيُّ وَحَقَّ الشَّرْعِ مَوْضُوعٌ عَنْهُ
ترجمہ اور مولی اپنے غلام پر خود سے حد قائم نہیں کرے گا۔ البتہ امام کی اجازت سے کر سکتا ہے۔ اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا ہے کہ مولی کیلئے یہ جائز ہے کہ وہ اپنے غلام پر خود حد قائم کرلے کیونکہ مولی کو اپنے غلام پر ولایت مطلقہ (مکمل ولایت) حاصل ہے جیسے کہ امام وقت کو حاصل ہوتی ہے بلکہ اس امام سے بھی بڑھ کر کیونکہ مولی کو اپنے غلام میں بھیج وغیرہ کے تصرفات میں اتنا اختیار ہوتا ہے جو امام کو بھی نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے یہ حد تعزیر کے مثل ہو گئی۔ امام مالک واحمد رحمتہ اللہ علیہا کا بھی قول ہے۔ البتہ امام کا حد قائم کرنا افضل ہے۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ چار چیزیں والی کے حوالہ اور ان کے اختیار میں ہیں۔ ان میں سے حدود کو بھی ذکر کیا ہے ( اور باقی تین یہ نیں جمعہ کو قائم کرنا، زکوۃ وصول کرنا اور خدود قائم کرنا ) مگر یہ حدیث نہیں ملی ہے۔ البتہ ابن ابی شیبہ نے حضرت حسن بصری وعطاء خراسان سے یہ قول ذکر کیا ہے۔ ع) اور اس دلیل سے بھی کہ
Can the master enforce hadd on his slave or not? 'And the master does not enforce the hadd on his slave except with the permission of the Imam.' And al-Shafi'i said: He may enforce it, because he has absolute authority over him like the Imam, rather even more so, because he possesses powers of disposal over him that the Imam does not, so it becomes like ta'zir. Our proof is: The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Four things are for the rulers [and among them are the hudud]' and because the hadd is a right of Allah the Exalted, for its purpose is to rid the world of corruption, and therefore it does not fall by the waiver of the slave, so it is executed by the one who is the representative of the Shari'ah, which is the Imam or his deputy. Unlike ta'zir, for it is a right of the slave, and therefore the minor is disciplined (ta'zir), and the right of the Shari'ah is waived from him. Translation: And the master will not enforce the hadd on his slave by himself; however, he can do so with the permission of the Imam. And Imam al-Shafi'i stated that the master may enforce the hadd on his slave by himself because the master has absolute authority (complete authority) over his slave, similar to that of the current Imam, rather even greater, because the master has so much power of disposal over his slave in matters of selling etc. that even the Imam does not have. Therefore, this hadd becomes like ta'zir. Imam Malik and Ahmad (may Allah have mercy on them) also hold this view. However, it is better for the Imam to enforce the hadd. Our proof is that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Four things are entrusted to the rulers [and among them are the hudud]'. (And the other three are: establishing Jumu'ah, collecting Zakat, and enforcing Hudud). However, this hadith has not been found. Rather, Ibn Abi Shaybah narrated this saying from Hasan al-Basri and 'Ata' al-Khurasani. And also on the basis of the proof that...
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah presents a dispute between the Hanafi school and al-Shafi'i (and Malik and Ahmad) regarding whether a master can enforce the hadd punishment on his own slave without the permission of the Imam. The Hanafi position is clear: the master cannot enforce hadd without the Imam's permission. The proof is that hadd punishments are rights of Allah, meant to purge corruption from society, and they cannot be waived by the individual. Therefore, they must be executed by the representative of the Shari'ah, i.e., the Imam or his deputy. This is unlike ta'zir (discretionary punishment), which is a right of the slave and can be applied by the master. The text also mentions that al-Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad allow the master to execute hadd, arguing that the master's authority over his slave is even more comprehensive than the Imam's. However, the Hanafi school considers the Imam's enforcement as superior. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that permission is required.

Key Terms
حد (hadd): Fixed punishment prescribed by Shari'ah for crimes like zina, theft, etc.
تعزير (ta'zir): Discretionary punishment left to the judge or master's judgment, not a fixed hadd.
الولاية المطلقة (al-wilayah al-mutlaqah): Absolute authority; here it refers to the master's complete control over his slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when can a master enforce hadd on his slave?
A) Anytime he wishes
B) Only with the permission of the Imam
C) Only if the slave is married
D) Never, only the Imam can enforce hadd

Key Takeaway
Hadd is a right of Allah that requires state authority; a master cannot execute it without the Imam's permission, unlike ta'zir which is a private right.

Ruling on Digging a Pit (Hafr) for Stoning: Distinction Between Men and Women
Establishes the ruling on digging a pit for stoning, distinguishing between men and women.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on digging a pit for stoning, distinguishing between men and women, and cite the primary evidence (hadith) supporting each ruling.

Core Idea
Pit is sunnah for women (modesty), not for men (tashhir); necessity permits it for both.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on digging a pit (hafr) during the stoning punishment (rajm). While the stoning itself is a fixed hadd, the details of its execution — specifically whether to partially bury the condemned — are based on the Prophetic practice. The Hanafi school derives a clear distinction: digging a pit is recommended for women for the sake of modesty, but not for men because the aim for men is public deterrence. We will trace the evidence from the acts of the Prophet (SAW) and the Companions, and explore the exceptional permission when necessity arises.

Guided Path
1
Ruling for Women: Sunnah, Not Obligatory
The passage states that if the Imam does not dig a pit for an adulteress, the punishment is still valid. Digging a pit is better (mustahabb) for greater concealment, but not commanded by the Prophet (SAW).
Evidence: Ali's action for Sharah al-Hamdaniyyah (Ahmad).
2
Ruling for Men: No Pit
For men, a pit shall not be dug because the Prophet (SAW) did not dig one for Ma'iz ibn Malik. The rationale is that the hadd for men aims at public deterrence (tashhir), and tying or restraining is not established.
Evidence: Hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri (Muslim).
3
Resolving Apparent Contradiction in Narrations
Some narrations (Buraydah, Abu Dharr) mention a pit for Ma'iz. Ibn al-Humam preferred Abu Sa'id's definitive negation, as it is more reliable and consistent with the principle that a pit would prevent escape.
This illustrates the Hanafi method of tarjih (preferring one evidence over another).
4
Exception: Permissibility in Necessity
If stoning cannot be carried out mercifully without a pit (e.g., to prevent excessive pain or escape), and zina has been proven by witnesses, then digging a pit is permissible. This is taken from al-'Inayah.
This shows legal flexibility (rukhsah) when the original sunnah cannot be applied without hardship.
5
Clarifying Tying (Rabi)
Tying the offender is also not established from the sunnah. It is only permissible in severe necessity, similar to the pit.
This underscores the Hanafi reluctance to add restrictions beyond the sunnah.

Source Text

كتاب الحدود
اور حضرت علی رضی اللہ عنہ نے شراحہ ہمدانیہ کے لئے گڑھا کھدوایا تھا۔ (رواہ احمد) اور اگر امام نے زانیہ عورت کے لئے گڑھا نہیں کھدوایا تو کوئی نقصان نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے اس کا حکم نہیں فرمایا ہے۔ اور عورت کا پردہ اس کے اپنے کپڑوں سے ہی باقی رہتا ہے۔ البتہ گڑھا کھود دینا بہتر ہے۔ کیونکہ ایسا کرنے سے عورت کے لئے پردہ پوشی زیادہ ہوتی ہے۔ سینہ تک گڑھا کھودنا اس حدیث سے ثابت ہے جسے ہم حضرت غامدیہ کے سلسلے میں پہلے بیان کر چکے ہیں۔ البتہ مرد کے لئے گڑھا نہیں کھودا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے حضرت ماعری کے واسطے گڑھا نہیں کھودا تھا اور اس دلیل سے کہ مردوں کے لئے خد قائم کرنے میں شہرت دینا مقصود ہے اور اسے باندھنا اور روکنا ثابت نہیں ہے۔
فائدہ لیکن اگر اس کے بغیر رحم کرناممکن نہ ہو حالانکہ گواہوں سے زنا ثابت ہو چکا ہو تو جائز ہے۔ جیسا کہ عنایہ میں ہے۔ تشریح.. ولا يحفر للرجل لانه عليه السلام ما حفز لما عزّ ولان مبنى الاقامة على التشهير الخ اور مرد کور جم کرنے کے لئے گڑھا نہیں کھودا جائے گا کیونکہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے حضرت ماعز بن مالک رضی اللہ تعالٰی عنہ کو سزا دینے کے لئے گڑھا نہیں کھدوایا تھا۔ فائده . چنانچہ حضرت ابو سعید خدری رضی اللہ عنہ نے کہا ہے کہ جب رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے ماعز بن مالک رضی اللہ عنہ کو رجم کرنے کا حکم دیا تو ہم نے ان کو بقیع میں رجم کیا۔ واللہ ہم نے اس وقت ان کو نہ تو باندھا اور نہ ہی ان کے گڑھا کھودا اور وہ تو کھڑے رہے۔ لیکن حضرت بریدہ وابوذر رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہما کی حدیث میں ہے کہ ان کے لئے گڑھا کھود لیکن ابن الہمام نے حضرت ابوسعید رضی اللہ عنہ کی
(رواه مسلم)
حدیث کو ترجیح دی ہے۔ اعتماد اور یقین کے ساتھ نفی کرنا دلیل ہے اور اگر گڑھا ہوتا تو بھاگنے کی گنجائش نہ ہوتی۔ (والربط) اور ایسے لوگوں کو باندھ دینا یا کسی طرح روک کر رکھنا ثابت اور مشروع نہیں ہے۔ البتہ اگر اس کے بغیر رحم ممکن نہ ہو تو اور زنا گواہوں کے ذریعہ ثابت ہو چکا ہو تو جائز ہے جیسا کہ عنایہ میں ہے۔
Book of Hudud. And Hadrat Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) had a pit dug for Sharah al-Hamdaniyyah (narrated by Ahmad). And if the Imam did not dig a pit for the adulteress woman, there is no harm, because the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) did not command it. And the woman's veiling remains through her own clothes. However, digging a pit is better, because by doing so the concealment for the woman is greater. Digging a pit up to the chest is proven from the hadith which we have previously mentioned regarding the Ghamidiyyah woman. However, for a man a pit shall not be dug, because the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) did not dig a pit for Ma'iz (may Allah be pleased with him), and on the evidence that establishing hadd for men is intended for publicizing, and tying and restraining him is not established. Benefit: But if mercy is not possible without it, while zina has been established through witnesses, then it is permissible, as is stated in al-'Inayah. Explanation: And a pit is not dug for the man, because he (peace be upon him) did not dig one for Ma'iz, and because the basis for establishing is for publicizing, etc. And a pit shall not be dug for the man for stoning, because the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) did not have a pit dug for Ma'iz ibn Malik (may Allah be pleased with him) when punishing him. Benefit: As Hadrat Abu Sa'id al-Khudri (may Allah be pleased with him) said: When the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) ordered the stoning of Ma'iz ibn Malik (may Allah be pleased with him), we stoned him in al-Baqi'. By Allah, we did not tie him nor dig a pit for him, and he remained standing. But in the hadith of Hadrat Buraydah and Abu Dharr (may Allah be pleased with them both) it is that a pit was dug for him, but Ibn al-Humam gave preference to the hadith of Abu Sa'id (may Allah be pleased with him) (narrated by Muslim). Negation with confidence and certainty is evidence, and if there had been a pit, there would not have been a possibility of escape. (And tying) And tying such people or restraining them in any way is not established or legislated. However, if mercy is not possible without it, and zina has been established through witnesses, then it is permissible, as is stated in al-'Inayah.
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage from the Book of Hudud discusses the ruling on digging a pit (hafr) for the stoning punishment (rajm). It begins by recalling that Hadrat Ali (RA) had a pit dug for a woman (Sharah al-Hamdaniyyah) as reported by Ahmad. The author then clarifies that if the Imam does not dig a pit for the adulteress, the punishment remains valid because the Prophet (SAW) never explicitly commanded it; the woman's modesty is already preserved by her own clothing. However, digging a pit up to chest level is considered better (mustahabb) for her greater concealment, based on the hadith of the Ghamidiyyah woman. For men, the ruling differs: no pit should be dug because the Prophet (SAW) did not dig one for Ma'iz ibn Malik (RA). The rationale is that establishing hadd for men aims at public deterrence (tashhir), and tying or restraining is not proven from the sunnah. A benefit (fa'idah) is added: if stoning cannot be carried out mercifully without a pit (e.g., to prevent escape or excessive pain), and zina has been proven by witnesses, then digging a pit is permissible, as stated in al-'Inayah. The explanation (tashrih) reiterates that no pit is dug for a man, citing the Prophet's practice with Ma'iz and the principle that hadd is for public display. The author notes a conflict in narrations: Abu Sa'id al-Khudri (RA) explicitly states no pit was dug for Ma'iz, while Buraydah and Abu Dharr mention one. Ibn al-Humam prefers Abu Sa'id's account because his definitive negation is stronger evidence, and the presence of a pit would have prevented any chance of escape. Finally, tying the offender is also not established; it is only permitted in extreme necessity. Throughout, the passage reflects the Hanafi position that the sunnah practice takes precedence, and any deviation is only allowed for necessity.

Key Terms
حفر (hafr): Digging a pit for stoning, specifically to partially bury the person being stoned.
الرجم (al-rajm): Stoning to death as a hadd punishment for married adulterers.
ربط (rabt): Tying or restraining the person being stoned to prevent escape.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is digging a pit (hafr) for stoning recommended for women but not for men according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because women are weaker and more likely to escape.
B) To preserve the woman's modesty and conceal her, while for men the aim is public deterrence.
C) Because the Prophet (SAW) ordered a pit for every woman but forbade it for men.
D) Because women cannot be stoned without a pit.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's practice (sunnah) distinguishes between men and women in the stoning procedure: a pit is recommended for women for modesty but not for men; only necessity permits a pit for men.

Hudud — Fixed Penalties
intermediate
10 min
Master Enforcing Hadd on Slave: Hanafi vs Shafi'i View
Inter-madhhab dispute on master's authority to enforce hadd.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school requires the Imam's permission for a master to enforce hadd on his slave and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Hadd is haqq Allah; only the Imam or his deputy can enforce it, not the master.

Does a master's absolute authority over his slave extend to enforcing fixed divine punishments (hudud)? The Hanafi school says no, while the Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali schools say yes. In this lesson, we examine the legal reasoning behind each position, the proofs cited, and the practical consequences of the dispute.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling from the matn of al-Hidayah: 'The master shall not enforce hadd upon his slave except with the permission of the Imam.' This is the foundational claim of the Hanafi school on this issue.
The ruling is unconditional; the master cannot act alone.
2
Identify the opposing school and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i, along with Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad, holds that the master can enforce hadd without the Imam's permission. They argue that the master's authority (wilayah mutlaqah) over his slave is even greater than the Imam's, so hadd becomes analogous to ta'zir.
This is a clear ikhtilaf across madhhabs, not just a theoretical difference.
3
Follow the opponent's proof (dalil)
The Shafi'i school cites hadith where the Prophet ﷺ ordered masters to flog their slave-girls for zina (Abu Hurairah, Bukhari/Muslim) and ordered Ali (RA) to flog a slave-girl. These appear to give direct authority to masters.
Also the principle of analogy (qiyas) with ta'zir, which the master can administer.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafis reinterpret (ta'wil) these hadith: the Prophet's command to masters was to bring the matter to the Imam, and if the Imam permits, then the master may act. The order to Ali (RA) was a specific permission, not a general rule. They also argue that hadd is haqq Allah, unlike ta'zir which is haqq al-'abd.
Ibn al-Humam criticized this ta'wil, but the Hanafi school still follows the precautionary view.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: In the Hanafi school, if a master flogs his slave for zina without permission, the punishment is not valid and the hadd remains unfulfilled; the master is sinful. In the other schools, the punishment is valid and the hadd is fulfilled.
This affects whether the slave must be punished again by the Imam if the master's action is invalid.

پیش کر دو اور اگر وہ تمہیں اجازت دید ہے تو تم اس پر حد جاری کر دو چنانچہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے حضرت علی کرم اللہ وجہہ کوحد قائم کرنے کی اجازت دی ۔لیکن ابن الہمام نے فرمایا ہے کہ یہ تاویل دوسرے ائمہ کرام کو قبول نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ احادیث سے یہی ظاہر ہے کہ شریعت نے اس معاملہ میں غلاموں کے مالکوں کو اپنا نائب مقرر کر دیا ہے۔ اس لئے جب تک اس کے معارض کوئی دوسری روایت اور دلیل نہ ہو تب تک ظاہر حدیث پر عمل کیا جائے گا۔ لیکن میں مترجم کہتا ہوں کہ صحابہ رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہم سب عادل اور اعتدال پر قائم بھی تھے اور حقوق وحدود کا پورا پورا خیال رکھتے تھے۔ اسلئے علماء حنفیہ نے ان کے نائب ہونے میں کچھ شک نہیں کیا ہے۔ لیکن اس مسئلہ میں تامل کیا ہے کہ دوسرے لوگ بھی ان کی طرح نائب ہو سکتے ہیں یا نہیں کیونکہ دوسروں کیلئے کوئی شرعی اجازت نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس بات کا احتمال باقی رہتا ہے کہ مالکان حدود مقررہ سے زیادتی کر کے اسے سخت تکلیفیں پہنچا ئیں بالخصوص اس صورت میں جب کہ اس سے ناراضگی بڑھی ہوئی وار حدود قائم کرنا بندوں کاحق نہیں ہے کیونکہ یہ تو خالص حق الہی ہے۔ اس لئے اس بات کا بہت خوف رہتا ہے کہ اصلاح کی بجائے فساد برپا ہو جائے۔ اس لئے یہی افضل ترین ہے کہ امام ہی حدود قائم کرے۔ اسی لئے علماء احناف نے احتیاطی امام ہی کے اختیار کو واجب کہا ہے۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب۔
Can a master enforce hadd on his slave or not? And the master shall not enforce hadd upon his slave except with the permission of the Imam. And al-Shafi'i said: He has the right to enforce it, because he has absolute authority over him like the Imam, rather even more so because he possesses powers of disposal over him that the Imam does not own, so it becomes like ta'zir. And for us is his statement (peace be upon him): 'Four things are in the charge of the rulers: among them are the hudud.' And because hadd is the right of Allah Almighty, for the intended purpose is to rid the world of corruption. Therefore it is not dropped by the slave's waiver. So it is carried out by the one who is the deputy of the Shari'ah, which is the Imam or his deputy, contrary to ta'zir because it is the right of the slave, and for this reason a child is disciplined (ta'zir) even though the right of the Shari'ah is removed from him. Translation: And a master will not enforce hadd on his slave by himself, but he can do so with the permission of the Imam. Imam Shafi'i said: It is permissible for the master to enforce hadd on his slave by himself, because the master has absolute authority over his slave like the Imam, rather even more so because the master has such powers of disposal over his slave as the Imam does not have. Therefore this hadd is like ta'zir. Imam Malik and Ahmad also hold this view, but the Imam's enforcement of hadd is more virtuous. Our evidence is the saying of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him): 'Four things are in the charge of the rulers: among them are the hudud.' (The remaining three are: establishing Jumu'ah, collecting Zakat, and enforcing hudud.) However, this hadith is not found; rather Ibn Abi Shaybah mentioned this statement from Hasan al-Basri and 'Ata' al-Khurasani. And also by the evidence that hadd is the right of Allah Almighty, because the purpose of enforcing hudud is to rid the world of corruption. Therefore even if the slave forgives, it is not dropped. So only the one who is the deputy of the Shari'ah, i.e., the Imam or his deputy like the qadi, enforces it, contrary to ta'zir because it is the right of the slaves, and for this reason every adult disciplines his children even though the child's legal right is exempt. Explanation: According to the Hanafis, if someone's owned slave commits zina, the master cannot enforce hadd on him by himself; only the ruler has the authority. However, if the ruler gives permission, then the master can enforce hadd. Imam Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad hold that the master can enforce it by himself and has the discretion, but the Imam's enforcement is more virtuous. (Imam Malik and Shafi'i support their position with various hadith: one is the hadith of Abu Hurairah (RA): The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) was asked about a slave-girl who committed zina and was not muhsan. He said: If she commits zina, flog her; if she commits zina again, flog her; if she commits zina again, flog her; if she commits zina again, sell her even for a she-goat. Bukhari and Muslim narrated it. And Hadrat Ali (RA) once delivered a sermon and said: O people, enforce hadd on your slave-girls whether they are married or not (if they commit zina). And a slave-girl of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) committed zina, and he ordered me to flog her. When I approached her, I found that she had recently given birth and was in the state of nifas. I feared that if I flogged her, she might die. So I returned and informed the Prophet. He said: You did well. Narrated by Tirmidhi. And in another hadith of Abu Hurairah, the Prophet said: When the slave-girl of any of you commits zina, flog her according to the Book of Allah; if she commits zina again, flog her; if she commits zina again, flog her; if she commits zina again, sell her. Narrated by Abu Dawud.) But Abu Hanifah interpreted these hadith to mean: present her to the Imam, and if he gives you permission, then enforce hadd. Thus the Prophet gave permission to Ali (RA) to enforce hadd. However, Ibn al-Humam said: This interpretation will not be accepted by other imams, because the apparent meaning of the hadith is that the Shari'ah has appointed the masters as deputies. So unless there is another contradictory narration, the apparent meaning must be acted upon. But I, the translator, say: The Companions were all just and moderate, and they fully observed rights and hudud. Therefore the Hanafi scholars have no doubt about their being deputies. But in this issue, there is hesitation whether others like them can be deputies, because there is no legal permission for others, and there is a possibility that masters may exceed the prescribed limits and cause severe pain, especially when they are angry. Enforcing hudud is not the right of the slaves; it is purely the right of Allah. So there is great fear that corruption may spread instead of reform. Therefore it is most virtuous for the Imam to enforce hudud. For this reason, the Hanafi scholars, as a precaution, have considered the Imam's authority as necessary. And Allah knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage addresses a significant inter-madhhab dispute regarding the authority to enforce hudud punishments on slaves. The Hanafi position, as stated in the matn (from al-Hidayah), is that a master (mawla) cannot enforce the hadd penalty on his own slave without the permission of the Imam (ruler). Imam al-Shafi'i, along with Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad, holds that the master has the right to enforce hadd on his slave directly because his authority (wilayah) over the slave is absolute, even greater than the Imam's in matters of disposal. They analogize this to ta'zir (discretionary punishment), which the master can administer. The Hanafi proof is twofold: first, the statement of the Prophet (SAW) that 'four things are in the charge of the rulers' – among them hudud – although this specific wording is not found as a hadith but is attributed to Hasan al-Basri and 'Ata' al-Khurasani. Second, and more fundamentally, hadd is a pure right of Allah (haqq Allah), established for the public good (to cleanse the world from corruption). As such, it cannot be waived by the victim or the slave; it must be carried out by the representative of the Shari'ah, i.e., the Imam or his deputy (like a judge). In contrast, ta'zir is a right of the individual (haqq al-'abd), so a master can discipline his slave or a father his child. The passage then presents the opposing school's evidence from hadith: the famous hadith of Abu Hurairah where the Prophet (SAW) instructs masters to flog their slave-girls for repeated zina and to sell them if necessary. Also, Hadrat Ali (RA) was ordered by the Prophet to flog a slave-girl, and the Prophet approved his action. Imam Abu Hanifah reinterpreted these hadith, stating that the Prophet's instruction to masters was to bring the matter to the Imam, and if the Imam permits, then the master may execute the hadd. The condition of Imam's permission is therefore derived from the need to prevent abuse. Ibn al-Humam criticized this interpretation, arguing that the apparent (zahir) meaning of the hadith gives direct authority to the masters. However, the Hanafi commentator (the translator) defends the Hanafi view by noting that the Companions were just and could be trusted, but for later generations, the potential for abuse (excess, personal vendetta) makes it safer and more prudent (ihriyatan) to restrict the enforcement of hadd to the Imam. The passage ends by affirming that the preferred view is that only the Imam should enforce hudud, and Allah knows best.

Key Terms
ولایت مطلقہ (wilayah mutlaqah): Absolute authority; here referring to the master's complete control over his slave, including the right to punish.
تعزیر (ta'zir): Discretionary punishment not specified by the Shari'ah; it is a right of the individual (e.g., master over slave, father over child).
حق اللہ (haqq Allah): A right of Allah; a punishment established for the public interest that cannot be waived by individuals.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary reason the Hanafi school gives for requiring the Imam's permission for a master to enforce hadd on his slave?
A) The master might be too lenient.
B) Hadd is a right of Allah, not a personal right, so only the Shari'ah's deputy can enforce it.
C) The Prophet (SAW) explicitly forbade masters from punishing slaves.
D) The slave must be given a fair trial first.

Key Takeaway
Hadd punishments are rights of Allah and must be enforced by the public authority (Imam), not by individuals, to prevent corruption and ensure justice.

Master's Authority to Establish Hadd on a Slave
Dispute over whether a master may establish hadd on his slave without imam's permission.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the master's authority to establish hadd on his slave and explain the Hanafi ta'wil of the opposing ahadith.

Core Idea
A master cannot enforce hadd on his slave without the imam's permission — hadd is a divine right, not a private one.

This lesson examines a key inter-madhhab dispute: whether a slave-owner can personally execute the fixed punishment (hadd) for zina upon his slave. The Hanafi school restricts this authority to the imam, while other schools grant it to the master. Understanding the basis of this difference deepens your grasp of how rights of Allah are administered in Islam.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi Position
Identify the clear ruling: the master does not establish hadd without the imam's permission. This is the starting point.
2
Identify the Opposing View and Its Proof
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad hold that the master may directly establish hadd. Their evidence includes ahadith where the Prophet commanded flogging of slave-girls without mentioning imam's permission.
Ahadith narrations are from Bukhari, Muslim, Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud.
3
Analyze the Hanafi Ta'wil
Understand how Abu Hanifa reinterprets these ahadith: they mean the master should bring the matter to the imam; if the imam permits, then flog. The case of 'Ali was with the Prophet's explicit authorization (Prophet as imam).
Hanafis argue that the general practice of Companions like 'Umar supports this ta'wil.
4
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
See the practical difference: according to Hanafis, if a master flogs without permission, the hadd is invalid and the master is liable for injury. According to Shafi'is, the hadd is valid and the master is not liable.
5
Apply the Tarjih
Confirm that the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is the Hanafi view because hadd is a pure divine right, and private enforcement risks abuse. The imam's authorization ensures justice and prevents corruption.
The Hanafi position is preferred as a precaution (ihtiyat).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يقيم المولى الحد على عبده الا باذن الامام وقال الشافعي له ان يقيمه .... الخ رواه البخاري ومسلم رواه الترمذي رواه ابو داؤد والله أعلم بالصواب
The master does not establish the hadd upon his slave except with the permission of the imam. Al-Shafi'i said: He may establish it... etc. Narrated by Bukhari and Muslim. Narrated by Tirmidhi. Narrated by Abu Dawud. And Allah knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the authority to execute hadd punishment on a slave. According to the Hanafi school, hadd is a pure divine right (haqq Allah), therefore only the imam or his deputy (like a qadi) may establish it. A master cannot punish his slave for zina with hadd unless the imam grants permission. Imam al-Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad hold that the master himself may establish the hadd, though the imam doing so is preferable. The text cites several ahadith in support of the latter view, such as Abu Huraira's hadith about a slave-girl who committed zina repeatedly, and the narration of 'Ali (the Prophet ordered him to flog a slave-girl). However, Imam Abu Hanifa interprets these ahadith as meaning that the master should refer the matter to the imam, who may then authorize the master. Ibn al-Humam comments that this ta'wil is not accepted by the other imams because the apparent meaning of the ahadith grants direct authority to the master. But the Hanafi position is preferred because hadd is a pure divine right, and allowing private execution could lead to excess and corruption. The text concludes that it is most virtuous for the imam to execute the hadd, and Hanafi scholars consider the imam's authorization necessary as a precaution (ihtiyat).

Key Terms
المولى (al-mawla): The master/owner of a slave (here, the male owner).
الحد (al-hadd): Corporal punishment prescribed by Shariah for certain crimes (e.g., zina, theft), considered a right of Allah (haqq Allah).
الإمام (al-imam): The supreme ruler of the Muslim state or his authorized deputy (e.g., qadi).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, may a master establish hadd punishment on his own slave for zina without the imam's permission?
A) Yes, the master may do so directly.
B) No, only with the imam's permission.
C) Yes, but only if the slave is a muhsan.
D) No, only the qadi can establish hadd on a slave.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires the imam's permission for establishing hadd on a slave because hadd is a pure divine right, and private enforcement risks abuse.

Conditions of Ihsan for Stoning in Hanafi Fiqh
Definition of ihsan for stoning with conditions and disputes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the six conditions of ihsan according to the Hanafi school and explain why Islam is required as a condition, defending the Hanafi position against the Shafi'i objection.

Core Idea
Ihsan requires completeness of favor: freedom, adulthood, sanity, Islam, valid marriage, and consummation—all in both spouses.

The punishment for zina in Islamic law depends on the offender's marital status. A muhsan (married and fully favored) is stoned; a non-muhsan is flogged. This passage from al-Hidayah defines the precise conditions for ihsan, highlighting a key dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i and even within the Hanafi school. Understanding these conditions illuminates the Hanafi emphasis on deterrents and the completeness of divine favor.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal consequence
The passage defines the conditions for a person to be considered muhsan, which determines whether the punishment for zina is stoning or flogging.
Ihsan is not a ruling on an act but a legal state.
2
List the conditions for ihsan
From the text: free, adult, sane, Muslim, valid marriage, and consummation with both spouses in the state of ihsan at the time of intercourse.
Each condition is justified as completing the 'favor' (ni'mah) and thus increasing the deterrent.
3
Understand the rationale
The passage explains that sanity and adulthood are conditions for legal capacity (ahliyyah). Beyond those, freedom, Islam, valid marriage, and consummation represent increasing levels of divine favor; ingratitude for great favor (zina) warrants a stricter punishment.
The text rejects nobility and knowledge as conditions because no textual evidence supports them.
4
Analyze the inter-madhhab dispute on Islam
Al-Shafi'i and Abu Yusuf (in one narration) argue that Islam is not required, citing the Prophet's stoning of two Jews. The Hanafi response: that was under Torah law, now abrogated; the hadith 'Whoever associates partners with Allah is not muhsan' proves Islam is necessary.
The practical difference: a Muslim marrying a non-Muslim and committing zina is stoned according to Shafi'i, but flogged according to Hanafis.
5
Examine the requirement for both spouses' ihsan at consummation
For a man to become muhsan, both he and his wife must meet all conditions at the time of intercourse. Examples: marrying a non-Muslim, slave, insane, or minor wife prevents ihsan. Similarly if the husband lacks a condition.
Intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf disagrees regarding the wife being non-Muslim; the mufta bihi view is Abu Hanifa's and Muhammad's.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَإِحْصَانُ الرَّجُمِ أَنْ يَكُونَ حُرَّاعًا قِلَا بَالِعًا مُسْلِمًا فَدْتَزَوَّجَ اِمْرَأَةً نِكَاحًا صَحِيْحًا وَدَخَلَ بِهَا وَهُمَا عَلَىٰ صِفَةِ الإِحْسَانِ فَالْعَقْلُ وَالْبُلُوعُ شَرْطٌ لِاهْلِيَّةِ الْعُقُوبَةِ إِذْلاخِطَابَ دُونَهُمَا وَمَا وَرَانَهُمَا يُشْتَرَطُ لِتَكَامُلِ الْجِنَايَةِ بِوَاسِطَةِ تَكَامُلِ النِعْمَةِ إِذْ كُفْرَاتُ النِّعْمَةِ يَتَغَلَّظُ عِندَ تَكَثُرهَا وَهَذِهِ الْأَشْيَاء مِنْ جَلَائِلِ النِّعَمِ وَقَدْ شُرعَ مُ بِالزِّنَاءِ عِنْدَ اسْتِجْمَاعِهَا فَيُنَاطُ بِهِ بِخِلَافِ الشَّرْفِ وَالْعِلْمِ لِاَنَّ الشَّرْعَ مَا وَرَدَ بِاعْتِبَارِ هِمَا وَنَصْبُ الشَّرْعِ بِالرَّاءِ مُتَعَدَّرٌ وَلَاتَ الْحُرِّيَّةَ مُمْكِنَة مِنْ النِّكَاحِ الصَّحِيحِ وَالنِّكَاحُ الصَّحِيحَ مُمْكِنَّ مِنَ الْوَطي مِنَ نِكَاحَ الْمُسْلِمَةِ وَيُؤكَدُ اعْتِقَادُ الْحُرْمَةِ فَيَكُونُ الْكُلُّ نِكَاحَ الْمُسْلِمَةِ وَيُؤكَدَاء الْحَلَالِ وَالْإِصَابَةُ شِبَعٌ بِالْحَلَالِ وَالْإِسْلَامُ يُمَكنه من شافِعِيُّ يُخَالِفُنَا فِي اشْتِرَاطِ الْإِسْلَامِ وَكَذَا أَبُويُوسُفٌ مَرْجِرَةٌ عَنِ الزَّنَاءِ وَالْجِنَايَةُ بَعْدَ تَوَفُرِ الزَّوَاجِرِ اغْلَظَ وَالشَّافِعِيُّ يُخَالِفُنَا فِي فِي رِوَايَةٍ لَهُمَا مَارُوِيَ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ اللهِ رَجَمَ يَهُودِيَّيْنِ قَدْزَنَيَا قُلْنَا كَانَ ذَالِكَ بِحُكْمِ التَّورَةِ ثُمَّ نَسَخَ يُوْيَدُهُ قَوْلُهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ مَنْ أَشْرَكَ بِاللَّهِ فَلَيْسَ بِمُحْصَنِ وَ الْمُعْتَبَرُ فِي الدُّخُولِ الْإِيْلَاجُ فِي الْقُبُلِ عَلَى وَجْهِ يُوجِبُ الْعُسْلَ وَشُرِطَ صِفَةُ الْإِحْصَانِ فِيهِمَا عِنْدَ الدُّخُولِ حَتَّى لَوْ دَخَلَ بِالْمَنَكْوُحَةِ الْكَافِرَةِ أَوِ الْمَمْلُوْكَةِ أوِ الْمَجْنُونَةِ أَوِ الصَّبِيَّةِ لَا يَكُونُ مُحْصَبًا وَكَذَا إِذَا كَانَ الزَّوْجُ مَوْصُوفًا بِإِحْدَى هَذِهِ الصَّفَاتِ وَهِيَ حُرَّةٌ مُسْلِمَةٌ عَاقِلَةٌ بَالِغَةٌ لأَنَّ النِّعْمَةَ بِذَالِكَ تَتَكَامَلُ إِذِ الطَّبْعُ يَنْفَرُّ عَنْ صُحْبَةِ الْمَجْنُونَةِ وَقُلْنَا يَرْغَبُ فِي الصَّبِيَّةِ لِقِلَّةِ رَغْبَتِهَا فِي الْمَنْكُوحَةِ الْمَمْلُوْكَةِ حَذْرَاعَنْ رِقِ الْوَلَدِوَلَا ابْتِلَافَ مَعَ الْاِخْتِلَافِ فِي الدِّينِ وَاَبُوْ يُوسُفٌ يُخَالِفُنَافِي الْكَافِرَةِ وَالْحُجَّةُ عَلَيْهِ مَا ذَكَرْنَا وَ قَوْلُهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لَا تُحْصِنُ الْمُسْلِمَ الْيَهُودِيَّةُ وَلَا النَّصْرَانِيَّةُ وَلَا الْحُر الامَةُ وَلَا الْحُرَّةُ الْعَبْدَ
He said: And the ihsan of stoning is that he be free, adult, [sane,] Muslim, and he marries a woman with a valid marriage and had intercourse with her while both are in the state of ihsan. So sanity and majority are conditions for eligibility for punishment because there is no address without them. And those beyond them are required for the completeness of the crime by virtue of completeness of favor, for ingratitude for favor is more severe when favors are abundant. And these things are among the great favors, and stoning for zina has been prescribed when they are combined, so it is attached to it. Contrary to nobility and knowledge, because no text has come considering them, and establishing a ruling by pure opinion is impossible. And freedom makes valid marriage possible, valid marriage makes intimate relations possible, and marriage of a Muslim woman and the belief in the prohibition [of zina] are strengthened, so all these are deterrents from zina. And the crime is more severe after the abundance of deterrents. And al-Shafi'i disagrees with us in requiring Islam, and similarly Abu Yusuf in a narration from them. A narration that the Prophet stoned two Jews who had committed zina is cited. We say: That was by the law of the Torah, then it was abrogated. It is supported by his saying, peace be upon him: 'Whoever associates partners with Allah is not muhsan.' And what matters in entry is penetration in the front (vagina) in a manner that necessitates ghusl. And the condition of ihsan is required in both [parties] at the time of entry. So if he entered a wife who is an unbeliever, a slave-girl, an insane woman, or a minor girl, he does not become muhsan. Likewise if the husband is described with one of these qualities while she is a free, Muslim, sane, adult woman, because the completeness of favor is [not achieved] due to that. Nature dislikes companionship of an insane woman, and we say he does not desire a minor girl because of her lack of desire, and [he avoids] marrying a slave-girl for fear of enslaving children, and there is no harmony with religious difference. And Abu Yusuf disagrees with us regarding the [unbelieving] wife, and the proof against him is what we mentioned and his saying, peace be upon him: 'A Jewish woman does not make a Muslim muhsan, nor does a Christian woman, nor does a free woman a slave, nor does a free woman a slave.'
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage from the Hidayah defines the conditions for ihsan (the state that makes a person liable for stoning for zina, as opposed to flogging). The definition: The offender must be free, adult, sane, Muslim, and must have contracted a valid marriage and consummated it with both being in the state of ihsan at the time of consummation. Sanity and adulthood are general conditions for legal capacity (ahliyyah) for punishment. The additional conditions (freedom, Islam, valid marriage, consummation) are required because they represent complete favors (ni'mah); ingratitude for great favors by committing zina deserves a stricter punishment. The text argues that freedom enables marriage, marriage enables lawful intercourse, and Islam strengthens the belief that zina is forbidden—thus all serve as deterrents. The text then addresses two disputes: (1) Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Abu Yusuf (in one narration) hold that Islam is not a condition for ihsan; they cite the incident where the Prophet stoned two Jews who had committed adultery. The Hanafi response: That was by the law of the Torah, which was then abrogated. Moreover, the hadith 'Whoever associates partners with Allah is not muhsan' supports requiring Islam. (2) Regarding consummation, penetration must occur in the vagina in a way that necessitates ghusl. The conditions of ihsan (freedom, Islam, sanity, adulthood) must be present in both spouses at the time of intercourse. Therefore, if a man marries an unbeliever, a slave-girl, an insane woman, or a minor girl and consummates, he does not become muhsan. Similarly, if he is insane, a minor, a slave, or an unbeliever while she meets the conditions, he does not become muhsan because the favor is incomplete: nature recoils from an insane wife, minors lack desire, marriage to a slave risks children becoming slaves, and religious difference prevents harmony. Abu Yusuf disagrees regarding the wife being an unbeliever, but the text proofs against him using the hadith that a Jewish or Christian woman does not make a Muslim muhsan.

Key Terms
إحصان (ihsan): The legal state that makes a person liable for stoning (rajm) for zina, defined by freedom, adulthood, sanity, Islam, valid marriage, and consummation with both in that state.
محصن (muhsan): A person who meets the conditions of ihsan (free, adult, sane, Muslim, married in valid marriage, and consummated).
رجم (rajm): Stoning to death, the punishment for zina committed by a muhsan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is NOT a condition for a man to become muhsan?
A) Being free.
B) Being Muslim.
C) Being a scholar (alim).
D) Having consummated the marriage after a valid nikah.

Key Takeaway
A person becomes muhsan (liable for stoning) only when free, adult, sane, Muslim, validly married, and consummated with both spouses fulfilling those conditions at the time of intercourse; Islam is a required condition, contra Shafi'i, and the relied-upon Hanafi position requires it in both spouses.

Conditions of Ihsan and the Dispute on Islam Requirement
Defining ihsan and addressing inter-madhhab dispute on Islam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the six conditions of ihsan according to the Hanafi school, identify the condition disputed by al-Shafi'i, and apply the Hanafi response to the opposing proof.

Core Idea
A Muslim is not muhsan by marriage to a non-Muslim — Islam is a required condition for ihsan.

This passage from Al-Hidayah defines the conditions that make a person muhsan (liable for Rajm for zina). It also addresses a key inter-madhhab dispute: whether Islam is a requirement. The Hanafi school holds that both spouses must be Muslim, while al-Shafi'i (and a narration of Abu Yusuf) hold otherwise. Understanding these conditions is crucial for correctly applying the hadd punishment for zina.

Guided Path
1
List the conditions of ihsan
Read the passage and extract all conditions that the Hanafi school requires for a person to be considered muhsan. These include freedom, sanity, adulthood, Islam, valid marriage, and consummation.
Note that sanity and adulthood are prerequisites for legal address; the rest complete the blessing that makes the crime more severe.
2
Understand the rationale for each condition
The passage explains why each condition is required: freedom enables marriage, marriage enables intercourse, Islam strengthens the belief in prohibition, etc. Grasp the reasoning behind the shurut.
The conditions are meant to make the act of zina more blameworthy due to the completeness of deterrents.
3
Identify the disputed condition
Al-Shafi'i and a narration of Abu Yusuf disagree on whether Islam is necessary. Locate the sentence in the passage where the author states this ikhtilaf.
The passage says: 'Al-Shafi'i differs with us on requiring Islam, and likewise Abu Yusuf in one narration.'
4
Analyze the opposing proof and Hanafi response
The opposing school cites the Prophet stoning a Jewish couple. The Hanafi response is that this was by Torah law and later abrogated, supported by the hadith 'Whoever associates partners with Allah is not muhsan'.
The Hadith is decisive because it explicitly states that shirk negates ihsan.
5
Apply the dispute to a practical scenario
Consider a Muslim man married to a Christian woman. According to Hanafi, he is not muhsan (rajm not applicable); according to Shafi'i, he is muhsan (rajm applicable). Understand the thamarah al-khilaf.
The practical difference is the punishment: 100 lashes vs. rajm.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صِفَةِ الإِحْسَانِ فَالْعَقْلُ وَالْبُلُوعُ شَرْطٌ لِأَهْلِيَّةِ الْعُقُوبَةِ إِذْ لَا خِطَابَ دُونَهُمَا وَمَا وَرَاءَهُمَا يُشْتَرَطُ لِتَكَامُلِ الْجِنَايَةِ بِوَاسِطَةِ تَكَامُلِ النِّعْمَةِ إِذْ كُفْرَانُ النِّعْمَةِ يَتَغَلَّظُ عِنْدَ تَكَثُّرِهَا وَهَذِهِ الْأَشْيَاءُ مِنْ جَلَائِلِ النِّعَمِ وَقَدْ شُرِعَ الرَّجْمُ بِالزِّنَا عِنْدَ اسْتِجْمَاعِهَا فَيُنَاطُ بِهِ بِخِلَافِ الشَّرَفِ وَالْعِلْمِ لِأَنَّ الشَّرْعَ مَا وَرَدَ بِاعْتِبَارِهِمَا وَنَصْبُ الشَّرْعِ بِالرَّأْيِ مُتَعَذِّرٌ وَالْحُرِّيَّةُ تُمَكِّنُ مِنَ النِّكَاحِ الصَّحِيحِ وَالنِّكَاحُ الصَّحِيحُ يُمَكِّنُ مِنَ الْوَطْءِ وَنِكَاحُ الْمُسْلِمَةِ يُؤَكِّدُ اعْتِقَادَ الْحُرْمَةِ فَيَكُونُ الْكُلُّ زَوَاجِرَ عَنِ الزِّنَا وَالْجِنَايَةُ بَعْدَ تَوَفُّرِ الزَّوَاجِرِ أَغْلَظُ وَالشَّافِعِيُّ يُخَالِفُنَا فِي اشْتِرَاطِ الْإِسْلَامِ وَكَذَا أَبُو يُوسُفَ فِي رِوَايَةٍ لَهُمَا مَا رُوِيَ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ ﷺ رَجَمَ يَهُودِيَّيْنِ قَدْ زَنَيَا قُلْنَا كَانَ ذَلِكَ بِحُكْمِ التَّوْرَاةِ ثُمَّ نُسِخَ يُؤَيِّدُهُ قَوْلُهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ: «مَنْ أَشْرَكَ بِاللَّهِ فَلَيْسَ بِمُحْصَنٍ» وَالْمُعْتَبَرُ فِي الدُّخُولِ الْإِيلَاجُ فِي الْقُبُلِ عَلَى وَجْهٍ يُوجِبُ الْغُسْلَ وَشُرِطَتْ صِفَةُ الْإِحْصَانِ فِيهِمَا عِنْدَ الدُّخُولِ حَتَّى لَوْ دَخَلَ بِالْمَنْكُوحَةِ الْكَافِرَةِ أَوِ الْمَمْلُوكَةِ أَوِ الْمَجْنُونَةِ أَوِ الصَّبِيَّةِ لَا يَكُونُ مُحْصَنًا وَكَذَا إِذَا كَانَ الزَّوْجُ مَوْصُوفًا بِإِحْدَى هَذِهِ الصِّفَاتِ وَهِيَ حُرَّةٌ مُسْلِمَةٌ عَاقِلَةٌ بَالِغَةٌ لِأَنَّ النِّعْمَةَ بِذَلِكَ تَتَكَامَلُ إِذِ الطَّبْعُ يَنْفِرُ عَنْ صُحْبَةِ الْمَجْنُونَةِ وَقُلْنَا لَا يَرْغَبُ فِي الصَّبِيَّةِ لِقِلَّةِ رَغْبَتِهَا وَفِي الْمَنْكُوحَةِ الْمَمْلُوكَةِ حَذَرًا مِنْ رِقِّ الْوَلَدِ وَلَا ائْتِلَافَ مَعَ الِاخْتِلَافِ فِي الدِّينِ وَأَبُو يُوسُفَ يُخَالِفُنَا فِي الْكَافِرَةِ وَالْحُجَّةُ عَلَيْهِ مَا ذَكَرْنَا وَقَوْلُهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ: «لَا تُحْصِنُ الْمُسْلِمَ الْيَهُودِيَّةُ وَلَا النَّصْرَانِيَّةُ وَلَا الْحُرُّ الْأَمَةَ وَلَا الْحُرَّةُ الْعَبْدَ»
Description of ihsan: sanity and puberty are conditions for being liable for punishment, as there is no address (of obligations) without them. What is beyond them is required for the completeness of the crime by way of completeness of blessing, because ingratitude for blessing becomes more severe when blessings are abundant. These things are among the great blessings, and stoning for zina has been legislated only when they are all present, so it is attached to them, unlike honor and knowledge, because the Law has not come considering them, and establishing law by opinion is impossible. Freedom enables valid marriage, valid marriage enables intercourse, and marriage of a Muslim woman strengthens the belief in its prohibition, so all are deterrents against zina, and a crime after many deterrents is more severe. Al-Shafi'i differs with us on requiring Islam, and likewise Abu Yusuf in one narration. Their proof: the Prophet ﷺ stoned two Jews who had committed zina. We say: That was by the ruling of the Torah, then it was abrogated. This is supported by his saying: 'Whoever associates partners with Allah is not muhsan.' What is considered in consummation is insertion in the front in a manner that necessitates ghusl. The quality of ihsan is required in both at the time of consummation, such that if he consummates with a married woman who is an unbeliever, a slave woman, an insane woman, or a minor girl, he is not muhsan. Likewise if the husband is described with one of these qualities while she is free, Muslim, sane, adult, because the blessing is complete thereby, for nature recoils from keeping company with an insane woman, and we say: he does not desire a minor girl because of her lack of desire, and in the married slave woman due to fear of the child being enslaved, and there is no affection with difference in religion. Abu Yusuf differs with us regarding the unbeliever woman. The proof against him is what we mentioned and his saying: 'A Muslim is not made muhsan by a Jewish woman, nor a Christian woman, nor a free man by a slave woman, nor a free woman by a slave.'
Source pages p. 148

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the conditions of ihsan (the status that makes one liable for Rajm for zina). The Hanafi position is that ihsan requires the following conditions in both spouses at the time of consummation: freedom, sanity, adulthood, Islam, valid marriage, and actual consummation. The text explains that sanity and adulthood are prerequisites for any legal address, while the other conditions are required because they complete the blessing, and ingratitude for great blessings makes the crime more severe. The author refutes the Shafi'i view (and a narration of Abu Yusuf) that Islam is not required, using the hadith that the Prophet stoned Jews but clarifying that this was by Torah law which was later abrogated. The Prophet's statement 'Whoever associates partners with Allah is not muhsan' decisively shows that Islam is necessary. The passage also details consummation: it requires full penetration as in the front that necessitates ghusl. Both spouses must have the quality of ihsan at that time; if either lacks any condition (e.g., spouse is unbeliever, slave, insane, minor), the other does not become muhsan. The reasoning is given for each case: nature recoils from an insane wife, desire is less for a minor, fear of offspring being enslaved with a slave wife, and lack of affection with religious difference. Abu Yusuf's difference regarding the unbeliever wife is rebutted with the same hadith.

Key Terms
الإحْصَان (al-ihsan): A legal status requiring freedom, sanity, adulthood, Islam, valid marriage, and consummation, making one liable for Rajm.
المُحْصَن (al-muhsan): A person who has achieved ihsan and thus is liable for Rajm.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Sanity
C) Islam
D) Consummation

Key Takeaway
Ihsan requires six conditions: freedom, sanity, adulthood, Islam, valid marriage, and consummation; Islam is the disputed condition.

Why Rajm and Jald Are Not Combined for a Muhsan
Stating Hanafi ruling that Rajm and Jald are not combined for a muhsan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on combining Rajm and Jald for a muhsan and evaluate the opposing schools' proof.

Core Idea
Rajm alone is enough for a muhsan — flogging is useless for the dead and the Prophet never combined them.

This lesson addresses a key inter-madhhab difference in hudud punishments. The Hanafi school holds that a muhsan (married person guilty of zina) should only be stoned, not flogged. The opposing view of Malik, Shafi'i, and Ahmad (in one narration) is that both punishments are combined. The text from Ashraf ul Hadaya provides both a Prophetic precedent and a rational argument for the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What does the passage rule for a muhsan? It states that Rajm and Jald are not combined; only Rajm is applied.
2
Locate the Hanafi proofs
Two proofs are given: (1) the Prophet ﷺ did not combine them, (2) a rational argument that Jald is devoid of purpose when combined with Rajm.
One is naqli, the other is 'aqli.
3
Analyze the rational argument
Why is Jald devoid of purpose? Because Rajm already achieves deterrence of others (as it is the most severe punishment), and deterrence of the culprit himself is impossible after death by stoning.
This shows that combining would be legally pointless.
4
Identify the opposing view
Malik, Shafi'i, and Ahmad (one narration) hold that both punishments are combined. Their proof is the hadith of 'Ubadah bin al-Samit that mentions flogging and exile (or flogging and Rajm).
5
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school responds that the 'Ubadah hadith was part of initial legislation and was later abrogated by the Prophet's actual practice (e.g., with Ma'iz and the Ghamidiyyah woman), where he ordered only stoning.
Thus the relied-upon position is that only Rajm applies to a muhsan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَلَا يُجْمَعُ فِى الْمُحْصَنِ بَيْنَ الرَّجُمِ وَالْجَلْدِ إِنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لَمْ يَجْمَعْ وَلِأَنَّ الْجَلْدَ يُعْرَى عَنِ الْمَقْصُوْدِ مَعَ الرَّجُمِ لِأَنَّ زَجْرَ غَيْرِهِ يَحْصُلُ بِالرَّجُمِ إِذْ هُوَ فِي الْعُقُوبَةِ أَقْصَاهَا وَزَجْرُهُ لَا يَحْصُلُ بَعْدَ هَلَاكِهِ
He said: And for the muhsan, Rajm and Jald are not combined; indeed, the Prophet ﷺ did not combine them, and because Jald is devoid of its purpose when combined with Rajm, since deterring others is achieved by Rajm, as it is the most extreme of punishments, and deterring the culprit himself cannot be achieved after his death.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding whether a muhsan (one liable for Rajm) should also receive flogging. The Hanafi ruling is clear: Rajm and Jald are not combined. Two proofs are given: first, the actual practice of the Prophet ﷺ, who never combined both punishments for a muhsan. Second, a rational argument: flogging serves as a deterrent, but after the muhsan is stoned to death, the flogging cannot deter him (since he is dead), and deterring others is already achieved by Rajm, which is the most severe penalty. The author notes that Imam Malik, Imam Shafi'i, and in one narration Imam Ahmad hold that both punishments should be combined. They rely on the hadith of 'Ubadah bin al-Samit which mentions flogging and exile (and in another version flogging and Rajm). The Hanafi response is that the 'Ubadah hadith was part of the initial legislation and was later abrogated by the Prophet's actual practice (e.g., with Ma'iz and the Ghamidiyyah woman). Thus the relied-upon position is that only Rajm is applied to a muhsan.

Key Terms
الرَّجُم (ar-rajm): Stoning to death as a punishment for zina committed by a muhsan.
الْجَلْد (al-jald): Flogging with lashes as a punishment for zina.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the Prophet combined them once, then forbade it
B) Because flogging is wasted on a dead person and Rajm alone deters others
C) Because the Qur'an only mentions flogging
D) Because ijma' of the Companions was against it

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that Rajm alone is the punishment for a muhsan because combining flogging is both contrary to the Prophet's practice and rationally unnecessary.

Hudud — Fixed Penalties
